Women in Congress: Why So Few?* // NYT // Derek\nWillis \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015 123\n\n*A Bad Voting Ban in Maryland* // NYT // The Editorial Board \xe2\x80\x93 June 1,\n2015.............................. 125\n\n*Congress Should Extend PATRIOT Act Provisions to Keep Us Safe* //Medium //\nJeb Bush \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015        126\n\n\n\n\n\n*TODAY\xe2\x80\x99S KEY STORIES*\n\n\n\n\n*Hillary sets venue for first big rally: Roosevelt Island\n<http://www.politico.com/story/2015/06/hillary-clinton-rally-roosevelt-island-118500.html>\n// Politico // Annie Karni \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nThe solemn memorial park at the southern tip of Roosevelt Island, Four\nFreedoms Park, will serve as the backdrop for Hillary Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s first\nsignificant speech as a presidential candidate on June 13, when she is\nexpected to lay out her vision for the future of the country and explain to\nvoters why she is the right person to lead it there.\n\n\n\nThe park, designed by architect Louis Kahn and dedicated in 2012, honors\nthe \xe2\x80\x9cfour freedoms\xe2\x80\x9d Franklin D. Roosevelt outlined in his 1941 State of the\nUnion address \xe2\x80\x94 freedom of speech, religion, freedom from want and freedom\nfrom fear. The symbolic backdrop won out over other potential sites for\nClinton\xe2\x80\x99s \xe2\x80\x9cvision\xe2\x80\x9d speech that were floated to the campaign by supporters,\nsuch as Seneca Falls, N.Y., the site of the first women\xe2\x80\x99s rights convention\nin 1848.\n\n\n\nIn announcing the venue for the much-anticipated speech, the campaign\nemphasized Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s long admiration of both Franklin and Eleanor\nRoosevelt. Clinton is expected to be joined at the kick-off speech by her\nfamily, Chelsea and Bill Clinton. It won\xe2\x80\x99t mark their first time there:\nBill Clinton was one of the speakers at the 2012 dedication ceremony of the\npark.\n\n\n\nClinton\xe2\x80\x99s New York speech will be open to the public and tickets will be\nfree, according to the campaign website. But that message came with a big\ndisclaimer: tickets do not guarantee admission and the rally will fill up\non a first-come, first-served basis. A spokesman said it was not clear yet\nhow many supporters the venue would accommodate.\n\n\n\nThe big rally will mark a break from the intimate roundtables Clinton has\nparticipated in during the first two months of her campaign. The speech\ncomes almost two months to the day after Clinton formally announced her\npresidential bid, and will be followed up by her busiest week on the trail\nyet: Clinton will fly directly to Iowa Saturday night, marking her third\nvisit there since announcing, followed by stops in New Hampshire, South\nCarolina and Nevada \xe2\x80\x94 all early states she has already visited at least\nonce during the ramp up phase of her campaign.\n\n\n\nThe Iowa organizing meeting that Clinton will participate in on Saturday\nevening will be simulcast at organizing meetings planned for nearly all of\nthe country\xe2\x80\x99s 435 congressional districts, campaign officials said.\n\n\n\nClinton\xe2\x80\x99s campaign is already lowering expectations as they explain how the\nformer secretary of state will fight for every vote and not take the\nprimary for granted \xe2\x80\x94 even while her challengers so far remain side players\nin the 2016 drama. In Iowa, the campaign pointed out, no Democratic\npresidential candidate has ever received more than 50 percent of the caucus\nvote, unless they were a sitting president, vice-president, or Iowa Sen.\nTom Harkin, who ran in 1992. In New Hampshire, the campaign underscored, no\nDemocrat in a contested primary in the last 25 years has won by more than\n27,000 votes, or received more than 50 percent of the vote.\n\n\n\nBut the campaign is building up the rally as a dramatic beginning of a new\nphase of the campaign. \xe2\x80\x9cThousands of Americans coming together to hear\nHillary lay out her vision for the future of our country,\xe2\x80\x9d is how campaign\nchairman John Podesta described it in an email. \xe2\x80\x9cAll at one of the most\nspectacular locations you\xe2\x80\x99ll ever see.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\n*EXCLUSIVE: Clinton looks to the future in Pride statement\n<http://www.washingtonblade.com/2015/06/01/exclusive-clinton-looks-to-the-future-in-pride-statement/#sthash.n6QIln0h.qxCmVE3D.dpuf>\n// Washington Blade // Chris Johnson \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nDemocratic presidential candidate Hillary Clinton said Monday past advances\nmade by the LGBT community should be recognized during Pride celebrations\nthis month, but noted that more work remains.\n\n\n\nIn an exclusive statement to the Washington Blade, the former secretary of\nstate recognized June as Pride month, calling for a rededication to\ncomplete the work of improving the lives of people everywhere.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cEach June, we honor the contributions of the LGBTQ community and proudly\nreaffirm our commitment to ensuring that every member of the American\nfamily can live, work, and marry the person they love without enduring\ndiscrimination or prejudice,\xe2\x80\x9d Clinton said. \xe2\x80\x9cAs we celebrate the\nhard-fought progress that has been made toward advancing the rights of\nLGBTQ Americans, we must also recognize that this work is far from\nfinished. I hope that each and every one of us will dedicate ourselves to\nbuilding a future in which every person can live in dignity, free from\nviolence or fear, free to be themselves, free to live up to their God-given\npotential no matter where they live or who they are \xe2\x80\x94 this month and every\nmonth.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nClinton made the statement on the same day she issued a message via Twitter\nhinting that, like many LGBT Americans, she\xe2\x80\x99s awaiting good news from the\nSupreme Court on same-sex marriage. This month, justices are expected to\nissue a decision on whether same-sex couples have a right to marry\nnationwide.\n\n\n\nAs of the time of this posting, neither former Maryland Gov. Martin\nO\xe2\x80\x99Malley nor U.S. Sen. Bernard Sanders (I-Vt.) \xe2\x80\x94 other Democratic\ncandidates in the race \xe2\x80\x94 had issued statements this year recognizing June\nas Pride month, nor had any of the Republican presidential candidates.\n\n\n\nClinton, who enjoys considerable support in the LGBT community, issued the\nstatement shortly after calling on the Supreme Court to issue a nationwide\nruling in favor of same-sex marriage. She\xe2\x80\x99s also spoken out against\nreligious freedom measures in Indiana and Arkansas seen to enable\ndiscrimination against LGBT people.\n\n\n\nAmong her achievements on behalf of the LGBT community as a U.S. senator\nare advocating for the Employment Non-Discrimination Act and twice voting\nagainst a U.S. constitutional amendment that would have barred same-sex\nmarriage throughout the country.\n\n\n\nDuring her tenure as secretary of state, Clinton coined the phrase \xe2\x80\x9cgay\nrights are human rights\xe2\x80\x9d during a Pride celebration at the State Department\nand delivered a high-profile speech in Geneva in favor of LGBT human rights\nacross the globe.\n\n\n\nBut Clinton didn\xe2\x80\x99t articulate support for same-sex marriage until 2013 and\nbefore that time said her position was that she opposed gay nuptials. In a\nlater interview with National Public Radio, she advocated a state-by-state\napproach to advancing marriage rights for same-sex couples. Two weeks\nbefore oral arguments at the Supreme Court, Clinton made clear she believes\nsame-sex couples should have a constitutional right to marry.\n\n\n\nAccording to a Clinton aide, staff and volunteers are set to participate in\na number of Pride events and parades throughout the country during the\nmonth of June.\n\n\n\n*Poll: New speed bumps for Clinton\n<http://www.cnn.com/2015/06/02/politics/hillary-clinton-2016-poll-gop-field-close/>\n// CNN // Jennifer Agiesta \xe2\x80\x93 June 2, 2015*\n\n\n\nMore people have an unfavorable view of Democratic front-runner Hillary\nClinton now than at any time since 2001, according to a new CNN/ORC poll on\nthe 2016 race.\n\n\n\nWhile Clinton remains strikingly dominant in the Democratic field, the poll\nshows that her numbers have dropped significantly across several key\nindicators since she launched her campaign in April.\n\n\n\nA growing number of people say she is not honest and trustworthy (57%, up\nfrom 49% in March), less than half feel she cares about people like them\n(47%, down from 53% last July) and more now feel she does not inspire\nconfidence (50%, up from 42% last March).\n\n\n\nIn head-to-head match-ups against top Republicans, her margin is tighter\nthan it has been at any point in CNN/ORC\'s polling on the contest.\n\n\n\nOn the Republican side, though, no candidate has successfully broken out of\nthe pack.\n\n\n\nThe group of seven that have come to dominate most polling on the race hold\nthe top of the charts in this poll, Sen. Marco Rubio and Jeb Bush leading\nthe pack with Mike Huckabee, Wisconsin Gov. Scott Walker, Sen. Ted Cruz,\nBen Carson and Sen. Rand Paul all in the hunt.\n\n\n\nMuch of Clinton\'s fade is attributable to shifts among independents, but\nshe\'s also losing some ground among her own partisans. Her support in the\nDemocratic nomination contest has dropped 9 points since April, and though\nmore than 8-in-10 Democrats said they thought she was honest and\ntrustworthy earlier this year; now, just 73% say so.\n\n\n\nThe new CNN/ORC poll looking at the shape of the race for the presidency in\n2016 finds these warning signs for Clinton, alongside some concerns for the\nRepublican Party\'s best-known contender, Jeb Bush.\n\n\n\nJeb Bush\'s family ties\n\nBush\'s efforts to separate himself from his brother have worked to some\nextent. Only about half of Americans say Bush is "a lot like his brother."\n\n\n\nBut most -- 56% -- say his connection to two former presidents would make\nthem less likely to back him for the presidency. Just 27% say that\nconnection would make them more likely to back the former Florida governor.\n\n\n\nThat\'s virtually the opposite situation of what his brother faced when\nGeorge W. Bush made his initial run for the presidency in 1999. Back then,\n42% said Bush\'s connection to his father made them more likely to back him,\nwhile only 24% said it was a deterrent.\n\n\n\nBush\'s family ties are slightly more of a draw for Republicans, but not by\nmuch. Among Republicans and Republican-leaning independents, 42% say\nthey\'re more likely to back Jeb Bush because of his connections, while 38%\nsay they are less likely to vote for him because of that.\n\n\n\nNo leader emerges in the GOP pack\n\nFor the bulk of the GOP field, however, the race for the Republican\nnomination remains an effort to distinguish themselves from the pack and no\none has yet succeeded at that.\n\n\n\nThough there has been some shuffling at the top of the GOP order since the\nlast CNN/ORC poll in April, no individual candidate\'s movement lies outside\nof the margin of sampling error.\n\n\n\nRubio tops the field with 14%, with Bush near even at 13%. Huckabee and\nWalker follow at 10% each, with Cruz (8%), Paul (8%) and Carson (7%) all\nwithin striking distance of double-digit support.\n\n\n\nPaul prompts the largest gender gap on the GOP side, drawing 13% and tying\nfor first among men while garnering just 2% support among women.\n\n\n\nThe top of the field is similar among conservative Republicans to the\noverall horse race numbers, but among those who consider themselves tea\nparty supporters, there\'s a clear leader: Scott Walker with 19% support.\nHis closest competitor is Ted Cruz with 12%.\n\n\n\nOverall, about half of Republicans (49%) would like to see the field\nresolve early, saying it would be best for the party if one strong\ncandidate emerged early as a clear frontrunner. But 46% say they would\nprefer a longer campaign, with a number of strong contenders competing over\nthe next year.\n\n\n\nOne possible differentiator emerges: The poll finds a distinct difference\nin which candidates Republicans view as representing the future rather than\nthe past.\n\n\n\nThree-quarters of Republicans describe Marco Rubio (77%) or Scott Walker\n(75%) as representing the future, nearly 7-in-10 say so about Rand Paul\n(68%), but Bush (51%) and Christie (51%) are far less likely to be seen as\nrepresentative of the future.\n\n\n\nThe growing Democratic field\n\nDemocrats are more likely than Republicans to say they would like a\ncompetitive primary (53% say that would be best for the party), but their\npreferences so far don\'t portend a close contest.\n\n\n\nClinton continues to hold a massive lead in that race, with 60% of\nDemocrats saying she would be their top choice for the nomination. Behind\nher, 14% would favor Vice President Joe Biden, and 10% prefer Vermont Sen.\nBernie Sanders.\n\n\n\nMartin O\'Malley, the former Maryland governor who announced his candidacy\non Saturday, barely registers with 1% support.\n\n\n\nSanders does fare better among liberals than overall, carrying 18% support\namong that group, but Clinton still notches 61% among the liberals in her\nparty.\n\n\n\nGetting closer to the general\n\nIn general election match-ups, Clinton now runs about even with Rand Paul,\nScott Walker and Marco Rubio, while she continues to top Bush and Ted Cruz\nby a significant margin.\n\n\n\nAs noted above, those shifts stem largely from a change among independents,\nthough Republicans appear to be solidifying their support for GOP\ncandidates while Democrats are slightly less certain about Clinton.\n\n\n\nOne feature of the race that has held even as the numbers shifted: These\nmatch-ups prompt enormous gender gaps. According to the poll, the gender\ngaps remain over 20 points in each of the five match-ups tested, including\na whopping 34-point gender gap in Clinton\'s match-up with Scott Walker.\n\n\n\nHer declining support in those general election match-ups, alongside\nfalling favorability ratings and worsening impressions of her, suggests\nrecent news about her actions as secretary of state may have taken a toll.\n\n\n\nThough most -- 61% -- think the release of Clinton\'s emails over the next\nmonths from her time as secretary of state will not reveal any previously\nhidden wrongdoing, the poll also finds 58% are dissatisfied with the way\nshe handled the attack in Benghazi in 2012.\n\n\n\nA narrow majority feel the Republican-led congressional hearings on the\nattack have been handled appropriately, just 41% say the GOP has gone too\nfar with them.\n\n\n\nClinton\'s family ties to a president are more of a wash than Bush\'s. While\n39% say her marriage to Bill Clinton makes them more likely to vote for\nher, the same share say it\'s a turn-off. And most Americans say Clinton is\nnot like her husband at all (54%).\n\n\n\nThe CNN/ORC Poll was conducted by telephone May 29-31, among a random\nnational sample of 1,025 adults. The margin of sampling error for results\namong the full sample is plus or minus 3 percentage points. It is 4.5\npoints for results among the 433 Democrats and Democratic-leaning\nindependents and the 483 Republicans and Republican-leaning independents.\n\n\n\n*Republican Lindsey Graham Announces 2016 Presidential Campaign\n<http://www.bloomberg.com/politics/articles/2015-06-01/republican-lindsey-graham-announces-2016-presidential-campaign>\n// Bloomberg // David Weigel \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nSenator Lindsey Graham announced his campaign for president on Monday,\nemphasizing his centrist challenge to the Republican Party\'s base.\n\n\n\n"I intend to be president not of a single party, but of a nation," Graham\nsaid in a speech in his hometown of Central, S.C. "I want to do more than\nmake big government smaller. I want to help make a great nation greater."\n\n\n\nGraham\'s speech finishes a months-long exploratory process, one that found\nthe Republican bantering with town hall audiences and baiting rivals into\nfights on foreign policy and immigration. Polling in single digits, joking\nabout his chances, Graham combines the candor of a dark-horse candidate\nwith the media profile of a front-runner.\n\n\n\nHe left little doubt as to his intentions during a May interview on CBS\nThis Morning: "I\'m running because I think the world is falling apart. I\'ve\nbeen more right than wrong on foreign policy," he said.\n\n\n\nGraham, 59, joins three younger Senate colleagues\xe2\x80\x94Ted Cruz of Texas, Rand\nPaul of Kentucky, and Marco Rubio of Florida\xe2\x80\x94in the Republican nomination\nfight. (Vermont Senator Bernie Sanders is seeking the Democratic\nnomination.) Elected in 2002 to replace the retiring Strom Thurmond, and\npreviously elected to four terms in the House of Representatives, he is\nlikely to have the longest Washington resume of anyone on the Republican\nstage.\n\n\n\nHe\'s also the only declared candidate with a military record, having been a\njudge advocate in the United States Air Force since 1982. Last week he\nannounced he would leave the reserves as he reaches the mandatory\nretirement age of 60 this summer.\n\n\n\nSince the January launch of his exploratory committee, Security Through\nStrength, the possibility of a Graham bid has been a puzzle. His is a\nresume not calculated to appeal to Republican primary voters. Graham\'s\nearly Washington career was defined by the impeachment of President Bill\nClinton, a case on which he served as a prosecutor, which quickly came to\nlook like a debacle for Republicans. In the Senate, he\'s advocated for an\naggressive foreign policy and strong security state even as his party\'s\nlibertarian tendency has grown. And every time legislation to change\nimmigration policy moved in the Senate, Graham was a co-sponsor.\n\n\n\n"We are going to solve this problem," he told the National Council of La\nRaza in a 2007 speech. We\'re not going to run people down. We\'re not going\nto scapegoat people. We\'re going to tell the bigots to shut up."\n\n\n\nTalk like that infuriated conservatives. In 2008 and 2014, Graham\'s enemies\nsearched for credible primary challengers. Both times, they came up far\nshort, and convinced Graham that the fringe could bark but not bite. In\n2010, he predicted that the Tea Party would "die out." After securing his\n2014 victory, he seemed to be proven right.\n\n\n\n"There\'s a growing element in our party that would like me to speak up,"\nGraham said earlier this year in an interview. "Where is the Republican\nParty on problem solving? Is there a rational way forward on immigration?\nDo you deport 11 million people? I don\'t think so."\n\n\n\nWry and affable, Graham\'s approach to presidential politicking owes much to\nhis friend and mentor John McCain. In 2000 and 2008, Graham campaigned hard\nfor the Arizona senator, who was running for president. In the Capitol,\nboth men share an open-door approach to the media and a hunger for deals\nwith Democrats. Graham shares McCain\'s readiness with a joke and talent for\nTV debate.\n\n\n\n"In debates, he\'ll shred \'em," McCain said when Graham announced his\nexploratory committee. "He has my all-out complete support."\n\n\n\nGraham may be kept out of the first Fox News debate, in August, which the\nnetwork intends to limit to the top 10 candidates according to national\npublic polling. Despite his steady presence in green rooms, Graham\'s\nfocusing more on the New Hampshire primary than any "national" race. Like\nMcCain, Graham is looking to prove that he can reason with the Republican\nprimary electorate one room at a time. Alone among the candidates, he\nfavors laws that would limit campaign spending\xe2\x80\x93an issue that boosted McCain\nin 2000.\n\n\n\nWhen challenged on immigration, he enters into a Socratic dialogue with\naudiences, to convince them that reform and pathways to citizenship are\nsensible but not amnesty.\n\n\n\nAnd like McCain, Graham is a hawk whose confidence is not dimmed by events.\n"I think the world is falling apart," he often says, "and I\'ve been right\nmore than wrong." Graham supported the 2003 invasion of Iraq and the 2007\nmilitary surge, and has insisted that the conflict was won, a victory\nsquandered by Barack Obama. He favored a more muscular intervention in\nLibya than the no-fly zone favored by the Obama administration, and favored\nan early military intervention on the side of Syria\'s rebels.\n\n\n\nGraham\'s foreign policy contrasts completely with that of Rand Paul, and\nthe two men have sparred across the primary states. Paul tends to avoid\nusing Graham\'s name when he refers to "a senator" who favors NSA\nsurveillance and treating captured terrorists as enemy combatants. Graham\nhas no such filter, and has said that Paul "would have the worst chance of\nanybody to make a case against Barack Obama\xe2\x80\x99s foreign policy."\n\n\n\nThat confidence grows out of a personal story that Graham has become more\ncomfortable telling on the trail. Born in Central, near Greenville, he\nworked at a pool hall and was compelled at an early age to take care of his\nyounger sister. "My mom\'s disease, Hodgkin\'s disease, wiped us out\nfinancially," Graham told Fox News in April. "We eventually lost our\nbusinesses. I understand we\'re all one car wreck from needing help. But\nwhat it told Lindsey Graham, above all else, is that family, friends and\nfaith really do matter."\n\n\n\nIn politics, since winning a state legislative seat in 1992, Graham has\ndefended the existence of the welfare state while arguing for reform.\nRaising the Social Security retirement age, like an immigration overhaul\nand foreign policy, has been a focus of Graham\'s early pitch. He starts\nwith less support than McCain\xe2\x80\x93but unlike the Arizonan, he hails from one of\nthe GOP\'s vital early primary states.\n\n\n\n"Get ready," Graham told a dinner audience in his native South Carolina\nlast month. "Get ready for a debate that\'s been long overdue within the\nparty. Get ready for a voice that understands you can\'t save America\nwithout someone willing to sacrifice and die for America."\n\n\n\nGraham holds undergraduate and law degrees from the University of South\nCarolina. On Sunday, while the Senate debated the Patriot Act, he\nofficially retired from the Air Force reserves, which he joined while\nattending school and caring for his sister in the absence of his late\nparents.\n\n\n\n"There are a lot of so-called \'self-made\' people in this world," Graham\nplanned to say in Central. "I\'m not one of them. My family, friends,\nneighbors, and my faith picked me up when I was down, believed in me when I\nhad doubts. You made me the man I am today."\n\n\n\n*SOCIAL MEDIA*\n\n\n\n*David Axelrod (5/31/15, 8:23 AM)*\n<https://twitter.com/davidaxelrod/status/605031777267290113>* - O\'Malley is\na dynamic, accomplished guy. It was reported in\nthe blog of Rick Hasen, an election law expert who works at the University\nof California, Irvine.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cThis lawsuit concerns the most fundamental of rights guaranteed citizens\nin our representative democracy \xe2\x80\x94 the right to vote,\xe2\x80\x9d the complaint states,\nthen refers to a curtailing of early voting in the state, among other\nchanges that affect minority voters and other groups. \xe2\x80\x9cThat right has been\nunder attack in Wisconsin since Republicans gained control of the\ngovernor\xe2\x80\x99s office and both houses of the State Legislature in the 2010\nelection.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nMrs. Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s aides said the suit was not filed on behalf of the campaign,\nbut they offered their support for it.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe are aware of it and strongly support its goal of ensuring the right to\nvote is not unduly burdened,\xe2\x80\x9d Brian Fallon, a spokesman for Mrs. Clinton,\nsaid in a statement.\n\n\n\nMr. Elias filed a similar lawsuit in Ohio recently, accusing the state of\ntrying to suppress the votes of traditional Democratic constituencies like\nblacks, Hispanics and young people.\n\n\n\nMr. Walker, as he travels around the country, often talks about his efforts\nto push through changes in the voting rights laws to require people to\nbring identification to the polls.\n\n\n\n*Journalists Meet To Discuss Frustration With Clinton Campaign\'s Control\nOver Access And Information\n<http://www.huffingtonpost.com/2015/06/01/journalists-clinton-campaign_n_7487076.html?1433194660>\n// HuffPo // Michael Calderone \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nNEW YORK -- Journalists covering Hillary Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s presidential campaign\nmet for nearly two hours in Washington on Monday to discuss concerns about\nwhat they believe is inadequate access to cover the Democratic\nfront-runner, according to people who attended.\n\n\n\nThe grievances discussed at the private gathering, which was held at the\nLos Angeles Times/Tribune Washington offices, go beyond Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s\nunwillingness so far to substantively engage with the press, a topic that\nhas already been discussed publicly on cable news and social media.\nAttendees of the meeting, who were not authorized by their news\norganizations to speak on the record, charge the Clinton campaign with\nkeeping an excessively tight grip on information, even when it comes to\nlogistical details that don\'t seem particularly sensitive or revelatory.\n\n\n\nAmong the problems discussed were the campaign\'s failure to provide\nadequate notice prior to events, the lack of a clear standard for whether\nfundraisers are open or closed press and the reflexive tendency to opt to\nspeak anonymously. The complaints mirror concerns that a number of\npolitical journalists have also raised in recent conversations with The\nHuffington Post.\n\n\n\nWhile the White House Correspondents\' Association has worked for greater\nmedia access for over a century and elects representatives to present the\ngroup\'s concerns to the administration, there isn\'t any comparable,\nestablished body working on behalf of the campaign press. Monday\'s meeting,\nwhich included about 17 journalists from outlets such as The New York\nTimes, The Washington Post, Politico, Time and McClatchy, was an attempt\nnot only to discuss such concerns, but eventually to present them to the\ncampaign in a unified way.\n\n\n\nAttendees discussed the feeling that the campaign hasn\'t provided enough\nnotice for events, resulting in logistical difficulties for those trying to\ncover them. It\xe2\x80\x99s still too early in the election cycle for the campaign to\nbe chartering the flights and buses that news organizations, at the cost of\nthousands of dollars, can sign up for to follow the candidate from stop to\nstop. For now, reporters are booking commercial flights to reach Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s\nevents, and networks need to make sure satellite trucks and camera\nequipment make it there on time. The group discussed urging the Clinton\ncampaign to provide information outlining the upcoming week so they can\nplan accordingly.\n\n\n\nAnother concern raised, according to attendees, was that the campaign had\ninitially said that fundraisers of more than 100 people would be open to\nthe press through a pool system. Under this arrangement, certain reporters\nare designated to cover events that cannot accommodate large numbers of\njournalists, and those reporters then provide information to the larger\npress corps. But recent Clinton fundraisers have been closed press.\n\n\n\nMeeting attendees also expressed dissatisfaction with the ground rules\nestablished for a Thursday briefing at the campaign\'s Brooklyn headquarters\nthat was attended by dozens of news outlets, including The Huffington Post.\n\n\n\nCNBC\xe2\x80\x99s John Harwood wrote Friday that reporters who attended the briefing\nwere not allowed to quote top campaign officials directly, even when it\ncame to information that appeared to be basic talking points. Harwood noted\nthat he could not show readers what campaign staffers\xe2\x80\x99 desks looked like\nbecause \xe2\x80\x9cthe post-briefing tour was deemed off-the-record.\xe2\x80\x9d (A week\nearlier, the Nashua Telegraph, a New Hampshire newspaper, similarly mocked\nthe Clinton campaign for holding a conference call in which mundane\ninformation was provided under ground rules that those speaking should not\nbe quoted.)\n\n\n\nCoincidentally, Monday\'s meeting wrapped up just before the campaign sent a\nmass email to journalists with details of an upcoming event. The campaign\nsaid the details could only be attributed to a \xe2\x80\x9ccampaign official,\xe2\x80\x9d which\nprompted New York Times reporter Adam Nagourney to out the sender on\nTwitter. Such rules for anonymity, Nagourney noted, are not done\nunilaterally but established between two parties. He also pointed out that\nthe information itself didn\'t "rise to [the] level" of requiring anonymity.\n\n\n\nThere was a general consensus at Monday\'s meeting that the ground rules for\nthe Thursday headquarters briefing were unacceptable. Attendees say they\nexpected that the group will urge the campaign to agree that similar\nbriefings need to be on the record in the future.\n\n\n\nWhen asked about the reporters\' complaints and how the campaign is\nreacting, Clinton spokesman Nick Merrill responded in an email to HuffPost.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99d say two things,\xe2\x80\x9d he wrote. \xe2\x80\x9cFirst, we want a happy press corps as much\nas the press corps does. Not in an effort to obtain favorable coverage, but\nbecause we\'re decent humans who want people to be able to plan their lives.\nIt\'s a long campaign, and we are going to do our best to find equilibrium.\nGriping on background is not a constructive solution though, and I can\'t\nhelp but point out the irony here."\n\n\n\nThe group also discussed its system for disseminating pool reports, which\nThe Washington Post criticized Friday for turning some reporters "into\nsecond-class journalists in the hunt for Clinton info.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nThe pool system, established at the urging of the Clinton campaign but run\nby campaign reporters, places journalists on a rotation and disseminates\nreports in real-time to fourteen news organizations. Those organizations,\nwhich do not bear the costs of being in the pool, receive the reports at\nthe end of the day.\n\n\n\nThough the Post put forth the idea of the system creating two classes of\nreporters, attendees at Monday\xe2\x80\x99s meeting stressed that the system allows\nfor wider dissemination of traveling pool reports than was possible during\nMitt Romney\'s campaign four years ago. At that time, only reporters\nphysically present for Romney campaign trips received pool reports, and\nthere was no wider dissemination to news organizations not in the rotation.\n\n\n\n*Hillary Clinton Focuses on Drug Addiction After Learning Scale of Problem\n<http://www.nytimes.com/politics/first-draft/2015/06/01/hillary-clinton-focuses-on-drug-addiction-after-learning-scale-of-problem/>\n// NYT // Amy Chozick \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nHillary Rodham Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s carefully choreographed round-table discussions\nwith voters don\xe2\x80\x99t lead to many moments of surprise. But Mrs. Clinton has\nseemed to have had some legitimate jolts when conversations in Iowa and New\nHampshire repeatedly drifted back to drug abuse.\n\n\n\nMrs. Clinton called heroin and methamphetamine addiction in rural America a\n\xe2\x80\x9cquiet epidemic\xe2\x80\x9d and told her policy advisers in Brooklyn to put it on the\nlist of priorities as her campaign inched closer toward presenting a\nspecific policy platform.\n\n\n\nAs part of that effort, last week senior campaign policy advisers held\nGoogle Hangout discussions with local officials and substance abuse\nactivists in Iowa and New Hampshire to see how the campaign could best\naddress the problem, the first of such discussions that will take place in\nthe early nominating states, according to the campaign.\n\n\n\nIn the six years Mrs. Clinton has been mostly out of the discussion on\ndomestic policies, heroin use has swept rural communities, and although\naides say she was aware of problem in an abstract way, from reading policy\nbriefings and talking to academics and advisers, her discussions with\nvoters on the issue were particularly eye opening.\n\n\n\nShe instructed her policy team \xe2\x80\x9cto go beyond standard policies and really\ntake a hard look at some of the more creative or forward-looking policy\npositions,\xe2\x80\x9d said Jake Sullivan, the campaign\xe2\x80\x99s senior policy director.\n\n\n\nThe Google Hangouts, led by the senior policy advisers Ann O\xe2\x80\x99Leary and Maya\nHarris, are part of that effort. Moving forward, drug addiction, according\nto aides, will be a central part of the \xe2\x80\x9cfour fights\xe2\x80\x9d that Mrs. Clinton\nroutinely references in her prepared remarks.\n\n\n\nParticipants in the hangouts included Candace Accord, of the Community\nBased Correctional Facility in Cedar Rapids, Iowa, and Abigail Shockley,\nexecutive director of the New Hampshire Alcohol and Other Drug Service\nProvider Association, among other local community leaders and elected\nofficials.\n\n\n\nBased on their suggestions, Mrs. Clinton is likely to propose\nbetter-financed prevention and treatment options before criminalization and\nbetter access to mental health services (an area that aides and voters have\nsaid is lacking under the Affordable Care Act). She has already called for\nreform to the criminal justice system and a prison system overflowing with\nlow-level drug offenders.\n\n\n\nDrug abuse has not been a central campaign issue since the 1980s and early\n1990s, when crime was on the rise and the crack cocaine epidemic threatened\nAmerican cities. Candidates, particularly Republicans, and the more\ncentrist-minded Bill Clinton were elected by vowing to be tough on drugs.\nUnder President Bill Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s administration, drug offenders received\nstiffer penalties under federal law.\n\n\n\nIn the 2016 election, Mrs. Clinton enters a very different situation, in\nwhich rural areas, like the ones she has visited in Iowa and New Hampshire,\nare seeing an increase in addiction. She is expected to present more\nspecific policy proposals after her campaign\xe2\x80\x99s official kickoff event on\nJune 13.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe have an increasing problem that is only beginning to break through the\nsurface so that people \xe2\x80\x93 I think a lot of people are thinking, well, that\xe2\x80\x99s\nsomebody else\xe2\x80\x99s problem, that\xe2\x80\x99s not my problem,\xe2\x80\x9d Mrs. Clinton has said.\n\n\n\n*It\'s time for the media to admit that Hillary Clinton is popular\n<http://www.vox.com/2015/6/1/8676727/hillary-clinton-popularity> // Vox //\nMatthew Yglesias \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nQuinnipiac is out with a new poll that confirms something the national\nmedia is loathe to admit and essentially never surfaces in their coverage\nof one of the most-covered people in the world today: Hillary Clinton is\nthe most popular politician in America.\n\n\n\nIt would be genuinely silly to think that her early leads in general\nelection polling tell us anything interesting about what will happen in\nNovember 2016. But they tell us a lot about how people feel in May 2015,\nand the way they feel is pretty good about Hillary Clinton.\n\n\n\nAccording to Gallup, for example, she is the most admired woman in the\nworld. What\'s more, she has been the most admired woman in the world for 17\nout of the past 18 years.\n\n\n\nJournalists don\'t like Hillary Clinton\n\n\n\nBut the press hates to admit this. For Clinton, good news is never just\ngood news. Instead it\'s an opportunity to remind the public about the\nmedia\'s negative narratives about Clinton and then to muse on the fact that\nher ratings somehow manage to hold up despite these narratives.\n\n\n\nHere\'s how the Wall Street Journal wrote up an earlier poll showing Clinton\nbeating all opponents:\n\n\n\nHillary Clinton\'s stature has been battered after more than a month of\ncontroversy over her fundraising and email practices, but support for her\namong Democrats remains strong and unshaken, a new Wall Street Journal/NBC\nNews poll finds.\n\n\n\nAnd here\'s how the New York Times wrote up yet another poll showing Clinton\nbeating all opponents:\n\n\n\nHillary Rodham Clinton appears to have initially weathered a barrage of\nnews about her use of a private email account when she was secretary of\nstate and the practices of her family\'s foundation, an indication that she\nis starting her second presidential bid with an unusual durability among\nDemocratic voters.\n\n\n\nThis framing is not surprising, since, among journalists, Clinton is one of\nthe least popular politicians. She is not forthcoming or entertaining with\nthe press. She doesn\'t offer good quotes. She doesn\'t like journalists,\nrespect what we do, or care to hide her disdain for the media. She feels\nthat the right-wing press has tried to destroy her for decades, that the\nmainstream press got played like a cheap fiddle by the conservative press,\nand that even the liberal press was overwhelmingly hostile to her during\nher 2008 campaign.\n\n\n\nThe public also hates journalists\n\n\n\nJournalists are obviously free to dislike politicians who are uncooperative\nwith the press, and to celebrate those who embrace a more freewheeling\nmedia-friendly style. But reporters all-too-often confused the conventional\nwisdom of the journo-pack with the opinions of actual voters.\n\n\n\nThe reality is that Clinton\'s disdain for the press is largely shared by\nthe public, which does not think journalists are credible or contribute to\nsociety\'s well-being.\n\n\n\nAt the same time, most of the "bad" narratives about both Clintons that\nexist in the media are essentially self-centered. From an impeachment\ngrounded in Bill\'s effort to keep an extra-marital affair out of the\nnewspapers to a scandal about an email server designed to keep the contents\nof Hillary\'s messages out of the newspapers, the Clintons have continually\nrun afoul of the press\' fervent desire to know everything.\n\n\n\nBut few regular people evaluate public figures on the basis of their level\nof cooperation with media inquiries. Clinton\'s brand of cautious\ncenter-left politics and her genuine passion for trying to bring people\ntogether and make deals more-or-less reflects what the public wants from a\npolitician.\n\n\n\n*Hillary Clinton Still Strong in Iowa Poll, Though Negative News Is a\nConcern\n<http://www.nytimes.com/politics/first-draft/2015/06/01/hillary-clinton-still-strong-in-iowa-poll-though-negative-news-is-a-concern/?module=BlogPost-Title&version=Blog%20Main&contentCollection=Politics&action=Click&pgtype=Blogs&region=Body>\n// NYT // Trip Gabriel \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nHillary Rodham Clinton continues to command a sizable lead in a poll\nreleased on Monday of Iowa Democrats, who will cast the first votes of the\npresidential nominating race early next year. At the same time, Democrats\nare worried that revelations about Mrs. Clinton could hurt her in the\ngeneral election.\n\n\n\nMrs. Clinton is the choice of 57 percent of likely Democratic Iowa\ncaucusgoers, followed by 16 percent for Senator Bernie Sanders of Vermont\nand 2 percent for former Gov. Martin O\xe2\x80\x99Malley of Maryland. Vice President\nJoseph R. Biden Jr., who has shown little interest in running, received 8\npercent.\n\n\n\nThe poll was conducted for The Des Moines Register and Bloomberg Politics\nfrom May 25 to 29. Mr. Sanders, who drew large crowds in the state during\nthe end of that period, was up from 5 percent in a January survey by the\nsame pollsters. He has inherited the support of his party\xe2\x80\x99s most liberal\nwing that once favored Senator Elizabeth Warren of Massachusetts, who was\nnot included in the poll after repeatedly saying she was not a candidate.\n\n\n\nMr. Sanders or Mr. O\xe2\x80\x99Malley, who officially entered the race on Saturday\nand is also carving out a lane to the left of Mrs. Clinton, seem to have\nroom to grow: 37 percent of likely Democratic caucusgoers said their\npolitical beliefs were closer to Ms. Warren\xe2\x80\x99s than Mrs. Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s.\n\n\n\nSupport for Mrs. Clinton stayed steady since the earlier Iowa poll in\nJanuary. It showed no softening despite the continuing spate of negative\nnews accounts of foreign donations to her family foundation while she was\nsecretary of state, her use of a private email account in office, and a\nRepublican-led investigation of her handling of the attacks in Benghazi,\nLibya.\n\n\n\nBut 66 percent of Democrats said that at least one of those issues will\nhurt Mrs. Clinton in the general election if she is the nominee.\n\n\n\n*Here\xe2\x80\x99s the best news for Hillary Clinton in that new Iowa poll\n<http://www.washingtonpost.com/blogs/the-fix/wp/2015/06/01/heres-the-best-news-in-that-new-iowa-poll-for-hillary-clinton/>\n// WaPo// Chris Cillizza \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nIt\'s not been a very good last month for Hillary Clinton\'s presidential\ncampaign. She\'s been dogged by questions regarding donations made to the\nClinton Foundation, bad publicity surrounding the release of her State\nDepartment e-mails and a continued unwillingness to engage the media.\n\n\n\nDoesn\'t matter! That\'s according to a new Des Moines Register/Bloomberg\npoll of Iowa Democratic caucus-goers, who in large majorities believe the\nClintons are getting a raw deal in all of this. Seven in ten respondents\n(71 percent) said that regarding the "controversies surrounding Bill and\nHillary Clinton," the couple is getting a "bad rap." Just 14 percent said\nthe controversies were indicative of a "pattern of unethical behavior" by\nthe former first couple.\n\n\n\nYes, these are Democrats. And Iowa Democrats, as we\'ve learned over the\npast decade or so, are on the liberal side of the ledger.  So if anyone was\ngoing to rally to Clinton\'s side against the perceived attacks of\nRepublicans and the mainstream media, it\'s true believers like the ones\ntested in the DMR poll.\n\n\n\nStill, the fact that there is a widespread belief that things like the\nprivate e-mail server or the donors to the Clinton Foundation are trumped\nup is extremely good news for Clinton.\n\n\n\nThe key for Clinton \xe2\x80\x94 in both the primary and, to a certain extent, the\ngeneral election \xe2\x80\x94 is to rally Democrats, especially liberal Democrats, to\nher cause. In the early days of her presidential campaign, she has staked\nout decidedly liberal positions on hot-button issues like immigration and\nincome inequality. But oftentimes, the best way to convince people you are\none of them is to come under attack from enemies of those people. (Enemy of\nmy enemy and all that.) And Republicans and, increasingly, the media, are\nvery much enemies in the eyes of dyed-in-the-wool liberals.\n\n\n\nIf liberals \xe2\x80\x94 like those in Iowa \xe2\x80\x94 continue to see stories about the e-mail\nserver and the Clinton Foundation as part of a broader witch hunt against\nClinton being organized by her political enemies and reporters with an ax\nto grind, that\'s a best-case scenario for the former secretary of state.\nWhy? Because with every report on her e-mails or her donors, it affirms the\nsense within her liberal base that she\'s being unfairly maligned.  The more\nthe merrier, from Clinton\'s point of view.\n\n\n\nThe alternate reality is that these scads of stories raise doubts about\nClinton\'s ability to win next November and, as a result, people begin to\nshop for a different candidate. While there is some evidence that\nDemocratic voters are slightly worried about that possibility (four in ten\nDemocrats in the DMR poll say that keeping a private e-mail server will\nhurt Clinton in the general election), they remain largely united behind\nher.\n\n\n\nThe more Clinton can turn the negative storylines around her into an "us\nversus them" (no matter who the "them" really entails) conversation, the\nbetter for her chances.\n\n\n\n*Meet the woman behind Hillary Clinton\'s Twitter account\n<http://fortune.com/2015/06/01/meet-the-woman-behind-hillary-clintons-twitter-account/>\n// Fortune // Nina Easton \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nKatie Dowd is the campaign\xe2\x80\x99s digital director, in charge of putting the\nswagger in Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s Twitter\xe2\x80\x93not to mention Facebook, Instagram, Tumblr and\nall the rest.\n\n\n\nWith many of the power players from Hillary Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s 2008 presidential run\nare sitting this one out, the big question is: Who\xe2\x80\x99s in?\n\n\n\nWhat follows is the latest installment of a Fortune series looking at the\nthe most influential women on Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s 2016 team. When this series wraps,\nwe\xe2\x80\x99ll turn our attention to the most powerful women on the GOP side of the\nrace.\n\n\n\nKatie Dowd may be in charge of the Clinton campaign\xe2\x80\x99s digital strategy, but\nshe\xe2\x80\x99s not all about pixels. Indeed, Dowd is a self-described \xe2\x80\x9cpeople\ngeek\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94a sociology major drawn to politics because she\xe2\x80\x99s interested in\nunderstanding what makes people tick. After graduating from Illinois\xe2\x80\x99\nWittenberg University, she headed to D.C. and wound up working for a direct\nmail firm, learning old-style political persuasion that would later become\nuseful in the exploding universe of social media. She worked at the two\norganizations charged with electing Democratic members of Congress\xe2\x80\x94the\nDemocratic Senate Campaign Committee and the Democratic Congressional\nCampaign Committee.\n\n\n\nMost recently, Dowd worked on a State Department project called TechCamp,\nwhich helped civil society groups around the globe harness web tools for\nsocial action. A prime example: The Lithuanian activist who wanted to make\nthe buildings in his town wheelchair accessible. Through TechCamp, he was\nable to use Google Maps to \xe2\x80\x9ctag\xe2\x80\x9d buildings and prove to authorities that\nphysically disabled residents were being excluded. Before this project,\nDowd worked on STEM (science, technology, engineering and math) issues as\nsenior adviser to the chief technology officer at the White House.\n\n\n\nWhen Dowd started out in political campaigns a decade ago, early engagement\nwith voters was mostly an exercise in fund-raising; operatives viewed the\nInternet as an ATM machine. That has changed dramatically. Now, engaging\nvoters online means a lot more than asking them to write checks. On the\nDemocratic side, the presidential campaigns of Howard Dean and John Kerry\nset the bar for using the web to create a grassroots network of passionate\nvoters\xe2\x80\x93a trend that Obama all but perfected in 2008. When Dowd was part of\nthe 2008 Clinton campaign, the team experimented with new digital\ntechniques, like enabling volunteers to make internet calls to fellow\nvoters from their own homes.\n\n\n\nThis time around it\xe2\x80\x99s a far bigger, more complicated ball game. Dowd and\nher staff (likely to grow to 150) will have to manage a range platforms,\nfrom Twitter and FaceBook to Instagram, Tumblr, Pintrest\xe2\x80\x94and likely other\nemerging networks we haven\xe2\x80\x99t even heard of yet. \xe2\x80\x9cWe have to think about\nwhere the audiences are,\xe2\x80\x9d says Dowd. Real-time video platforms like Meerkat\nand Periscope will change how campaigns operate. In the 2016 race, says\nDowd, the focus will be on \xe2\x80\x9cletting people feel like they are part of the\nreal-time movement of a campaign.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nAnd of course, there is the low-tech, but essential challenge: How to give\nvoters a lasting personal connection to Hillary connection. Already, Dowd\nhas helped craft the candidate\xe2\x80\x99s famous Twitter bio: Wife, mom, grandma,\nwomen+kids advocate, FLOTUS, Senator, SecState, hair icon, pantsuit\naficionado, 2016 presidential candidate.\n\n\n\nWhat\xe2\x80\x99s her next move? Keep an eye on your screens.\n\n\n\n*Hillary Clinton camp seeks to both raise and lower expectations\n<http://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/hillary-clinton-camp-seeks-to-both-raise-and-lower-expectations/2015/06/01/6302ac86-0882-11e5-a7ad-b430fc1d3f5c_story.html?tid=HP_politics?tid=HP_politics>\n// WaPo // Anne Gearan \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nHillary Rodham Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s campaign spokesman on Monday sought to raise and\nlower expectations at the same time, announ\xc2\xadcing a New York City venue for\nher first big rally while also suggesting that she does not expect to break\n50 percent in the early primary states of Iowa and New Hampshire.\n\n\n\nThe dueling messages reflect the Democratic front-runner\xe2\x80\x99s desire not to be\nseen as an inevitable nominee \xe2\x80\x94 a posture that hurt her during her failed\nrun in 2008 \xe2\x80\x94 while also ramping up excitement at the prospect of the\nnation\xe2\x80\x99s first female president.\n\n\n\nAt her first major rally, to be held June 13 on New York\xe2\x80\x99s Roosevelt\nIsland, Clinton will lay out the main principles of her campaign. PAC\n<http://www.washingtonexaminer.com/watchdog-accuses-clinton-campaign-of-illegally-obtaining-email-list-from-super-pac/article/2565394>\n// Washington Examiner // Sarah Westwood \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nA watchdog group is asking the Federal Election Commission to review\nwhether Hillary Clinton\'s presidential campaign legally obtained a massive\nemail list from a political action committee associated with the candidate.\n\n\n\nThe Foundation for Accountability and Civic Trust pressed the FEC Monday on\nhow the Clinton campaign was able to "swap" unknown items for a collection\nof nearly 4 million supporters\' email addresses that had been compiled by\nthe Ready for Hillary super PAC.\n\n\n\n"Federal law explicitly prohibits a candidate from coordinating with and\naccepting donations, including an in-kind donation of a mailing list, from\na super PAC," wrote Matthew Whitaker, FACT\'s executive director, in a\nletter Monday supplementing a complaint filed in April.\n\n\n\nThe original FEC complaint alleged Clinton had used Ready for Hillary to\nvacuum up supporter information and contributions in a manner befitting a\nfull-fledge campaign long before announcing her candidacy.\n\n\n\nWhitaker cited a Saturday report from Politico that suggested the Clinton\ncampaign had "gained entry to the independent super PAC\'s list through a\nswap with another independent group," although Politico did not name the\nthird group involved in the transfer.\n\n\n\nA spokesman for the Clinton campaign declined to comment on the swap.\n\n\n\nLarry Noble, senior counsel at the Campaign Legal Center, said the debate\nover whether the transaction was legal boils down to the "fair market\nvalue" of Ready for Hillary\'s email list.\n\n\n\n"It would be considered an illegal in-kind contribution to the campaign if\nthe campaign did not pay, in monetary or list-swap terms, what the fair\nmarket value is for the list that it\'s getting," Noble said.\n\n\n\nThe FEC would be the ultimate arbiter of the fair market value if a\nquestion was raised, he noted.\n\n\n\n"I think we\'re going to run into an issue here because, as far as I know,\nthe campaign hasn\'t identified the groups involved and until we know more\nabout that, there are going to be a lot of serious questions raised," Noble\nsaid. "The concern is that the Clinton campaign is getting a list of\ntremendous value and paying little or nothing for it."\n\n\n\nWhitaker said his group had long suspected Ready for Hillary was preparing\nto transfer the email list to Clinton\'s campaign.\n\n\n\n"If the campaign swapped lists with the super PAC, what value would a list\nhave to a closing super PAC?" Whitaker said. "Right now, we do not know who\nthe Clinton campaign swapped lists with or how, if not the super PAC, that\ngroup got the lists."\n\n\n\nReady for Hillary reportedly began to shutter its operations in April.\n\n\n\nThe super PAC survived an FEC review earlier this year after an\nanti-Clinton group complained about Ready for Hillary\'s decision to rent an\nemail list from the candidate-in-waiting\'s prior Senate race.\n\n\n\nThe commission had an "insufficient number of votes" to find the super PAC\nin violation of a number of campaign laws and dismissed outright several\nother allegations, including that Ready for Hillary had sent an email to\nsupporters in January 2014 that was authorized by Clinton herself.\n\n\n\n*Hillary Clinton to Rally in New York, Then Tour Early Voting States\n<http://www.nytimes.com/politics/first-draft/2015/06/01/hillary-clinton-to-rally-in-new-york-then-tour-early-voting-states/>\n// NYT // Amy Chozick \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nHillary Rodham Clinton will hold the first major rally of her presidential\ncampaign on June 13 on Roosevelt Island in New York City, before embarking\non a five-day swing through the four states with the earliest Democratic\nnominating contests, her campaign said on Monday.\n\n\n\nIn a midday speech at Four Freedoms Park \xe2\x80\x94 a memorial to Franklin D.\nRoosevelt, for whom the East River island is named \xe2\x80\x94 Mrs. Clinton will\nsketch out her view of the problems facing the nation and her \xe2\x80\x9cvision and\nideas\xe2\x80\x9d for how to move the country forward, a top spokesman, Jesse\nFerguson, said in an email to reporters that also noted Mrs. Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s\nadmiration for both F.D.R. and Eleanor Roosevelt.\n\n\n\n>From New York, she will travel to Iowa, New Hampshire, South Carolina and\nNevada.\n\n\n\nIn the email, Mr. Ferguson also sought to lower expectations for Mrs.\nClinton in Iowa and New Hampshire. Roosevelt Four Freedoms Park, which belatedly opened in\n2012, four decades after architect Louis Kahn first began designing the\nmemorial to the former president.\n\n\n\nClinton can count on an impressive backdrop of the skyscrapers of Midtown\nManhattan as she gives what her campaign says will be her fullest\nexplanation yet of why she should be elected president next year.  How a\ncrowd of thousands might reach the island is less clear at this point \xe2\x80\x93 it\nhas a single subway station that rarely deals with large crowds, and a tram\ncar system, memorably featured in the climactic battle scene in the 2002\n\xe2\x80\x9cSpider-Man\xe2\x80\x9d film, that can deliver about 100 people to the island at a\ntime. There is also a small bridge connecting the mostly car-free island to\nthe borough of Queens.\n\n\n\nClinton, who moved to New York in 1999 ahead of a successful run to become\na Democratic U.S. senator for the state, picked the park in part because\nshe said she was inspired by Roosevelt\xe2\x80\x99s presidency and considered his\nwife, Eleanor Roosevelt, a role model, according to the announcement email.\nWhen she last ran for president in 2007, she held her first rally at school\ngym in Des Moines, Iowa, a few days after her initial announcement. This\ntime around, Clinton has been an announced candidate for about seven weeks,\nbut has only held small events with little or no access for the general\npublic.\n\n\n\nThe hospitals and prisons that once made the island infamous have long been\nreplaced by small clusters of middle-class housing, popular with people who\nwork at the United Nations headquarters just across the water. Although\nClinton is yet to discuss much in the way of specific policies, she has\nsaid she is concerned both about reducing the number of people the U.S.\nsends to prison and making it easier for people with mental health problems\nto get treatment. Given the setting of her rally, Clinton may be tempted to\ninvoke the work of Nellie Bly, the celebrated journalist whose 1887 book\n\xe2\x80\x9cTen Days in a Mad-House\xe2\x80\x9d, written after she feigned insanity and got\nherself committed, caused outrage for exposing the abusive treatment of\nmentally ill inmates on the island.\n\nHillary Clinton: First stop is New York City\xe2\x80\x99s Welfare Island\n<http://www.washingtontimes.com/news/2015/jun/1/hillary-clinton-sets-first-big-rally-new-york-city/>\n// Washington Times // S. A. Miller \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015\n\n\n\nAttempting to draw a connection with a liberal hero, Hillary Rodham Clinton\narranged for her first big campaign rally to take place this month in New\nYork City\xe2\x80\x99s Franklin D. Roosevelt Four Freedoms Park \xe2\x80\x94 a landmark\npreviously known as Welfare Island.\n\n\n\nThe Clinton campaign stressed the Roosevelt connection rather than the\nwelfare moniker that until 1973 was the name for the narrow island in New\nYork\xe2\x80\x99s East River, campaign officials said.\n\n\n\nThey said the location will showcase her ties to the city as a former\nsenator from New York, who also put her campaign headquarters in Brooklyn,\nand reflect how her life\xe2\x80\x99s work was inspired by former President Franklin\nD. That island is Riker\'s Island.\n\n\n\nI\'m not the type to go looking for metaphors in things! I am not that type!\nI am merely here to offer insights as a New Yorker-American into the ins\nand outs of New York life. Including the details of Roosevelt Island.\n\n\n\nFirst of all: Roosevelt Island is a cool place to visit. It use to house a\nsmallpox quarantine center at its southern end, which is still in the\nprocess of being restored (after partially collapsing a few years back).\nIt\'s got a bunch of new housing and a spectacularly painted public pool.\nBut it is about as inconvenient a place to get to in New York as is\nconceivable.\n\n\n\nThere are three ways onto the island.\n\n\n\nBy car: The red line shows the one route onto the island by car. You have\nto get to Queens and make your way through back streets in an industrial\narea to do so. The Queensboro Bridge (or whatever it is called now that New\nYorkers ignore) passes over the island, but has no outlets onto it. (It\nwould be hard to do so, given how high the bridge is.)\n\n\n\nWhat\'s left, then, is that little scroungy two-lane bridge from Queens,\nlimiting how many people can get across it. But most people don\'t.\n\n\n\nBy train: Instead, they usually use the subway (the black line). Now, here\nis a secret about taking the subway to Roosevelt Island: It is terrible.\n\n\n\nIn order to get under the East River, the train tunnel is very deep\nunderground, meaning you have to take about six escalators up to get to the\nsurface. Maybe more, I haven\'t counted. I tried to take the stairs once,\ninstead, and actually almost passed out. I\'m not an athlete. But still.\n\n\n\nBy tram: The cool way to get to the island, the way that\'s mentioned\ninHollywood Movies, is to take the newly refurbished tram, seen here in\nblue.\n\n\n\nIt holds maybe 20 people at a time and takes probably 10 minutes. It\'s\nbeautiful! I recommend it to visitors. However, it is not mass transit in\nthe sense of accommodating masses of people for rapid transit.\n\n\n\nI am not the type to find metaphors in things, as I said. I am just\nreporting that the Hillary Clinton campaign is launching from one of the\nleast accessible parts of New York City. That is all I am doing here in\nthis article. I\'ve made a lot of money. I\'m giving it\nall back to society," he said.\n\n\n\nClinton\'s populist critique of hedge fund manager tax rates has also come\nunder scrutiny for its accuracy.\n\n\n\n"Her broad-brush assertion does not hold up to scrutiny, even when the\ntalking point is uttered correctly," the Washington Post\'s Glenn Kessler\nwrote in May. "Overall, even hedge fund managers pay higher taxes\xe2\x80\x94and tax\nrates\xe2\x80\x94than middle-class Americans."\n\n\n\nThe Tampa Bay Times\' Politifact concurred.\n\n\n\n"She is certainly wrong for dollar amounts, which is what her statement was\nabout. On Sunday,\nO\'Malley renewed that criticism by noting that Goldman Sachs CEO Lloyd\nBlankfein allegedly said that he would be happy if either Clinton or Jeb\nBush was elected president in 2016.\n\n\n\nBlankfein is an investor with Eaglevale Partners, which Mezvinsky started\nwith his former Goldman Sachs colleagues Bennett Grau and Mark Mallon.\n\n\n\n*Journalists Meet To Discuss Frustration With Clinton Campaign\'s Control\nOver Access And Information\n<http://www.huffingtonpost.com/2015/06/01/journalists-clinton-campaign_n_7487076.html?1433194660>\n// HuffPo // Michael Calderone \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nNEW YORK -- Journalists covering Hillary Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s presidential campaign\nmet for nearly two hours in Washington on Monday to discuss concerns about\nwhat they believe is inadequate access to cover the Democratic\nfront-runner, according to people who attended.\n\n\n\nThe grievances discussed at the private gathering, which was held at the\nLos Angeles Times/Tribune Washington offices, go beyond Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s\nunwillingness so far to substantively engage with the press, a topic that\nhas already been discussed publicly on cable news and social media.\nAttendees of the meeting, who were not authorized by their news\norganizations to speak on the record, charge the Clinton campaign with\nkeeping an excessively tight grip on information, even when it comes to\nlogistical details that don\'t seem particularly sensitive or revelatory.\n\n\n\nAmong the problems discussed were the campaign\'s failure to provide\nadequate notice prior to events, the lack of a clear standard for whether\nfundraisers are open or closed press and the reflexive tendency to opt to\nspeak anonymously. The complaints mirror concerns that a number of\npolitical journalists have also raised in recent conversations with The\nHuffington Post.\n\n\n\nWhile the White House Correspondents\' Association has worked for greater\nmedia access for over a century and elects representatives to present the\ngroup\'s concerns to the administration, there isn\'t any comparable,\nestablished body working on behalf of the campaign press. Monday\'s meeting,\nwhich included about 17 journalists from outlets such as The New York\nTimes, The Washington Post, Politico, Time and McClatchy, was an attempt\nnot only to discuss such concerns, but eventually to present them to the\ncampaign in a unified way.\n\n\n\nAttendees discussed the feeling that the campaign hasn\'t provided enough\nnotice for events, resulting in logistical difficulties for those trying to\ncover them. It\xe2\x80\x99s still too early in the election cycle for the campaign to\nbe chartering the flights and buses that news organizations, at the cost of\nthousands of dollars, can sign up for to follow the candidate from stop to\nstop. For now, reporters are booking commercial flights to reach Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s\nevents, and networks need to make sure satellite trucks and camera\nequipment make it there on time. The group discussed urging the Clinton\ncampaign to provide information outlining the upcoming week so they can\nplan accordingly.\n\n\n\nAnother concern raised, according to attendees, was that the campaign had\ninitially said that fundraisers of more than 100 people would be open to\nthe press through a pool system. Under this arrangement, certain reporters\nare designated to cover events that cannot accommodate large numbers of\njournalists, and those reporters then provide information to the larger\npress corps. But recent Clinton fundraisers have been closed press.\n\n\n\nMeeting attendees also expressed dissatisfaction with the ground rules\nestablished for a Thursday briefing at the campaign\'s Brooklyn headquarters\nthat was attended by dozens of news outlets, including The Huffington Post.\n\n\n\nCNBC\xe2\x80\x99s John Harwood wrote Friday that reporters who attended the briefing\nwere not allowed to quote top campaign officials directly, even when it\ncame to information that appeared to be basic talking points. Harwood noted\nthat he could not show readers what campaign staffers\xe2\x80\x99 desks looked like\nbecause \xe2\x80\x9cthe post-briefing tour was deemed off-the-record.\xe2\x80\x9d (A week\nearlier, the Nashua Telegraph, a New Hampshire newspaper, similarly mocked\nthe Clinton campaign for holding a conference call in which mundane\ninformation was provided under ground rules that those speaking should not\nbe quoted.)\n\n\n\nCoincidentally, Monday\'s meeting wrapped up just before the campaign sent a\nmass email to journalists with details of an upcoming event. The campaign\nsaid the details could only be attributed to a \xe2\x80\x9ccampaign official,\xe2\x80\x9d which\nprompted New York Times reporter Adam Nagourney to out the sender on\nTwitter. Such rules for anonymity, Nagourney noted, are not done\nunilaterally but established between two parties. He also pointed out that\nthe information itself didn\'t "rise to [the] level" of requiring anonymity.\n\n\n\nThere was a general consensus at Monday\'s meeting that the ground rules for\nthe Thursday headquarters briefing were unacceptable. Attendees say they\nexpected that the group will urge the campaign to agree that similar\nbriefings need to be on the record in the future.\n\n\n\nWhen asked about the reporters\' complaints and how the campaign is\nreacting, Clinton spokesman Nick Merrill responded in an email to HuffPost.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99d say two things,\xe2\x80\x9d he wrote. \xe2\x80\x9cFirst, we want a happy press corps as much\nas the press corps does. Not in an effort to obtain favorable coverage, but\nbecause we\'re decent humans who want people to be able to plan their lives.\nIt\'s a long campaign, and we are going to do our best to find equilibrium.\nGriping on background is not a constructive solution though, and I can\'t\nhelp but point out the irony here."\n\n\n\nThe group also discussed its system for disseminating pool reports, which\nThe Washington Post criticized Friday for turning some reporters "into\nsecond-class journalists in the hunt for Clinton info.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nThe pool system, established at the urging of the Clinton campaign but run\nby campaign reporters, places journalists on a rotation and disseminates\nreports in real-time to fourteen news organizations. Those organizations,\nwhich do not bear the costs of being in the pool, receive the reports at\nthe end of the day.\n\n\n\nThough the Post put forth the idea of the system creating two classes of\nreporters, attendees at Monday\xe2\x80\x99s meeting stressed that the system allows\nfor wider dissemination of traveling pool reports than was possible during\nMitt Romney\'s campaign four years ago. At that time, only reporters\nphysically present for Romney campaign trips received pool reports, and\nthere was no wider dissemination to news organizations not in the rotation.\n\n\n\n*New York Times reporter blows up Clinton campaign\xe2\x80\x99s \xe2\x80\x98background\xe2\x80\x99 e-mail\n<http://www.washingtonpost.com/blogs/erik-wemple/wp/2015/06/01/new-york-times-reporter-blows-up-clinton-campaigns-background-e-mail/>\n// WaPo // Erik Wemple \xe2\x80\x93June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nAdam Nagourney is the Los Angeles bureau chief for the New York Times.\nThough he\xe2\x80\x99s the paper\xe2\x80\x99s former chief political reporter, he\xe2\x80\x99s not currently\nassigned to cover the campaign of Democratic 2016 hopeful Hillary Rodham\nClinton. But he receives the campaign\xe2\x80\x99s e-mails.\n\n\n\nAnd tweets about them:\n\n\n\nThat tweet was an apparent reference to a June 1 e-mail from the Clinton\ncampaign that included this data point: \xe2\x80\x9cIn Iowa, no Democratic candidate\nfor president has ever received more than 50% of the caucus vote unless\nthey were a sitting President or Vice-President, or incumbent Iowa\nSenator.\xe2\x80\x9d More Nagourney:\n\n\n\nAs Nagourney noted, the e-mail addressed Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s June 13 campaign kickoff\nspeech at Franklin D. For example:\n\n\n\nHillary Clinton grew up in Illinois, and her career spent working on behalf\nof children and families has taken her from Massachusetts to Washington,\nD.C., Arkansas to New York. But it was the voters of New York who elected\nher to serve as their first female senator.\n\n\n\nNow let\xe2\x80\x99s attribute that snippet in accordance with the rules of the e-mail:\n\n\n\nHillary Clinton grew up in Illinois, said a Clinton campaign official in an\ne-mail sent to reporters, and her career spent working on behalf of\nchildren and families has taken her from Massachusetts to Washington, D.C.,\nArkansas to New York. But it was the voters of New York who elected her to\nserve as their first female senator, noted the campaign official.\n\n\n\nIn a chat with the Erik Wemple Blog, Nagourney said, \xe2\x80\x9cReporters negotiate\nthe terms of information with sources\xe2\x80\xa6.you can\xe2\x80\x99t go preemptively.\xe2\x80\x9d He\ncalled the information in the e-mail \xe2\x80\x9canodyne stuff.\xe2\x80\x9d \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s like give me a\nbreak,\xe2\x80\x9d he says. Nagourney isn\xe2\x80\x99t writing a piece on Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s campaign\nlaunch, nor has he heard any complaint from the Clinton people about his\ntweets. The Twitter commentary from Nagourney, furthermore, lands on a heap\nof other backlash pieces against the Clinton campaign team for generally\nworthless press briefings.\n\n\n\nAnd Nagourney has some experience torpedoing background e-mails. Way back\nin December 2003, Nagourney did a story on how the capture of Iraqi\nstrongman Saddam Hussein would affect the then-incipient race for the\nDemocratic presidential nomination. Around that time, Howard Dean was\nviewed as a threat to vanquish his rivals, who included eventual nominee\nSen. John Kerry. Nagourney wrote:\n\n\n\nThe strains this created were evident on Sunday. Mr. Kerry\xe2\x80\x99s press\nsecretary, Stephanie Cutter, sent an e-mail message to news organizations\nlisting remarks Dr. Dean had made over the past six months that she said\ndemonstrated that his opposition to the war was \xe2\x80\x9dpolitically driven.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nBut Ms. Cutter, reflecting the concern among the campaigns that they not be\nviewed as turning a foreign policy victory to political advantage, put a\nnote on the top of the statement demanding that it be reported as\n\xe2\x80\x9dbackground\xe2\x80\x9d and attributed only to a Democratic campaign.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cShe was upset,\xe2\x80\x9d Nagourney recalls, when asked how Cutter reacted to the\nouting.
