VOGEL \xe2\x80\x93 June 2, 2015*\n\n\n\nWinning over such donors is seen as critical to Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s White House\n\nprospects.\n\nHillary Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s allies are working to win over unenthusiastic rich\nliberals by pitting her against the Koch brothers and prospective GOP\nrivals rather than more progressive Democrats, according to a draft of a\nsecret memo obtained by POLITICO.\n\n\n\nThe memo was prepared for Clinton enforcer David Brock ahead of an April\nmajor donor meeting in San Francisco. But the concerns it reveals about\nliberal donors\xe2\x80\x99 coolness toward her presidential candidacy \xe2\x80\x93 with some even\nholding out hope for a robust primary challenge from the left \xe2\x80\x93 are just as\nacute today, Clinton allies say.\n\n\n\nWinning over such donors is seen as critical to Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s White House\nprospects.\n\n\n\nThe Clinton forces are counting on a constellation of allied outside groups\nto raise as much as $500 million to take on a Republican big-money machine\nthat has been raking in cash from dozens of super-rich and highly engaged\npartisans. By contrast, the main super PAC supporting Clinton, Priorities\nUSA Action, has struggled to collect million-dollar checks.\n\n\n\nPart of the reticence stems from liberal queasiness about the expanding\nrole of big money in politics since the Supreme Court\xe2\x80\x99s 2010 Citizens\nUnited decision. But there\xe2\x80\x99s also some discomfort with Hillary Clinton, the\nformer New York Senator and Secretary of State, who is seen as too hawkish\non foreign policy and insufficiently progressive on key issues like\nfighting climate change, income inequality and the role of big money in\npolitics. Additionally, Democratic finance operatives say, efforts to\nrustle up seven-figure checks are suffering from a lack of a single,\nunifying enemy on the right.\n\n\n\nAll those concerns are addressed in the Brock memo, which appears to have\nbeen drafted in preparation for his appearance at the annual spring meeting\nof the Democracy Alliance major liberal donor club in April in San\nFrancisco. The memo is written as a question-and-answer exchange between\nBrock and Democracy Alliance donors .\n\n\n\nThe memo suggests that Brock, who has built a fleet of deep-pocketed groups\naligned with Clinton, is taking a conciliatory approach to assuage donors\xe2\x80\x99\nconcerns \xe2\x80\x93 conceding she\xe2\x80\x99s not as liberal as some donors wish, but\nemphasizing her progessiveness in public service and minimizing the\nprospects of a vigorous Democratic primary.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou say the Kochs represent all that is bad in this broken system, yet our\npresumptive nominee is in the pocket of big Wall Street banks,\xe2\x80\x9d begins one\nof the memo\xe2\x80\x99s hypothetical donor questions. \xe2\x80\x9cAren\xe2\x80\x99t we going to have a hard\ntime going after the Kochs\xe2\x80\x99 big money when some could argue that Sec.\nClinton is bank rolled by Wall Street and therefore there is a pox on both\nour houses?\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nThe answer Brock should give, according to the memo: \xe2\x80\x9cIt is no secret that\nSec. Clinton is fair-left and not far-left. I think it is safe to say that\nthere will be a dramatic difference between Sec. Clinton and whoever is the\nRepublican opponent. She has spent a lifetime advocating for women and\nchildren and fighting for the middle class and there is not one GOP\ncandidate who has that record.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nBrock did not dispute the authenticity of the memo, which leaves a pair of\nquestions about the internal politics of the Clinton big-money effort\nunanswered. But he declined to comment on the memo, or whether it reflected\nhis fundraising approach or his presentation at the Democracy Alliance,\nwhich was closed to the press.\n\n\n\nThe three-day meeting of the Democracy Alliance \xe2\x80\x94 a group that includes\nmore than 100 individual and institutional donors and various unions \xe2\x80\x94 took\nplace at San Francisco\xe2\x80\x99s Four Seasons Hotel just as Clinton officially\nlaunched her campaign.\n\n\n\nWhile some of the group\xe2\x80\x99s major donors \xe2\x80\x94 including billionaires George\nSoros and Tom Steyer \xe2\x80\x94 have displayed varying levels of support for\nClinton, others have grumbled mostly privately that she doesn\xe2\x80\x99t reflect\ntheir worldviews. Many Democracy Alliance members supported then-Illinois\nSen. Barack Obama over Clinton in the 2008 Democratic presidential primary\nand urged Massachusetts Sen. Elizabeth Warren to run in 2016.\n\n\n\nThe group\xe2\x80\x99s importance to Democratic big-money efforts was underscored by\nthe attendance of Clinton campaign chairman John Podesta, who held a\nbriefing on the sidelines of the San Francisco meeting. Podesta founded the\nCenter for American Progress think tank, which has benefited from Democracy\nAlliance support, and he has close relationships with many club members. At\nleast one \xe2\x80\x93 CREDO Mobile co-founder Michael Kieschnick \xe2\x80\x93 told Podesta\nduring the side session that his campaign role made Kieschnick more\nsupportive of Clinton.\n\n\n\nAnother donor who attended, Utah-based investor Art Lipson, told POLITICO\nthat Podesta didn\xe2\x80\x99t overtly seek support for Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s campaign. \xe2\x80\x9cFirst of\nall, that would have gone over badly. And he is much too smart to say it\nand doesn\xe2\x80\x99t need to say it,\xe2\x80\x9d said Lipson, who has donated about $2.5\nmillion over the years to Democratic candidates and committees.\n\n\n\nLipson said he recently donated to a super PAC trying to draft Warren into\nthe Democratic presidential primary. In an assessment that could apply to\nmany Democracy Alliance members, he said \xe2\x80\x9cher message is exactly my\nmessage, so I am 100 percent behind her. But there is no chance she is\ngoing to run.\xe2\x80\x9d Lipson plans to attend a fundraiser this month in Salt Lake\nCity for Martin O\xe2\x80\x99Malley\xe2\x80\x99s Democratic presidential campaign and said the\nformer Maryland governor \xe2\x80\x9ccomes across as being highly intelligent.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nLipson said he\xe2\x80\x99s \xe2\x80\x9cfine with Hillary\xe2\x80\x9d given \xe2\x80\x9cthat it would take some sort of\na national disaster to have some other Democratic candidate\xe2\x80\x9d win the\nnomination. But he said that, while he\xe2\x80\x99ll vote for her over prospective\nRepublican rivals, he does not plan to donate to her campaign, let alone\nany supportive super PAC..\n\n\n\nBrock has sought to rally donors who might not otherwise give to Clinton by\nhighlighting expected attacks against her from the most reviled of liberal\nbogeymen \xe2\x80\x93 the billionaire industrialist mega-donors Charles and David Koch\nand their conservative political and policy network.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cThey have their sights on Sec. Clinton,\xe2\x80\x9d reads the memo prepared for Brock\nahead of the meeting.\n\n\n\nHe spoke on a panel called \xe2\x80\x9cThe Electoral Arms Race,\xe2\x80\x9d focused on the\nunprecedented $889-million spending spree planned by the Koch network in\nthe 2016 run-up, according to an agenda obtained by POLITICO.\n\n\n\nAt the meeting, sources say, Brock detailed a new initiative of his\nAmerican Bridge political outfit to highlight key 2016 states in which Koch\nIndustries, the brothers\xe2\x80\x99 multinational manufacturing conglomerate, could\nbe used against GOP candidates. The model for this project, the sources\nsaid, were the attacks that Democrat Gary Peters and his allies leveled\nagainst the Kochs and Republican Terri Lynn Land in his successful 2014\nMichigan Senate race.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cThis is a brand new project and we project it will cost around $3\nmillion,\xe2\x80\x9d reads Brock\xe2\x80\x99s memo. \xe2\x80\x9cWe think it is critical to start the project\nearly and we are looking for support to get staffed up very soon. We are\nhoping to get immediate support coming in at the $250,000 level.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nThe memo also includes responses to questions about how liberals could\njustify their criticism of the Koch groups for not disclosing their donors\nwhen some of Brock\xe2\x80\x99s groups \xe2\x80\x93 including Media Matters and American Bridge\n21st Century Foundation \xe2\x80\x93 also do not disclose the identities of their\ndonors.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cHow can we stand up here and expect to be taken seriously talking about\nwhat they are doing when we are doing the same thing?\xe2\x80\x9d reads one question.\nIn the suggested answer, Brock expresses disapproval for the proliferation\nof so-called \xe2\x80\x9cdark money,\xe2\x80\x9d which Clinton herself has criticized, but adds,\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe will play by the existing rules in this election because we cannot\nunilaterally disarm \xe2\x80\x93 too much of what we care about is at stake.\xe2\x80\x9d And he\nasserts: \xe2\x80\x9cThere is a major difference here \xe2\x80\x93 the Kochs are flooding the\npolitical system with money for pure self interest and self gain,\xe2\x80\x9d alleging\nKoch-backed groups back policies and candidates committed to \xe2\x80\x9cslash(ing)\ngovernment regulations so they can pollute with abandon and increase their\nbottom line. People in this room are not motivated by personal gain, and\noften work against their own self-interest.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nThe Kochs\xe2\x80\x99 allies reject this argument on its face, contending that their\nactivism is motivated by a belief that society as a whole stands to benefit\nfrom small-government policies that allow the free market to thrive.\n\n\n\nTold of the characterization in the memo, James Davis, a spokesman for the\nKoch network umbrella group Freedom Partners, said its members are focused\non \xe2\x80\x9cadvancing a future with more economic opportunities for every American.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nDavis accused the Kochs\xe2\x80\x99 liberal critics of \xe2\x80\x9claunching personal attacks and\ntaking away those freedoms.\xe2\x80\x9d And, alluding to support by Democrats\nincluding Clinton for reauthorizing the Export-Import Bank, which Freedom\nPartners opposes, Davis said \xe2\x80\x9cmany of them are rigging the system to fatten\ntheir wallets with taxpayer-funded corporate welfare. This is the culture\nof corruption in Washington that we\xe2\x80\x99re fighting against.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\n*Hillary Clinton Returning to L.A. for June 19 Fundraising Swing\n<http://variety.com/2015/biz/news/hillary-clinton-visiting-l-a-june-19-fundraiser-1201509648/>\n// Variety // Ted Johnson \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nHillary Clinton is returning to Los Angeles on June 19 for a fundraising\nswing that includes an event at the home of HBO\xe2\x80\x99s Michael Lombardo and\nhusband Sonny Ward, sources said.\n\n\n\nThe event will be a day after President Obama treks to L.A. for a\nfundraiser at the home of Tyler Perry. She held three fundraisers on May 7 in Los Angeles before returning\nto the Bay Area on Friday, May 8 for a luncheon at the Portola Valley home\nof eBay President and CEO John Donahoe and Eileen Donahoe, global affairs\ndirector for Human Rights Watch and former U.S. ambassador to the U.N.\nHuman Rights Council.\n\n\n\nClinton declared her candidacy April 12 and has been busily visiting\nearly-primary states since, but her campaign announced Monday that she\xe2\x80\x99ll\ngive her \xe2\x80\x9cofficial campaign launch speech\xe2\x80\x9d on Saturday, June 13 at the\nFranklin D. Roosevelt Four Freedoms Park on New York City\xe2\x80\x99s Roosevelt\nIsland. The event is open to the public, and members of the public can\nregister for tickets online. She has yet to hold any public campaign events\nin California.\n\n\n\n*Marco Rubio And Rand Paul Pose Greatest Threat To Hillary Clinton\n<http://thefederalist.com/2015/06/01/marco-rubio-and-rand-paul-pose-greatest-threat-to-hillary-clinton/>\n// The Federalist // Emily Ekins \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nA recent CNN/ORC poll finds 75 percent of Republican partisans prefer that\ntheir party nominate a \xe2\x80\x9cpresidential candidate who can beat the Democratic\ncandidate,\xe2\x80\x9d while only 25 percent prefer a nominee who agrees with them on\nissues that matter most to them. This clashes with partisans\xe2\x80\x99 reported\npreferred candidates for the Republican nomination. Numerous polls find\ndisproportionate support among partisans for former Florida Gov. Jeb Bush\nand Wisconsin Gov. Scott Walker; however, U.S. senators Rand Paul and Marco\nRubio perform better in general election matchups against likely Democratic\ncandidate Hillary Clinton.\n\n\n\nDespite this, 2016 election coverage has tended to pay more attention to\nBush and Walker over Rubio and Paul. In fact, a May Fox News poll even\nexcluded Paul from its general-election matchups with Hillary Clinton.\n\n\n\nOne reason less attention is being paid to these candidates is that only a\nquarter of Republican voters believe either Rubio or Paul have the \xe2\x80\x9cbest\nchance of beating the Democratic nominee in the general election,\xe2\x80\x9d\naccording to another recent CNN/ORC poll. But the matchup data say\ndifferently.\n\n\n\nTo be sure, Clinton enjoys a sizable lead against all Republican\ncontenders. That being said, Quinnipiac\xe2\x80\x99s latest poll shows that in a\nhypothetical general-election matchup, Paul and Rubio come the closest to\nbeating Clinton. Paul would garner 42 percent of the vote to Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s 46\npercent and Rubio would capture 41 percent to Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s 45 percent.\n\n\n\nHigher Heights, Lower Lows for Paul and Rubio\n\n\n\nThis poll is not an anomaly. In fact, an analysis of major polls conducted\nin 2015 shows that Paul has fared best against Clinton from January-March\nof this year, with Rubio pulling ahead in April. Quinnipiac found that Paul\nand Rubio are the only widely known candidates whose favorables are not\n\xe2\x80\x9cunder water.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nIf Republicans care about nominating a candidate who can beat the\nDemocratic nominee in 2016, they might want to pay more attention to Rubio\nand Paul.\n\n\n\nWhy might Paul and Rubio lead other Republicans in match-ups with Hillary\nClinton? There are a number of possible explanations. One likely\nexplanation is that Paul and Rubio beat Clinton on empathy.\n\n\n\nPerception of candidate empathy matters. Readers may recall going into the\n2012 presidential election that Mitt Romney and Barack Obama were tied on\nseveral candidate qualities, including being honest and trustworthy and\nbeing strong leaders. But Obama trounced Romney on \xe2\x80\x9ccares about the needs\nand problems of people like you\xe2\x80\x9d 60 to 48 percent. In fact, a slim majority\n(51 percent) of Americans thought Romney did not care about the needs of\npeople like themselves.\n\n\n\nHow could anyone honestly expect to win if a majority of the people doesn\xe2\x80\x99t\nthink he or she cares about them?\n\n\n\nHillary Clinton is not Barack Obama. The Quinnipiac Poll finds that only 48\npercent of Americans think Hillary cares about the needs and problems of\npeople like themselves and 47 percent think she does not care about them.\n\n\n\nRepublicans Who Care\n\n\n\nBut Paul and Rubio are the only GOP contenders who Americans are more\nlikely to believe \xe2\x80\x9ccares about the needs and problems of people like\n[them]\xe2\x80\x9d than don\xe2\x80\x99t. In this, Paul has a +6 point advantage and Rubio has a\n+3 point advantage. In fact, Paul and Rubio are the only Republican\ncandidates in the poll who Americans believe care about their needs. For\ninstance, Jeb Bush has a -7 point deficit, Walker has a -5 point deficit,\nand Donald Trump has a -53 point deficit on empathy.\n\n\n\nWhy might Americans think Paul and Rubio care about people like them?\nPerhaps because they have taken stands on issues most Republicans avoid.\nFor instance, Paul has actively sought reform of the criminal-justice\nsystem and is an outspoken critic of police misconduct and the justice\nsystem\xe2\x80\x99s disparate impact on African-American and Hispanic communities.\nFurther, Paul has twice filibustered (or quasi-filibustered) over drone\nassassinations of citizens in the United States and renewal of the Patriot\nAct.\n\n\n\nRepublicans have lost the popular vote in five of the six presidential\nelections since 1992. However, candidates like Rubio and Paul who expand\ntheir scope of issue ownership beyond conventional Republican issues may be\nexpanding their base of support. It\xe2\x80\x99s worth noting that what Rubio and\nPaul\xe2\x80\x99s unique stances share in common is expanding freedom and choice, and\nthis may be attractive to new GOP voters.\n\n\n\nPickups Among Independent Voters\n\n\n\nIndependent voters seem to largely drive these results. Paul (+5) and Rubio\n(+1) are the only Republicans who lead Clinton among independent voters.\nInstead, Walker trails Clinton by 2 points, New Jersey Gov. Chris Christie\nby 3 points, Bush by 5 points, former Arkansas Gov. Mike Huckabee by 7\npoints, Sen. Ted Cruz by 8 points, and Trump by 15 points.\n\n\n\nWho are these voters that would not vote for any other Republican candidate\nbesides Paul or Rubio in a matchup with Clinton? Unfortunately, little raw\ndata are publicly available, besides a December 2014 CNN/ORC poll available\nvia the Roper Center that included Paul, but not Rubio. Furthermore, sample\nsizes are small so data should be interpreted with caution.\n\n\n\nHowever, data from this survey suggest that national-security issues, such\nas the U.S. government\xe2\x80\x99s use of torture, may attract new voters into the\nPaul camp. Indeed, civil liberties are precisely the issues on which Paul\nhas distinguished himself from the Republican pack. More publicly available\ndata are needed to investigate Rubio\xe2\x80\x99s voters.\n\n\n\nExamining respondents from a Gallup March 2015 survey who are not favorable\nof Republican presidential candidates besides Paul or Rubio provides\nfurther insight into these non-traditionally Republican voters. Paul seems\nto attract younger, white, male liberals who are non-religious, and Rubio\nseems to attract middle-age, Hispanic moderates, and particularly women.\n(Once again, sample sizes are small, so data should be interpreted with\ncaution.)\n\n\n\nRight-Wing, or Leftist?\n\n\n\nSome might find it ironic that Rubio and Paul, who were catapulted to high\nelected office via what many call the \xe2\x80\x9cfar right-wing\xe2\x80\x9d Tea Party movement,\nare also the very candidates posing the most formidable challenge to the\npotential Democratic nominee. In fact, Dana Milbank from the Washington\nPost even argued that Paul had taken a \xe2\x80\x9cleft turn,\xe2\x80\x9d and that his positions\nwould work well if he were challenging Hillary for the Democratic\nnomination. How can one come from the \xe2\x80\x9cfar right\xe2\x80\x9d and compete for the\nDemocratic nomination at the same time?\n\n\n\nWhile many Republican lawmakers are known by their stances on gay marriage,\ntaxes, and spending, these issues are simply not a high priority for many\noutside of the GOP base. Instead, many Americans are more worried about\nbeing unnecessarily (and unjustly) hassled by the police than by the\nInternal Revenue Service. Many fear being profiled by law enforcement,\nworry their grandmother may be deported, and wonder if they will eventually\nbe accepted by their communities.\n\n\n\nAmericans gravitate to politics of inclusivity, of empathy. This is not the\nsame as handing out \xe2\x80\x9cgifts,\xe2\x80\x9d as Romney suggested. Americans do not need to\nbe bought\xe2\x80\x94they want to be asked for their vote (well in advance of Election\nDay).\n\n\n\n*Dan Pfeiffer: Hillary Is \xe2\x80\x98Going To Have To Engage The Press\xe2\x80\x99\n<http://dailycaller.com/2015/06/01/dan-pfeiffer-hillary-is-going-to-have-to-engage-the-press-video/>\n// Daily Caller // Al Weaver \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nOn his first day as a CNN contributor, former Obama adviser Dan Pfeiffer\nargued that Hillary Clinton is \xe2\x80\x9cgoing to have to engage the press\xe2\x80\x9d if she\nwants to have a success in her presidential campaign.\n\n\n\nAppearing on \xe2\x80\x9cThe Lead\xe2\x80\x9d with host Jake Tapper, Pfeiffer said that her\ndealings with the press will be \xe2\x80\x9ccritical to her success\xe2\x80\x9d as the campaign\ndrags on.\n\n\n\nJAKE TAPPER: Let\xe2\x80\x99s talk about Hillary Clinton who is obviously way favored\non the Democratic side of the aisle. So you have to find the balance. As the\ncampaign goes on I think they\xe2\x80\x99ll be able to do that.\n\n\n\n*20 things for Hillary Clinton to worry about\n<http://www.washingtonpost.com/blogs/right-turn/wp/2015/06/01/20-things-for-hillary-clinton-to-worry-about/>\n// WaPo // Jennifer Rubin \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nFor a presidential candidate who is so \xe2\x80\x9cinevitable,\xe2\x80\x9d Hillary Clinton is in\nan odd position. You probably should\nnot base your vote in the upcoming election on this.\n\n\n\nLAST PLACE: Rand Paul, Ted Cruz, Ben Carson, Lindsey Graham, and Carly\nFiorina\n\n\n\nIf you don\xe2\x80\x99t put any effort into making your 404 page fun at all, you make\nlast place on our list. In the case of Ted Cruz\xe2\x80\x99s website, trying to access a page that\ndoesn\xe2\x80\x99t exist will simply spit you back out to the home page.\n\n\n\nThanks for not playing along, guys and gals!\n\n\n\n6. More demerits\nwere calculated in for the Republican since his site ostensibly lifted the\n\xe2\x80\x9cmean Hillary Clinton joke 404\xe2\x80\xb3 idea from his party\xe2\x80\x99s official website.\n(Also, the GOP\xe2\x80\x99s Hillary 404 is way funnier.)\n\n\n\n5. We can appreciate those\ntraits in and of themselves, but imagining the conversation Bernie had with\nsome web designer intern just before filming the vid, that\xe2\x80\x99s the part that\nmakes us smile the most.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat\xe2\x80\x99s that?! You want me to point at the bottom of the screen?!\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\n2. Mike Huckabee\n\n\n\nThe fishing Mike shown in Governor Huckabee\xe2\x80\x99s 404 page cleverly reinforces\nthe Republican\xe2\x80\x99s good ol\xe2\x80\x99 boy persona. The bonus points added for\nincorporating a dog bring him to second on our list. Simple and appealing.\nAnd a dog!\n\n\n\n1.       Hillary Clinton\n\n\n\nRight now, former Secretary of State Hillary Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s cute and punny 404\ngets our vote for number one. Hers, featuring a family picture at Disney\nwith Bill and Chelsea, was the first we came across this election cycle and\nnone of the other candidates have been able to dethrone the queen yet.\n\n\n\n*\n\n\n\nOf course, the party primaries leading up to the 2016 election are still a\nlong way away, and plenty of candidates have yet to officially launch their\ncampaign websites. (We hold high hopes for Donald Trump\xe2\x80\x99s 404, for\nexample.) So between now and then, we\xe2\x80\x99ll be updating our ranking as other\nhopefuls launch their respective Internet campaign home pages.\n\n\n\n*OTHER DEMOCRATS NATIONAL COVERAGE*\n\n\n\n*The race is on to become Hillary Clinton alternative\n<http://www.cnn.com/2015/06/02/politics/hillary-clinton-democratic-primary/>//\nCNN // Eric Bradner - June 2, 2015*\n\n\n\nWashington \xe2\x80\x93 The race to become the liberal alternative to Hillary Clinton\nis on.\n\n\n\nThanks to a new poll, which shows Clinton has some serious vulnerabilities\nwhen it comes to trustworthiness and likeability, contenders like Vermont\'s\nBernie Sanders and Maryland\'s Martin O\'Malley may have more room to make\ntheir case than previously thought.\n\n\n\nA more alarming sign for Clinton: Prospective Republican opponents have\nclosed on her in head-to-head matchups, with Kentucky Sen. Rand Paul,\nFlorida Sen. Marco Rubio and Wisconsin Gov. Scott Walker all now polling\nwithin the margin of error.\n\n\n\nClinton\'s favorability rating is now 46% -- down from 53% in March. And\njust 42% said they view Clinton as honest and trustworthy, compared to 50%\nin March, according to a new CNN/ORC poll.\n\n\n\nThe greatest threat to her chances of securing the Democratic nomination --\nthe potential for a Sen. Elizabeth Warren candidacy -- is apparently over.\nBut the polling shows she\'ll still have to come to play against the likes\nof liberal folk hero Sanders and the willing-to-throw-a-punch O\'Malley.\n\n\n\nClinton\'s share of Democrats\' support has slipped from 69% in April to 60%\nsix weeks later. Second, though, is Vice President Joe Biden, at 14%.\nSanders is at 10%, double his support from March, while O\'Malley still\nbarely registers at 1%.\n\n\n\nThe former Maryland governor officially launched his campaign over the\nweekend, and Sanders made news by attracting crowds of hundreds to events\non his first swing through Iowa.\n\n\n\n"That was an indication of the fact that Iowa voters definitely want to get\nengaged," said Tom Henderson, the Democratic chairman in Polk County,\nIowa\'s most populous county.\n\n\n\nThough there are apparent cracks in the armor, top Democratic hands say\nClinton is still on safe territory.\n\n\n\n"If either one of them were to win, it would be the greatest upset in the\nhistory of politics," said Dan Pfeiffer, a CNN political commentator and\nformer senior White House aide to President Barack Obama.\n\n\n\nAnd Clinton\'s campaign is making as clear as it can that the former\nsecretary of state is preparing for a real primary battle -- particularly\nin early-voting states like Iowa.\n\n\n\nOn June 13 -- the same day Clinton holds her first major speech and rally\nof the campaign in New York City -- she\'ll meet with key supporters and\nvolunteers in the Hawkeye State, and simulcast that meeting to similar ones\nin nearly all 435 congressional districts across the country.\n\n\n\nIn the 2008 campaign, Clinton was stunned by a third-place finish behind\nBarack Obama and Sen. John Edwards. It\'s a lesson that seems to have been\ntaken to heart for her 2012 campaign.\n\n\n\nTeam Clinton already employs 21 field organizers and six regional\norganizing directors in Iowa, and those organizers are working down to the\nprecinct level. The staff includes state director Matt Paul and deputy\nstate director Molly Schermann, who both worked for former Iowa governor\nand Agriculture Secretary Tom Vilsack, as well as political director Troy\nPrice, the former executive director of the Iowa Democratic Party.\n\n\n\nThat said, her advisers know Iowa has always been a game of expectations,\nand they are doing their best to temper them.\n\n\n\nClinton campaign spokesman Jesse Ferguson on Monday highlighted a number\nmany Clinton allies have cited: No Democrat who wasn\'t a sitting president,\nvice president or Iowa senator has ever topped 50% of the state\'s caucus\nvote.\n\n\n\nStill, Clinton is far from a typical candidate.\n\n\n\nHenderson, the Polk County Democratic chair, said it\'s unfair to compare\nlow-profile candidates like Sanders and O\'Malley with Clinton.\n\n\n\n"We keep comparing these candidates to Hillary Clinton, who may be the most\nfamous women in the world, and a lot of them are still emerging -- people\nare getting to know them," he said. "It\'s still early in the campaign."\n\n\n\nThe biggest danger to Clinton\'s candidacy is the emergence of a damaging\nnarrative -- that she acts like she\'s above reproach when it comes to\nquestions over her use of private email while heading the State Department\nor the controversial donations accepted by the Clinton Foundation. Or that\nshe\'s completely untrustworthy.\n\n\n\n*Martin O\xe2\x80\x99Malley\xe2\x80\x99s first challenge: Bernie Sanders\n<http://www.msnbc.com/msnbc/martin-omalley-first-challenge-bernie-sanders>\n// MSNBC // Alex Seitz-Wald \xe2\x80\x93 6/1/15*\n\n\n\nMartin O\xe2\x80\x99Malley was supposed to be the main liberal alternative to Hillary\nClinton. But when he announced his candidacy Saturday in Baltimore, he\nfound that spot already taken by someone else.\n\n\n\nVermont Sen. Bernie Sanders, who is now Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s top rival in early polls,\nbeat the former Maryland governor to a presidential announcement by exactly\na month, and to a outdoor kickoff rally by five days.\n\n\n\nBoth men served two terms as mayor in the largest city in their states.\nBoth were then elected statewide. And both returned to those cities this\nweek to announce their underdog presidential campaigns. But the scenes were\nvery different.\n\n\n\nO\xe2\x80\x99Malley had several hundred, perhaps a thousand, supporters to cheer him\non Saturday at a park overlooking Baltimore\xe2\x80\x99s skyline. There were also\nabout a dozen protesters, who heckled O\xe2\x80\x99Malley over his policing policies\nas mayor.\n\n\n\nSanders, on the other hand, drew more than 5,000 supporters in Burlington,\na city of 40,000. A sea of fans overflowed the lakefront park Sanders\nhelped build as mayor, and packed in behind portapotties and platforms,\nwhere they had no hope of a view.\n\n\n\nAnd it was just the kickoffs. Both candidates this week visited Iowa where\nSanders drew 700 in Davenport for the biggest rally any candidate of either\nparty has seen in the state this election season, according to the New York\nTimes. In a tiny town of Kensett, population 240, Sanders drew 300.\n\n\n\nO\xe2\x80\x99Malley visited Davenport three days later and spoke to 50 supporters. He\nmet another 200 in Des Moines later that night, according to the Des Moines\nRegister.\n\n\n\nMeanwhile, Sanders headed to Minneapolis, Minnesota, where he fired up an\noverflow crowd of more than 3,000 in a basketball gym, according to the\nMinneapolis Star Tribune. Hundreds more listed from outside, unable to get\nin.\n\n\n\nOn the Internet, 84,000 Facebook users generated 120,000 interactions about\nO\xe2\x80\x99Malley in the 24 hours after his launch, according to the social\nnetworking company. In the same period after Sanders\xe2\x80\x99 announcement,\nFacebook record 10 times the interactions \xe2\x80\x93 1.2 million \xe2\x80\x93 from 592,000\ndifferent users. (Hillary Clinton blew both of them out of the water with\n10.1 million interactions from almost 5 million users.)\n\n\n\nCraig Varoga, who served as O\xe2\x80\x99Malley\xe2\x80\x99s chief strategist on his 2010\nreelection campaign, but is not involved with the candidate today, said\nO\xe2\x80\x99Malley needs to find a way to deal with Sanders soon.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cHis first real challenge is dealing with Bernie Sanders\xe2\x80\x99 campaign, rather\nthan directly going after Hillary Clinton,\xe2\x80\x9d said Varoga.\n\n\n\nOnly perhaps 30-40% of Democrats are currently not supporting Clinton. If\nO\xe2\x80\x99Malley and Sanders split that bloc, neither will be seen as credible,\nVaroga said.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cThey have to find a way to talk about Sanders without talking about him.\nThe worst thing is for one longshot to get in a fight with another\nlongshot,\xe2\x80\x9d Varoga said.\n\n\n\nO\xe2\x80\x99Malley\xe2\x80\x99s camp, however, insists they\xe2\x80\x99re not concerned about Sanders \xe2\x80\x93 in\nfact they welcome his success.\n\n\n\nAs they see it, O\xe2\x80\x99Malley\xe2\x80\x99s more immediate challenge is breaking through the\npsychological barrier of Hillary Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s inevitability. No candidate will\nbe taken seriously until the idea that Clinton can lose is taken seriously.\nSo the more any progressive alternative to Clinton rises in the polls, the\nbetter for everyone running to her left.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI think it\xe2\x80\x99s an encouragement to my candidacy,\xe2\x80\x9d O\xe2\x80\x99Malley said of Sanders\non ABC\xe2\x80\x99s \xe2\x80\x9cThis Week\xe2\x80\x9d Sunday. Why should progressive support O\xe2\x80\x99Malley over\nSanders? \xe2\x80\x9cBecause I have a track record of actually getting things done,\nnot just talking about things,\xe2\x80\x9d O\xe2\x80\x99Malley added.\n\n\n\nThe former governor\xe2\x80\x99s allies view Sanders as essentially a protest\ncandidate, while O\xe2\x80\x99Malley is presidential. If they can convince voters\nthere\xe2\x80\x99s a chance for an alternative to actually win against Clinton, they\nthink Sanders\xe2\x80\x99 supporters will flock to the more electable O\xe2\x80\x99Malley.\n\n\n\nTeam O\xe2\x80\x99Malley looks to the 2012 Republican presidential primary, in which\nnearly every candidate had a moment in the sun, and sees Sanders\xe2\x80\x99 fling\nwith Democratic primary voters as fleeting.\n\n\n\nAnd O\xe2\x80\x99Malley\xe2\x80\x99s allies are pointing to another historical parallel as well.\n\xe2\x80\x9cBernie Sanders is in some ways like Sen. McCarthy was in 1968,\xe2\x80\x9d said\nformer Maryland governor Parris Glendening, who is supporting O\xe2\x80\x99Malley.\n\n\n\nThe 1968 Democratic primary featured a thought-to-be-inevitable frontrunner\nin Lyndon Johnson, the incumbent president. None of the party\xe2\x80\x99s top\nprospects dared challenge Johnson. But the Vietnam War created an opening\nfor an anti-war progressive, exploited by underfunded longshot candidate\nSen. Eugene McCarthy.\n\n\n\nAfter McCarthy came shockingly close to winning the New Hampshire primary,\nRobert F. Kennedy sensed Johnson\xe2\x80\x99s weakness and jumped into the race. That\nprompted the once-inevitable president to throw in the towel on his\nreelection bid entirely and quit. Kennedy won a string of contests, but\ntragically did not make it to the Democratic Convention when he was\nassassinated after winning the California primary in June.\n\n\n\nIn O\xe2\x80\x99Malleyland\xe2\x80\x99s eyes, Sanders is McCarthy and O\xe2\x80\x99Malley is Kennedy, the\nyoung, handsome Catholic pol.\n\n\n\nWhile they agree on most issues, Sanders is an anti-politician at a time\nwhen politicians are liked, while O\xe2\x80\x99Malley looks like a central casting\ncandidate. And without a critical issue like the Vietnam War where the\ncandidates differ, it\xe2\x80\x99s unclear if O\xe2\x80\x99Malley can draw a clear contrast with\nhis rivals and distinguish himself.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cO\xe2\x80\x99Malley\xe2\x80\x99s advantage is that he\xe2\x80\x99s not just out there on these issues, but\nhe\xe2\x80\x99s been very effective on these issues,\xe2\x80\x9d Glendening said, pointing to\nO\xe2\x80\x99Malley\xe2\x80\x99s track record in Maryland. \xe2\x80\x9cHis other big advantage is\norganization,\xe2\x80\x9d Glendening added, pointing to the former governor\xe2\x80\x99s years as\na political organizer and operative before he sought elected office himself.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cSanders\xe2\x80\x99 support is just a representation of the explosiveness of these\nissues,\xe2\x80\x9d he added.\n\n\n\nIndeed, even many of Sanders supporters don\xe2\x80\x99t necessarily see him as\npresidential. And a danger for the self-proclaimed democratic socialist was\non display this weekend, when he had to answer questions about a\ncontroversial 1972 essay, in which he wrote that women fantasize about\nbeing raped. Sanders called it \xe2\x80\x9cstupid\xe2\x80\x9d and said he was imitating the voice\nof the male chauvinist he was criticizing.\n\n\n\nFor the meantime, though, both candidates will be focused squarely on\nClinton, not each other.\n\n\n\n*Martin O\xe2\x80\x99Malley misses his chance: How Hillary Clinton closed off his\nbiggest 2016 opening\n<http://www.salon.com/2015/06/01/martin_omalley_misses_his_chance_how_hillary_clinton_closed_off_his_biggest_2016_opening/>\n// Salon // Simon Maloy \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nAfter months and months of hemming, hawing, and dithering, Martin O\xe2\x80\x99Malley\nis finally an official candidate for the presidency. He\xe2\x80\x99s entered the race\nwith literally nowhere to go but up \xe2\x80\x93 his RealClearPolitics national\npolling average is, as of this writing, a clinically dead 0.8 percent. That\nputs him at the very bottom of the Democratic primary barrel. He\xe2\x80\x99s being\nbadly outpolled by Elizabeth Warren and Joe Biden, neither of whom have\ntaken any steps towards 2016 bids, and he\xe2\x80\x99s even behind bored vanity\ncandidates Lincoln Chafee and Jim Webb. It\xe2\x80\x99s a weird position for an\naccomplished two-term governor of a reliably blue state to find himself in.\n\n\n\nSo what hope does O\xe2\x80\x99Malley have of snatching the nomination away from\nrunaway favorite Hillary Clinton? At the moment, not much, but he\xe2\x80\x99s at\nleast going to try and make things interesting. Both O\xe2\x80\x99Malley and Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s\ncurrent chief rival, Bernie Sanders, have indicated that they\xe2\x80\x99re going to\ncome at Hillary from the left and appeal to the slice of the Democratic\nbase that is maybe a little uneasy over her perceived centrist tendencies.\nUnfortunately for O\xe2\x80\x99Malley, Clinton has already moved to cut him off at the\nknees on one issue he clearly hopes to challenger her on: immigration.\n\n\n\nRemember last summer\xe2\x80\x99s border crisis? Thousands and thousands of\nundocumented immigrant children were pouring over the southern border,\nstraining the resources of immigration agencies and causing a major\npolitical controversy. The crisis had the weird effect of dividing\nDemocrats on immigration, an issue that typically unites the party in the\nface of Republican fractiousness. At the time, the White House moved to\naccelerate deportation proceedings for the undocumented minors to send a\nmessage to Central American countries that there was no benefit in making\nthe dangerous journey through Mexico.\n\n\n\nO\xe2\x80\x99Malley, who was still governor of Maryland, very publicly broke with\nPresident Obama and condemned the White House for pursuing a cruel and\nimmoral policy. \xe2\x80\x9cIt is contrary to everything we stand for as a people to\ntry to summarily send children back to death,\xe2\x80\x9d he said, \xe2\x80\x9cin a place where\ndrug gangs are the greatest threat to stability, rule of law and democratic\ninstitutions in this hemisphere.\xe2\x80\x9d It was smart politics for O\xe2\x80\x99Malley, as he\nsimultaneously galvanized liberals on a contentious issue, put daylight\nbetween himself and a president whose popularity wasn\xe2\x80\x99t so hot at the time,\nand directly challenged Hillary Clinton, who had said the undocumented\nminors \xe2\x80\x9cshould be sent back as soon as it can be determined who responsible\nadults in their families are.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nPicking a fight with Clinton on immigration made sense. She\xe2\x80\x99d stumbled\nbadly on the issue in 2007 when she refused to directly answer whether or\nnot she\xe2\x80\x99d back driver\xe2\x80\x99s licenses for undocumented immigrants. That\nexperience, combined with her support for Obama\xe2\x80\x99s policy towards the border\ncrisis, seemed to indicate that there\xe2\x80\x99d be at least some space to attack\nher from the left on the issue. As for O\xe2\x80\x99Malley\xe2\x80\x99s own record, he could\npoint to legislation he signed allowing undocumented immigrants access to\ndriver\xe2\x80\x99s licenses and his support for a state-level version of the DREAM\nAct.\n\n\n\n\n\nBut O\xe2\x80\x99Malley waited too long, and while he sat on the sidelines, Clinton\nseized the initiative. Last month she laid out her own vision for\nimmigration reform that preserves and expands upon the policies Obama has\nput in place through executive action. She spoke to the urgency liberals\nand Latino voters feel about passing immigration reform, and aggressively\nchallenged the Republican presidential candidates, attacking them for not\n\xe2\x80\x9cclearly and consistently supporting a path to citizenship.\xe2\x80\x9d At the very\nleast, O\xe2\x80\x99Malley could have used the issue to be perceived as the person who\nwas forcing Hillary to the left. Instead, she went there on her own.\n\n\n\nO\xe2\x80\x99Malley still has a strong record on immigration issues, and he\xe2\x80\x99s hired\nObama\xe2\x80\x99s former director of Hispanic media to help craft policy and conduct\noutreach. And all indications are that he\xe2\x80\x99s still going to make an issue of\nHillary\xe2\x80\x99s response to the border crisis as part of a broader critique of\nher immigration stance. He\xe2\x80\x99s absolutely right to do that, but Hillary\xe2\x80\x99s\nalready making moves to align herself more closely with the portion of the\nelectorate that he\xe2\x80\x99ll be targeting. There wasn\xe2\x80\x99t a whole lot of room on\nHillary\xe2\x80\x99s left to begin with, and if this keeps up, O\xe2\x80\x99Malley could soon\nfind himself with nowhere left to go.\n\n\n\n*O\xe2\x80\x99Malley\xe2\x80\x99s Bad Timing\n<http://www.washingtonmonthly.com/political-animal-a/2015_06/omalleys_bad_timing055835.php>\n// Washington Monthly // Ed Kilgore \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nWhen I was first in the vicinity of Martin O\xe2\x80\x99Malley, right after he was\nfirst elected mayor of Baltimore (in 1999), the prevailing question wasn\xe2\x80\x99t\nif but when he\xe2\x80\x99d run for president. In the New Democrat circles I ran in\nback then, he was a pretty hot property, interested in policy innovations\non a wide range of issues that transcended his current position on the\npolitical career ladder. Even then, there was a sort of ambivalent feeling\nabout him: he had a bit of the Bobby Kennedy aura about him\xe2\x80\x94a prized\nquality for Democrats regardless of their ideological tendencies\xe2\x80\x94but there\nwere also questions about his depth and vision. And then there was the\npersonal image: the wonky Irish rocker whom a lot of women found very\nattractive (I don\xe2\x80\x99t get the sense this last credential has survived the\nintervening decade-and-a-half, though I could be wrong).\n\n\n\nSo now after two ostensibly successful terms as mayor and then as Governor,\nthe appointed time for the O\xe2\x80\x99Malley presidential run has arrived, and you\nget the sense his timing is just completely off. His earlier time served in\nHillary Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s orbit makes him an unlikely and very long-shot challenger\nto her nomination. His sudden emergence as a would-be \xe2\x80\x9ctrue progressive\xe2\x80\x9d\nchampion is singularly undermined by the prior presence in the presidential\nfield of Bernie Sanders, who has a few decades on O\xe2\x80\x99Malley in rousing\ncrowds with attacks on Wall Street and centrist \xe2\x80\x9csell-outs.\xe2\x80\x9d And he\xe2\x80\x99s\ndefinitely been wrong-footed by recent events in Baltimore, where fairly or\nunfairly the suspicion has been sowed that his supposedly wonky policing\nstrategies fed a old-school habit of harassing young black men for who they\nwere, and created a poisonous atmosphere that is now boiling over in\nviolence and mistrust of government. It doesn\xe2\x80\x99t help O\xe2\x80\x99Malley that his\nchief accuser on this front is television writer and producer David Simon,\nwhose depiction of Baltimore in the HBO series The Wire probably represents\n99% of what political and journalistic elites in the rest of the country\nknow about that city.\n\n\n\nAdd in the disillusionment with O\xe2\x80\x99Malley among Democrats in his home state\nafter his tax policies helped sink his designated successor in 2014,\nAnthony Brown, and you have a guy who at the age of 52 should probably\nthink about deferring his presidential ambitions until 2020 or 2024. For\nall I know, of course, this campaign is mostly strategic, aimed at\npositioning O\xe2\x80\x99Malley to become HRC\xe2\x80\x99s running-mate or a lively prospect for\nthe future. But right now he\xe2\x80\x99s in a position where if he doesn\xe2\x80\x99t get some\nattention by going after both Sanders and Clinton, his candidacy could sink\nlike a stone.\n\n\n\nAt FiveThirtyEight Harry Enten put up a rather deadly post about O\xe2\x80\x99Malley\nover the weekend that suggested the lack of support for his candidacy in\nMaryland made him a really unusual presidential aspirant compared to, well,\njust about everybody else past or present. He\xe2\x80\x99ll have a brief window of\ninterest in his candidacy before it closes for the cycle (barring some\ncalamity hitting Clinton). If he can reverse all the indicators pointing\ndownward in that time, then the promise a lot of people saw in him back in\nthe day can yet be redeemed.\n\n\n\n*O\'Malley on changing his mind about Clinton: \'Times change\'\n<http://www.politico.com/story/2015/06/martin-omalley-hillary-clinton-no-support-2016-118479.html>\n// Politico // Nick Gass \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nMartin O\xe2\x80\x99Malley supported Hillary Clinton in 2008 and 2012, but \xe2\x80\x9ctimes\nchange,\xe2\x80\x9d the Democratic presidential candidate and former governor of\nMaryland said Monday in an interview with ABC News\xe2\x80\x99 George Stephanopoulos.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI believe that the presidency is a sacred trust,\xe2\x80\x9d O\xe2\x80\x99Malley said, echoing\nremarks from his weekend campaign announcement in which he railed against\nWall Street\xe2\x80\x99s preference for Clinton and former Florida Gov. Jeb Bush.\n\n\n\nThe Democratic Party has not \xe2\x80\x9cdelivered\xe2\x80\x9d on its promise to \xe2\x80\x9cmake the\nAmerican dream real again for more families,\xe2\x80\x9d O\xe2\x80\x99Malley said in the\ninterview aired on \xe2\x80\x9cGood Morning America.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nOn Sunday, former top White House adviser David Axelrod tweeted that\nO\xe2\x80\x99Malley\xe2\x80\x99s support of Clinton in 2008 might make it \xe2\x80\x9ca bit awkward\xe2\x80\x9d to slam\npolitical \xe2\x80\x9croyal families\xe2\x80\x9d during his campaign. O\xe2\x80\x99Malley responded, saying\nthat while people don\xe2\x80\x99t change, the times do, noting that his support of\nClinton preceded the financial collapse.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cWell I was for Secretary Clinton in 2008. She and I both worked hard to\nelect the president and to re-elect the president. But times change, and\ndifferent challenges require new leadership,\xe2\x80\x9d he said, noting that he keeps\nhearing from people that new leadership is necessary.\n\n\n\nHe also fired back at a Wall Street Journal editorial published Sunday that\nwent after his gubernatorial record.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cMr. O\xe2\x80\x99Malley may attract some Democrats as an alternative to Clintonian\ninevitability and cynicism, but he has little chance at the nomination\nunless Mrs. Clinton unexpectedly washes out, and then other Democrats would\njoin the race. Republicans would be only too happy to run against the\nMaryland progressive model,\xe2\x80\x9d the editorial said.\n\n\n\nO\xe2\x80\x99Malley touted his leadership of the state, mentioning the state\xe2\x80\x99s\nTriple-A bond rating, the best public schools in America, the highest\nmedian income of any state, and a better rate of job creation than\nneighboring states.\n\n\n\n*O\'Malley, stumping in N.H., sells himself as alternative to Clinton\n<http://www.baltimoresun.com/news/maryland/martin-omalley/bs-md-omalley-new-hampshire-20150531-story.html>\n//\nBaltimore Sun // John Fritze \xe2\x80\x93 May 31, 2015*\n\n\n\nAttempting to push back on the idea that his presidential campaign is a\nnearly insurmountable long shot, Martin O\'Malley arrived in New Hampshire\non Sunday to sell himself as a fresh voice and progressive alternative to\nfront-runner Hillary Clinton.\n\n\n\nVisiting the key presidential primary state a day after announcing his\nlong-expected candidacy in Baltimore, the former two-term Maryland governor\nused phrases like "new leadership" and "trying different things" almost\nimmediately upon hitting the ground here \xe2\x80\x94 and it was a theme he repeatedly\nreturned to throughout the day.\n\n\n\nAs he spoke with voters at a diner, addressed a small house party and\ndelivered pizza to Dartmouth College students on the eve of their finals,\nO\'Malley engaged in exactly the kind of retail politicking analysts say he\nneeds to perfect in order to climb out of the single-digits in polls.\n\n\n\n"I\'ve always been drawn to the toughest of fights," O\'Malley told a group\ngathered in Gilford, N.H., recounting his first run for mayor in 1999.\n\n\n\n"The people I\'ve met in New Hampshire refuse to be intimidated by big\nmoney, pundits, or the concentration of power [and] insisted on meeting\nevery candidate, looking them in the eye, asking them questions and making\nup their own mind," he said.\n\n\n\nO\'Malley is far less well known than either Clinton or Vermont Sen. Bernie\nSanders, the self-described democratic socialist who has carved out space\non Clinton\'s left since announcing his own campaign in April. Perhaps\nbecause of that, O\'Malley made himself perpetually available as he traveled\nthe state \xe2\x80\x94 to voters, to elected officials and to reporters.\n\n\n\nThe informal, less scripted interactions stood in contrast to the view of\nO\'Malley many have seen in national television appearances and the\nsometimes stilted speeches he has delivered during his career.\n\n\n\nAfter eating a few spoonfuls of a cup of Milky Way ice cream, O\'Malley\nworked a small crowd gathered inside the Goldenrod Drive-In Restaurant in\nManchester. He walked from table to table, fielding questions on college\naffordability, the economy and the country\'s nuclear posture.\n\n\n\nHis message appeared to resonate with several people in the room.\n\n\n\n"I don\'t think Hillary\'s a lock," said Peter Morin, a 55-year-old\nManchester resident after speaking briefly with O\'Malley. "I don\'t like to\nsee anyone anointed."\n\n\n\nBut whether O\'Malley\'s focus on his past executive leadership or his\nincreasingly strong admonishments of Wall Street will be enough to build\nmomentum for his campaign is an open question. More than 60 percent of\nDemocrats in New Hampshire identified Clinton as their first choice in a\nBloomberg Politics/Saint Anselm poll in early May.\n\n\n\nO\'Malley was the first choice for 3 percent.\n\n\n\nThe former governor spoke with several dozen Democrats gathered at the home\nof Jerry Slagle, a Maryland native who worked with O\'Malley on Gary Hart\'s\n1984 presidential campaign. He stuck mainly to lines from his announcement\nspeech, but also took questions from attendees.\n\n\n\nAs he spoke from atop a piano bench \xe2\x80\x94- so he could be heard in the back of\nthe room \xe2\x80\x94 O\'Malley did not mention Clinton or Sanders directly. But he\naddressed both of his declared rivals with subtle political code.\n\n\n\nTo draw a distinction with Clinton \xe2\x80\x94 a former secretary of state, senator\nand first lady \xe2\x80\x94 O\'Malley repeatedly described himself as a next-generation\nleader and argued that elections should not be coronations for political\nroyalty. To distance himself from Sanders, he notes he hasn\'t "just talked\nabout" liberal ideals, but has achieved them.\n\n\n\nO\'Malley announced his presidential campaign in Federal Hill Park on\nSaturday, entering a race many believe he has been considering for years.\nDuring his address, O\'Malley cast the election in broad economic terms,\nsuggesting middle class families have not benefited from the recovery as\nmuch as they should have.\n\n\n\nHe reiterated that point in an interview on ABC\'s "This Week" on Sunday,\nwhile also suggesting he is no friend of Wall Street.\n\n\n\n"I don\'t know what Secretary Clinton\'s approach to Wall Street might be.\nShe will run her own campaign and I will run mine," O\'Malley said. "I can\ntell you this. I am not beholden to Wall Street interests. There are no\nWall Street CEOs banging down my door and trying to participate or help my\ncampaign."\n\n\n\nAnother presidential candidate with Maryland ties, former Johns Hopkins\nneurosurgeon Ben Carson, also spoke on the program. The Republican was\nasked about a national poll that showed him tied for first place for his\nparty\'s nomination with former Florida Gov. Jeb Bush, former Arkansas Gov.\nMike Huckabee, Sen. Marco Rubio of Florida and Wisconsin Gov. Scott Walker.\n\n\n\n"Whether I\'m a front-runner or not doesn\'t matter," Carson said. "What\nmatters is that the people themselves are starting to listen and evaluate\nfor themselves rather than listening to what people say I said and what\npeople say that I meant."\n\n\n\n\n\nO\'Malley will spend significant time in early primary states such as Iowa,\nNew Hampshire and South Carolina. That\'s partly because the Iowa caucuses\ndramatically shifted the course of the race for the Democratic nomination\nin 2008, when then-Sen. Barack Obama upset Clinton there by running as a\nchange candidate.\n\n\n\nThe trip Sunday was O\'Malley\'s fourth to New Hampshire this year.\n\n\n\nPatrick Gosselin, a Hooksett, N.H., resident, wondered whether O\'Malley\ncouldn\'t do the same next year. Gosselin spoke with the former governor at\nthe diner for several minutes before revealing that he had come to hear him\nspeak despite never before voting for a Democrat.\n\n\n\n"I\'m tired of the old politics, tired of the Democrats and Republicans\ngetting entrenched with their old ideas," Gosselin said as O\'Malley walked\naway. "It just seems like he has the right personality to challenge the\nstatus quo, to challenge Hillary."\n\n\n\n*Martin O\xe2\x80\x99Malley is targeting Latino voters\n<http://www.washingtonpost.com/blogs/post-politics/wp/2015/06/01/martin-omalley-is-targeting-latino-voters/?wprss=rss_politics>\n// WaPo // Arelis H. Hern\xc3\xa1ndez \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nFormer Maryland governor Martin O\xe2\x80\x99Malley is making a special effort to\ntarget Latino voters during the first week of his presidential campaign,\nappearing on the Spanish-language television channel Univision, offering\ninterviews on immigration policy to major news outlets and speaking to the\nHispanic Chamber of Commerce.\n\n\n\n"I believe Latino Americans, like all Americans, want the American Dream to\nbe truthful and real,\xe2\x80\x9d O\xe2\x80\x99Malley (D) told The Washington Post on Monday. \xe2\x80\x9cI\nbelieve my record speaks to my heart.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nImmigration is among the issues where O\xe2\x80\x99Malley has sought to draw\ndistinctions between himself and Hillary Rodham Clinton, the overwhelming\nfront-runner in the Democratic primary race. While he was governor,\nMaryland passed its version of the Dream Act, which extended in-state\ntuition benefits to undocumented immigrants at public universities and\ncolleges provided their families meet certain conditions. The state also\nadopted a two-tiered system that allows undocumented immigrants to get\nlimited driver\'s licenses that can\'t be used for other purposes, such as\nboarding an airplane.\n\n\n\nDuring the battle over the state\'s adoption of the Dream Act, \xe2\x80\x9cwe met every\nweek with O\xe2\x80\x99Malley,\xe2\x80\x9d said Gustavo Torres, executive director of the\nadvocacy group CASA of Maryland.\n\n\n\nIn April, after Clinton announced her support for providing immigrants with\nlimited driver\'s licenses, O\'Malley said he was \xe2\x80\x9cglad she\xe2\x80\x99s come around to\nthat position now, too.\xe2\x80\x9d He declined on Monday to name specific differences\nbetween himself and other Democratic presidential candidates, saying only\nthat \xe2\x80\x9cthe distinctions will be made clear.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nO\xe2\x80\x99Malley said that as president he would \xe2\x80\x9cforge a new consensus\xe2\x80\x9d and\nrevisit the criteria used by law enforcement to lock-up and deport\nimmigrants \xe2\x80\x94 a sticking point for immigrant advocacy groups who have\ncriticized the Obama administration\xe2\x80\x99s record number of deportations.\n\n\n\nIn a brief interview with Maria Elena Salinas -- the well-known anchor on\nUnivision, the nation\xe2\x80\x99s largest Spanish-language news network -- O\'Malley\nsaid he doesn\'t think any candidate can win the White House "without the\nLatino vote." Asked what he would want to say to Spanish-speaking voters,\nO\xe2\x80\x99Malley replied: \xe2\x80\x9cPor favor,\xe2\x80\x9d or please. The rest of the interview with\nSalinas will air on Univision on Sunday.\n\n\n\nOn Wednesday, O\xe2\x80\x99Malley is scheduled to participate in a question-and-answer\nsession with Hispanic Chamber of Commerce president Javier Palomarez at the\nNewseum in Washington. The event is the latest in a series of forums with\npresidential candidates hosted by the organization, which says it\nrepresents 3.2 million Hispanic business owners.\n\n\n\nO\xe2\x80\x99Malley recently hired Gabriela Domenzain, director of Hispanic media for\nObama\xe2\x80\x99s 2012 campaign, as his director of public engagement. His campaign\nlaunch on Saturday included remarks from Jonathan Jayes-Green, who worked\non the governor\xe2\x80\x99s Hispanic affairs commission and is the son of\nundocumented immigrants.\n\n\n\nJayes-Green said his family came to the United States from Panama in 2005\nand, after receiving erroneous legal advice, overstayed their visas and\nbecame undocumented. O\xe2\x80\x99Malley, he added, \xe2\x80\x9cunderstands we are Americans, we\njust don\xe2\x80\x99t have documentation yet."\n\n\n\nLast summer, O\'Malley clashed with the White House last summer over what to\ndo with migrant children streaming over the border from Central America,\naccusing the Obama administration \xe2\x80\x94 in which Clinton had served \xe2\x80\x94 of being\ntoo eager to return the children.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhen refugee children arrive on our doorstep, fleeing starvation and death\ngangs, we don\xe2\x80\x99t turn them away," O\xe2\x80\x99Malley said in South Carolina in April.\n"We act like the generous, compassionate people we have always been.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nAt his launch on Saturday, he said \xe2\x80\x9cthe enduring symbol of our nation is\nnot a barbed wire fence, it is the Statue of Liberty.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nWhen he talks about immigration, O\'Malley recalls his own family history of\ncoming to this country from Ireland. Martin O\'Malley, who announced Saturday that he will\nofficially seek the Democratic Party\'s nomination for president, continued\ntrying to separate himself from frontrunner Hillary Clinton, telling ABC\nNews Chief Anchor George Stephanopoulos during an exclusive interview\nMonday morning that the "times have changed" and pointing to the 2008 crash\non Wall Street as evidence for the country needing a new generation of\nleadership.\n\n\n\nOn the campaign trail, O\'Malley has attacked Clinton for what he says is a\nclose relationship to Wall Street.\n\n\n\nO\'Malley told Stephanopoulos that the "people of the United States, not\nWall Street," should to decide the next president, and leaders on Wall\nStreet allegedly seeming OK with a Clinton or a Bush in the White House\nshould be "wake-up call for all of us."\n\n\n\nIn 2008, O\'Malley supported Clinton\'s first run for president, a fact that\nformer Obama adviser and campaign strategist David Axelrod noted this week\non Twitter, saying, "O\'Malley is a dynamic, accomplished guy. But he was\nall in for HRC [Hillary Rodham Clinton] in \'08, so isn\'t it a bit awkward\nto rail against \'royal families\' now."\n\n\n\nO\'Malley responded by saying the country faces "different challenges now."\nHe told Stephanopoulos the most notable difference between then and now was\nthe 2008 economic crash, adding that since then the country had failed to\nreign in the "excess of Wall Street."\n\n\n\n"I believe we need new leadership," he said. "We need to get things done\nagain."\n\n\n\nHe said that he called Clinton this week and said he told her he was\nlooking forward to "a robust conversation about the issues that face our\ncountry."\n\n\n\nO\'Malley emphasized his experience as an executive, having served two terms\nas mayor of Baltimore and two terms as governor of Maryland. He added that the U.S. Chamber of\nCommerce, which "hardly ever says nice things about Democratic elected\nofficials anywhere," named Maryland No. 1 in innovation and\nentrepreneurship three years in a row.\n\n\n\nFor fans of his other talents -- singing and playing guitar -- O\'Malley\nsaid stay tuned.\n\n\n\n"When I go through Iowa and New Hampshire, guitars seem to fall out of the\nrafters," he joked, saying that supporters can expect to see him strumming\nagain soon.\n\n\n\n*Martin O\'Malley\'s Hometown Challenge\n<http://abcnews.go.com/Politics/martin-omalleys-hometown-challenge/story?id=31426720>\n// ABC News // Maryalice Parks \xe2\x80\x93 May 31, 2015*\n\n\n\nMartin O\'Malley faces an uphill battle. The former Maryland governor and\nBaltimore mayor who officially announced his run for the Democratic\npresidential nomination Saturday is relatively unknown nationwide, polling\naround 1 percent among Democratic voters across the country, according to a\nnew poll from Quinnipiac University this week. But perhaps his greatest\nchallenge comes from his own backyard.\n\n\n\nDuring his campaign kickoff event Saturday in downtown Baltimore, a small\ngroup of protesters made a scene, speaking out against police brutality and\nblaming O\'Malley for what they see as the negative consequences of his\ntough stance on crime.\n\n\n\n"If he wants to be president, if he wants to come home, he must atone,"\nsaid Tawanda Jones, one of the protesters. "Our streets are not even safe\nno more, because of all of the anger in our city."\n\n\n\nGov. Martin O\xe2\x80\x99Malley Announces Run for President\n\nO\xe2\x80\x99Malley Cites Executive Experience in Comparison to Obama\n\nWhen he first ran for mayor of Baltimore in 1999, O\'Malley promised to cut\ncrime, and when he came into office he instituted a zero-tolerance policing\npolicy. Supporters say that while arrests went up, even for minor offenses,\ncrime came down.\n\n\n\nBut critics say his methods harmed the relationship between the city\'s\nresidents and law enforcement.\n\n\n\nIn an exclusive interview with ABC News\' Chief Anchor George\nStephanopoulos, O\'Malley defended his reputation. "I would not have been\nelected with 91 percent of the vote first time, or re-elected four years\nlater with 88 percent of the vote, if we were not making substantial\nprogress," he said.\n\n\n\n"When I was elected in 1999, our city had become the most violent, and\naddicted, and abandoned city in America. It was a huge challenge. But we\nwent on in the next ten years to achieve the biggest reduction of part one\n[or serious] crime of any city in America," he continued. "For all of the\nprogress that we make, there\'s always so much more that needs to be done."\n\n\n\nLast month the violent protests in Baltimore after the death of an\nAfrican-American man at the hands of police reignited criticism of\nO\'Malley\'s policies. And in a front page article in the Baltimore Sun the\nday of O\'Malley\'s campaign kickoff event, a former head of the city\'s NAACP\nchapter hit the former mayor hard, saying, "He\'s going around now like\n[Baltimore] is his claim to fame. We can do better as a country.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nPrior to leaving office as governor in October, O\'Malley\'s approval ratings\nin Maryland were at an eight-year low (41 percent, according to a\nWashington Post poll), though his presidential announcement rally was full\nof energetic elected officials and supporters from across the state.\n\n\n\nOne fan, Baltimore City Councilwoman Rikki Spector, brought a rock with the\nword "Believe" etched in it as a gift for the governor.\n\n\n\nDespite all the controversy she said this was their \xe2\x80\x93 Baltimore\'s \xe2\x80\x93\npresidential race.\n\n\n\n*Martin O\xe2\x80\x99Malley, mild-mannered man: Why the media are yawning\n<http://www.foxnews.com/politics/2015/06/01/martin-omalley-mild-mannered-man-why-media-are-yawning/>\n// Fox News // Howard Kurtz \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nOn paper, Martin O\xe2\x80\x99Malley should be a serious contender for the Democratic\npresidential nomination.\n\n\n\nBut on paper, the Washington Nationals should have won last year\xe2\x80\x99s World\nSeries.
