Martin O\'Malley of Maryland."\n\n\n\nSanders also generated other lively turnouts in the state on his first\nvisit to Iowa since declaring his candidacy. In Ames, he drew a crowd that\nspilled out of a brewery, and held an event in Kensett where the size of\nthe crowd exceeded the population of the town itself, according to the New\nYork Times.\n\n\n\nThe spike in attention is reflected in recent polling. According to a new\nBloomberg Politics/Des Moines Register poll of Iowa voters, Sanders has\nmore than tripled his support among likely Democratic caucus-goers than he\nwas in January, with 16% of likely caucus-goers saying Sanders is their\nfirst choice.\n\n\n\nAs you can see in the chart below, courtesy of Bloomberg Politics, Clinton\nis dominant among likely Democratic caucus-goers in Iowa \xe2\x80\x94 she\'s the first\nchoice for 57% (one percentage point more than in January). Sanders ranks\nsecond at 16% \xe2\x80\x94 still far from Clinton, but notable for the leap from 5% in\nJanuary. Vice President Joe Biden, who has not made any overt signals that\nhe\'s considering a bid for the White House, came in next at 8%. Former\nMaryland Gov. Martin O\'Malley was the first choice for 2%, as was former\nVirginia Sen. Jim Webb.\n\n\n\nThe Iowa caucuses, which are scheduled to be held in February, are the\nfirst contest of the presidential race, and mark a critical juncture for\ndetermining momentum in the early stages of the nomination race. Given that\nthe voting is several months away, the specific numbers right now aren\'t as\nimportant as their changes.\n\n\n\nSanders\' big bump in recent months reflects a hunger among the Democratic\nelectorate for a candidate who can serve as an alternative to the Clinton\ndynasty. The self-avowed democratic socialist doesn\'t have a history in the\nnational spotlight, but he is the king of Reddit, and he has quickly taken\nthe anti-establishment mantle from Sen. Elizabeth Warren of Massachusetts,\nwho shows no signs of interest in running for president.\n\n\n\nSanders still has his work cut out for him. While Clinton\'s campaign\nalready has 30 paid staffers devoted to mobilizing caucus-goers in Iowa,\nSanders only has two, according to the New York Times. If Sanders is to\nevolve into a formidable player, his organizing apparatus will have to\nmatch the size of his ambitions.\n\n\n\nToward that end, Sanders has called for additional early presidential\ndebates this year, which would include both Democrats and Republicans. The\ndebates would provide him with a major (and free) opportunity to make his\ncase to the public in direct contrast to Clinton, and facilitate his\nability to shed the label of outsider nipping at the heels of an inevitable\nheir to the throne. According to the Huffington Post, any such debates\nmight be in violation of debate rules for Democratic candidates. Clinton is\nunlikely to benefit from such an arrangement, and her strategy so far has\nlargely been to ignore Sanders\' criticism. But as she knows all too well\nfrom 2008, she can never take her lead for granted.\n\n\n\n*Bernie Sanders pleads for more debates\n<http://www.politico.com/blogs/media/2015/06/bernie-sanders-pleads-for-more-debates-208036.html>\n// Politico // Dylan Byers \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nDemocratic presidential hopeful Bernie Sanders has sent a letter to the\nDemocratic National Committee requesting more primary debates, including\ninter-party debates among candidates from both parties.\n\n\n\nIn a letter to DNC Chairwoman Debbie Wasserman Schultz, the Vermont\nsocialist argued that the candidates "should engage in a series of debates\nbeginning this summer," in order to increase voter turnout. Inter-party\ndebates could also be used to convince registered Republican voters that\nthey would be better off voting for a Democrat, Sanders said.\n\n\n\n"I am extremely concerned by the fact that many working-class Americans are\nvoting against their best economic interests by supporting right-wing\nRepublicans whose agenda represents the interests of the billionaire class,\nand not the needs of working Americans," Sanders wrote. "I believe that\nthese inter-party debates would put in dramatic focus the shallow and at\ntimes ridiculous policies and proposals being advocated by the Republican\ncandidates and by their party\xe2\x80\x99s platform."\n\n\n\nFor Sanders, a relatively little-known candidate with limited resources,\nmore debates would mean more free air time and publicity. Sanders is\ncurrently polling 54.8 points behind Hillary Clinton in the latest\nRealClearPolitics aggregate.\n\n\n\nIn an email to the On Media blog, DNC spokesperson Holly Shulman\neffectively put the kibosh on Sanders\' request: "We\xe2\x80\x99re thrilled to see the\nSenator is eager to participate in our debates," she wrote. "We\xe2\x80\x99ve already\nreleased our primary debate framework, and we believe that six debates will\ngive plenty of opportunity for the candidates to be seen side-by-side.\nWe\xe2\x80\x99ll have more details in the coming weeks, and we look forward to Senator\nSanders and other candidates participating. I\xe2\x80\x99m sure there will be plenty\nof other forums for the candidates to make their case to voters, and that\nthey will make the most out of every opportunity."\n\n\n\nThe DNC has sanctioned six primary debates for the 2016 cycle, which are\nscheduled to begin this fall. Host states will include the early caucus and\nprimary states of Iowa, New Hampshire, Nevada and South Carolina, though\nthe committee has yet to announce which national broadcast media and local\nmedia outlets will sponsor and moderate these debates.\n\n\n\nBoth the Hillary Clinton and Martin O\'Malley campaigns have confirmed that\ntheir candidates will participate in all six of the debates.\n\n\n\nIn his plea for more debates, Sanders argued that low voter turnout "has\nhurt progressive candidates all across our nation" and that "a larger\nnumber of debates beginning in the weeks ahead would encourage such voter\nparticipation."\n\n\n\nSanders also said inter-party debates between Democrats and Republicans\nwould "serve to engage large numbers of voters who typically do not pay\nattention to the process until much later when the general election begins\nto come into focus. By engaging these voters early and raising the stakes\naround the election I believe we can get people to participate at higher\nlevels which will undoubtedly benefit Democrats up and down the ticket."\n\n\n\n*GOP*\n\n\n\n*Lindsey Graham on the Issues\n<http://www.nytimes.com/2015/06/02/us/politics/lindsey-graham-republican-presidential-candidate-on-the-issues.html?rref=politics&module=Ribbon&version=context&region=Header&action=click&contentCollection=Politics&pgtype=article>\n// NYT // Gerry Mullany- June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nSenator Lindsey Graham of South Carolina announced Monday that he plans to\nseek the Republican nomination for president. In his three terms, he has\nfocused on military and foreign affairs and developed a reputation for\nworking together with Senate Democrats. Here are some of Mr. Graham\xe2\x80\x99s\nstands on important issues.\n\n\n\nForeign Policy\n\n\n\nMr. Graham has been skeptical of President Obama\xe2\x80\x99s efforts to reach a deal\nwith Iran over its nuclear program, saying Congress should reject any\nagreement that does not include inspections of Iran\xe2\x80\x99s military facilities.\nHe sees the group calling itself the Islamic State as a threat to the\nmainland United States, saying \xe2\x80\x9cthe likelihood of an attack against our\nnation is growing by the day\xe2\x80\x9d and calling it a \xe2\x80\x9cfantasy\xe2\x80\x9d to think that it\ncan be defeated without American ground forces. Describing Israel as the\n\xe2\x80\x9cbest friend\xe2\x80\x9d of the United States, Mr. Graham has vowed that if the United\nNations takes actions against Israel\xe2\x80\x99s interest he will use his powers in\nCongress to cut Washington\xe2\x80\x99s financial support of the organization. He has\nsaid the United States should provide lethal weaponry to the Ukrainian\nmilitary to battle Russian-backed separatists, a step the Obama\nadministration has resisted.\n\n\n\nEnvironment\n\n\n\nUnlike other Republican presidential contenders, Mr. Graham believes that\nclimate change is a problem and that it is caused by human activity. But he\nis concerned about using federal laws to curb greenhouse-gas emissions,\nsaying he wants to make an issue of whether \xe2\x80\x9cyou have to destroy the\neconomy to solve the problem\xe2\x80\x9d of global warming.\n\n\n\nSame-Sex Marriage\n\n\n\nHe has supported a constitutional amendment defining marriage as between a\nman and a woman. Mr. Graham has spoken out against the possibility that the\nSupreme Court could strike down same-sex marriage bans, saying: \xe2\x80\x9cWhat\xe2\x80\x99s the\nlegal difference between a ban on same-sex marriage being unconstitutional\nbut a ban on polygamy being constitutional?\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nImmigration\n\n\n\nMr. Graham differs from many of his fellow Republican contenders in that he\nis a strong proponent of making it possible for immigrants who are in the\ncountry illegally to become citizens. \xe2\x80\x9cIf I were president of the United\nStates, I would veto any bill that did not have a pathway to citizenship,\xe2\x80\x9d\nhe told USA Today, adding: \xe2\x80\x9cYou would have a long, hard path to\ncitizenship.\xe2\x80\x9d He says Republicans have been losing Hispanic support because\nof hostility toward immigrants.\n\n\n\nEconomy and Budget Issues\n\n\n\nMr. Graham supported giving Mr. Obama \xe2\x80\x9cfast track\xe2\x80\x9d authority to negotiate\nthe Trans-Pacific Partnership trade deal. He opposed the president\xe2\x80\x99s $789\nbillion stimulus package in 2009. He believes the federal government\xe2\x80\x99s debt\nlimit should be increased only when that is accompanied by spending cuts,\nbut he has not ruled out tax increases, as many other Republicans have.\n\n\n\n*Lindsey Graham, in announcing White House run, gets personal\n<http://www.politico.com/story/2015/06/lindsey-graham-2016-presidential-election-announcing-bid-118489.html#ixzz3bpsFTrnZ>\n// Politico // Katie Glueck \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nCENTRAL, S.C. \xe2\x80\x94 He\xe2\x80\x99s spent a third of his life in Congress and is a fixture\non the Sunday morning news-show circuit, making nearly 70 appearances in\nthe past five years.\n\n\n\nBut as he announced his presidential bid Monday here in the tiny town where\nhe grew up, Lindsey Graham sought to knock down the idea that he\xe2\x80\x99s a\ncreature of Washington and instead told a personal story that\xe2\x80\x99s largely\nbeen overlooked over the course of his two decades in the House and Senate.\n\n\n\nIt\xe2\x80\x99s the tale of a son of pool-hall owners, who grew up near-impoverished\nin the back room of his parents\xe2\x80\x99 bar. As a college student, he raised, and\neventually adopted, his little sister after their parents died, before\ngoing on to have a career as an Air Force lawyer and then rising to become\nSouth Carolina\xe2\x80\x99s senior senator.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cThose of you who\xe2\x80\x99ve known me a long time know I had some ups and downs as\na young man,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cI lost my parents, and had to struggle financially\nand emotionally \xe2\x80\xa6 There are a lot of so-called \xe2\x80\x98self-made\xe2\x80\x99 people in this\nworld. I\xe2\x80\x99m not one of them. My family, friends, neighbors and my faith\npicked me up when I was down, believed in me when I had doubts. You made me\nthe man I am today.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nGraham\xe2\x80\x99s sister, Darline Graham Nordone, spoke proudly of her brother and\nlate parents during a brief interview Sunday night before Graham\xe2\x80\x99s\nwalk-through.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cOur parents were small-business owners here in the town of Central,\xe2\x80\x9d she\nsaid. \xe2\x80\x9cAs any other small-business owners, they understood the long hard\nhours that go into running a small business, and just the strong work ethic\nthat we got from that and the values \xe2\x80\xa6 It\xe2\x80\x99s just amazing that we come from\nthis and went on to bigger and better things, but our roots are here.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nThe humble-origins narrative is a staple of presidential campaigning, but\nit\xe2\x80\x99s a fairly new device for Graham, who has only started to employ it in\nrecent years. It wasn\xe2\x80\x99t until his 2014 Senate race, when he squared off\nwith six primary challengers, that he slowly and sometimes reluctantly\nbegan to use that part of his biography in part to fight back against\ncriticism that he had been in Washington too long.\n\n\n\nNow, as a long-shot presidential candidate, Graham once again told that\nstory in this sleepy speck of a town located about 45 minutes from\nGreenville, where Main Street consists of a thrift shop, a hair salon, and\na restaurant or two \xe2\x80\x94 including the remnants of the Graham family\xe2\x80\x99s bar.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI think it\xe2\x80\x99s a good idea for people to realize, he\xe2\x80\x99s certainly a\nself-educated, self-made guy,\xe2\x80\x9d said Hank Scott, a major donor who is very\nclose to Graham. \xe2\x80\x9cHe worked hard to get where he is, he\xe2\x80\x99s not a person that\ngrew up with privilege, like, say, [Jeb] Bush.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nDavid Woodard, an operative and professor who managed Graham\xe2\x80\x99s first two\nHouse races in the 1990s, said he never heard Graham talk about his\nfamily\xe2\x80\x99s troubles, even when those issues were fresher for him.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cDid he talk about it? No, he never talked about it,\xe2\x80\x9d Woodard said, adding\nlater, \xe2\x80\x9cHe\xe2\x80\x99s kind of a self-made story, but he didn\xe2\x80\x99t talk about it.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nDuring his reelection last year, after some reluctance about getting too\npersonal, Graham allowed his team to run an ad featuring his sister,\nDarline, who grew emotional in the spot when she reflected on how Graham\nhelped raise her.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt was hard when we lost my mom and my dad,\xe2\x80\x9d she said in the ad. \xe2\x80\x9cLindsey\nassured me that he was going to take care of me, he was going to be there\nfor me. He never let me down. Never. I don\xe2\x80\x99t see how he did it, to take on\nthe responsibility of raising a little sister. That came from within for\nLindsey.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nGraham won that race just as he\xe2\x80\x99s won every congressional contest in which\nhe\xe2\x80\x99s run, starting in 1994, many of them with the help of South Carolina\xe2\x80\x99s\ntop political talent. Yet as he begins his run for president, many of them\nare not on board. When he indicated he was serious about running for\npresident, many of the state\xe2\x80\x99s most well-respected operatives were caught\noff guard \xe2\x80\x94and had already agreed to help other candidates.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99ve been involved in all of his Senate campaigns, and it was tough, but\nmy ship has sailed,\xe2\x80\x9d said J. Warren Tompkins, a veteran South Carolina\noperative who is committed to Florida Sen. Marco Rubio. \xe2\x80\x9cI had committed\nlong before I had any inkling he had any interest in running for president.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nIn some state political circles, even where Graham is popular, there\xe2\x80\x99s a\nsense of bewilderment about why he\xe2\x80\x99s running \xe2\x80\x94 and some donors and\noperatives say privately that they wish he\xe2\x80\x99d stick to the Senate. In a very\ncrowded Republican field, Graham barely registers in the national polls; he\nhas low name identification and his record on issues like immigration\nreform is still anathema to the grassroots conservative voters who are so\ncritical in early-voting states like Iowa.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99ll always be supporting Lindsey any and every way I can,\xe2\x80\x9d said Scott,\nthe donor, whose own divided loyalty is revealing \xe2\x80\x94 he says he\xe2\x80\x99s supporting\nboth his friend and Rubio. Noting how crowded the field is, \xe2\x80\x9cI tried to\nencourage him to play the Strom Thurmond role and stay in the Senate,\xe2\x80\x9d\nScott added.\n\n\n\nIn his announcement speech Monday, Graham highlighted his national security\ncredentials, another reminder that pushing a more assertive foreign policy\nis the core rationale for his run.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI want to be president to defeat the enemies trying to kill us, not just\npenalize them or criticize them or contain them, but defeat them,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.\n\n\n\nIt\xe2\x80\x99s unclear how well Graham is polling in South Carolina presidential\nsurveys \xe2\x80\x94an NBC News poll from February found him leading the pack but an\nApril poll from local Winthrop University reported that more than half of\nhis home state GOP voters would not considering voting for him for the\nnomination.\n\n\n\nHis South Carolina political colleagues aren\xe2\x80\x99t lined up behind him either:\nGOP Gov. Nikki Haley has said she won\xe2\x80\x99t be making any early endorsements\nand several of the state\xe2\x80\x99s House members appeared at a presidential launch\nevent for Rand Paul \xe2\x80\x94 Graham\xe2\x80\x99s nemesis on foreign policy matters \xe2\x80\x94 though\nthey stopped short of endorsing.\n\n\n\nGraham\xe2\x80\x99s supporters believe he will play a key role in pushing national\nsecurity issues to the forefront, and that the senator \xe2\x80\x94 who at Republican\ncattle calls so far this year has impressed with his sense of humor and\ncommand of foreign policy \xe2\x80\x94 will expand his base as more people get to know\nhim. He\xe2\x80\x99s a natural, folksy campaigner and his hawkish foreign policy\nmessage plays well with a Republican base that\xe2\x80\x99s grown increasingly anxious\nabout instability in the Middle East and the rise of ISIS.\n\n\n\nDespite the seemingly impossible path to the GOP nomination, Graham\xe2\x80\x99s\nallies insist he is seriously interested in pursuing a White House bid and\nwouldn\xe2\x80\x99t run if he didn\xe2\x80\x99t see a path to victory, even as speculation\nabounds in South Carolina about whether he\xe2\x80\x99s positioning for another job,\nlike secretary of defense, or to be a kingmaker during the\nfirst-in-the-South South Carolina primary.\n\n\n\nIn the meantime, a super PAC supporting Graham, Security is Strength, is\nalso gearing up and announced its staff over the weekend. It is largely\ndriven by former Graham campaign and Senate staffers, and also includes\nformer Minnesota Sen. Norm Coleman. Graham is a favorite of hawkish donors\n\xe2\x80\x94 mega-donor Sheldon Adelson co-hosted a fundraiser on Capitol Hill for him\nseveral months ago, and plenty of people aligned with other candidates\nshowed up and even served on the host committee.\n\n\n\nFor Graham, the uphill climb ahead was obvious on Sunday night: a handful\nof interested bystanders who appeared in Central before Graham\xe2\x80\x99s\nwalk-through said they supported him in his Senate bid \xe2\x80\x94 but none was ready\nto commit to him for president yet.\n\n\n\n*Graham Begins Foreign Policy-Focused Bid\n<http://www.bloomberg.com/politics/articles/2015-06-01/challenges-await-as-lindsey-graham-begins-foreign-policy-focused-bid>\n// Bloomberg // Mark Halperin \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nStyle: Played the self-effacing hometown boy, keeping up his colloquial\nstyle even when talking about fearsome international threats. Quite\nlow-energy for an announcement speech, although the typical Southern crowd\nwhooped, cheered, and applauded throughout, allowing Graham to piggyback on\ntheir liveliness. Kept unscripted asides to a minimum (for him).\n\n\n\nSubstance: Heavy rhetorical emphasis on signature issues such as fighting\nterror, building alliances around the world, and enacting entitlement\nreform, but not much specifics there or anywhere else.\n\n\n\nBest moment: Jazzed the audience by declaring he has more foreign policy\nexperience than everyone else in the race, including Hillary Clinton.\n\n\n\nWorst moment: Lapsed into reading his text for several minutes in the\nmiddle of his remarks, further sapping momentum.\n\n\n\nOverall: The national security candidate chose to make national security\nthe center of his announcement by starting with it, seeding it throughout,\nand ending with it. While he talked about working with Democrats, he didn\xe2\x80\x99t\nemphasize his past efforts on immigration reform and climate change, which\nhave put him out of step with the party base. Instead, he focused on his\nlong-time fidelity to the three-legged Reagan stool of national security,\nsocial issues, and the economy. The whole event felt more like a personal\nmoment for Graham than the launching of a national movement, and he did not\nsummon the determined air of someone who thinks he can actually win. Still,\nit was a well-written speech, and he can move on to life as an official\ncandidate, where fundraising and poll challenges await.\n\n\n\nStyle: B- Substance: B- Overall: B-\n\n\n\nNote: The overall grade is not an average of the style and substance\ngrades, but takes into account other aspects of the announcement, such as\nstaging and crowd reaction.  In addition, a candidate\xe2\x80\x99s overall grade\nreflects the degree to which the candidate\xe2\x80\x99s standing in the race is\nimproved by the event and performance.\n\n\n\n*Lindsey Graham has a plan to win the GOP nomination. If it works, it\xe2\x80\x99d be\na first.\n<http://www.washingtonpost.com/blogs/post-politics/wp/2015/06/01/lindsey-graham-has-a-plan-to-win-the-gop-nomination-if-it-works-itd-be-a-first/>\n// WaPo // Jose A. DelReal \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nSen. Lindsey Graham, R-S.C., gives a thumbs up after being re-elected,\nTuesday, Nov. 4, 2014, in Columbia, S.C. Graham beat Democratic state Sen.\nBrad Hutto of Orangeburg. (AP Photo/Rainier Ehrhardt)\n\nAs a native South Carolinian, GOP Sen. Lindsey Graham\xe2\x80\x99s candidacy could\nshake up that early-voting state\xe2\x80\x99s primary.\n\n\n\nBut that\'s not the same thing as shaking up the presidential race.\n\n\n\nGraham certainly carries an advantage in The Palmetto State, where his name\nrecognition is nearly universal after having serving the state as U.S.\nsenator for more than 12 years. And a February NBC News/Marist poll of\nSouth Carolina voters showed Graham leading the GOP pack with 17 percent\nsupport. Former Florida governor Jeb Bush (R) followed Graham with 15\npercent, while Wisconsin Gov. Scott Walker (R) placed third with 12\npercent.*\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cFor a guy like me, it\xe2\x80\x99s pretty simple,\xe2\x80\x9d Graham recently told Time\nMagazine. \xe2\x80\x9cI do well in Iowa and finish in the top tier in New Hampshire,\nI\xe2\x80\x99ll win South Carolina. By the end of South Carolina there are three or\nfour people left at the most.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nIn other words, the strategy is: 1) Don\'t tank in Iowa or New Hampshire. 2)\nCome in strong in the home state. 3) ???\n\n\n\nAs of now, Graham is barely registering in polls anywhere else, including\nstates he would need to compete in in the later stages of the Republican\nprimary process. But let\'s start with Step 1.\n\n\n\nA WMUR Granite State poll of likely New Hampshire voters has him far behind\nmost of his would-be rivals, carrying the support of just around 1 percent\nof primary voters. For context, former Florida governor Jeb Bush leads the\npack with 15 percent. Meanwhile, even longshot candidate Donald Trump has 5\npercent.**\n\n\n\nAnd in Iowa, Graham is the first-choice candidate for just 1 percent of\nlikely GOP voters, according to a May Des Moines Register poll.*** He\ncompletely fails to register in another poll by Quinnipiac.\n\n\n\nHistory doesn\'t seem to be on Graham\'s side either. Presidential candidates\nwho hail from early voting states have frequently failed to make a splash\nnationwide and have also occasionally been met with resistance from\nin-state allies who fear their state\'s primary could be rendered irrelevant\nby a home grown contender.\n\n\n\nPut another way: in the modern era, there has never been a presidential\nnominee who hailed from Iowa, New Hampshire, South Carolina, or Nevada.\n\n\n\nConsider former Iowa governor Tom Vilsack, who made a short-lived run for\nthe 2008 Democratic nomination but quickly dropped out of the race \xe2\x80\x93 ending\nhis campaign in February of 2007. Though Vilsack stood a strong chance of\nwinning the caucuses if he had stayed in the race, Hillary Clinton and\nBarack Obama\xe2\x80\x99s fundraising strength proved to be an intractable challenge\nnationwide. For what it\'s worth, The Iowa Democratic Party responded to\nVilsack\'s candidacy by promising to remain neutral for fear that Vilsack\xe2\x80\x99s\ncandidacy would discourage candidates from competing in the state.\n\n\n\nWhen former New Hampshire senator Bob Smith ran for the 2000 GOP nomination\n\xe2\x80\x93 also as a longshot \xe2\x80\x93 New Hampshire Republicans balked at the thought of\nthe Granite State losing its sacred status as a must-compete contest. He\ntoo dropped out before the primaries actually began.\n\n\n\nIowa\'s Tom Harkin, who retired from the Senate last year, ran for the\nDemocratic nomination in 1992 and swept the Iowa contest, receiving the\nsupport of nearly 80 percent of caucusgoers. But in New Hampshire the next\nweek, Harkin took just 10 percent of the vote.\n\n\n\nOf course, Graham\'s candidacy will largely rest on his clearly-defined,\nhawkish foreign policy positions in an election where foreign affairs have\nalready taken center stage. That could bode well for him, particularly as\nKentucky Sen. Rand Paul\'s strong critique of GOP hawks presents a\nheadline-grabbing foil for Graham to pit himself against.\n\n\n\n*The NBC News/Marist survey of 450 likely South Carolina GOP voters has a\nmargin of error of plus or minus 4.6 percentage points.\n\n\n\n**The WMUR survey of 293 likely GOP primary voters has a margin of error of\nplus or minus 5.7 percent.\n\n\n\n***That survey of 402 likely caucusgoers was conducted between May 25 to\nMay 29 and has a margin of error of plus or minus 4.9 percentage points.\n\n\n\nSouth Carolina Sen. Lindsey Graham is a Republican contender for the White\nHouse in 2016. Here\'s his take on Obamacare, guns and more, in his own\nwords. (Julie Percha/The Washington Post)\n\n\n\n*Lindsey Graham joins crowded 2016 presidential field\n<http://www.msnbc.com/msnbc/lindsey-graham-joins-crowded-2016-presidential-field>\n// MSNBC // Benjy Sarlin \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nCENTRAL, South Carolina \xe2\x80\x93 Warning that \xe2\x80\x9cthe world is exploding in terror\nand violence,\xe2\x80\x9d Sen. Lindsey Graham (R-S.C.) announced a long-shot\npresidential campaign in his small home town on Monday predicated on\naggressively confronting threats from the Islamic State and Iran abroad.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m pretty sure no one here, including me, ever expected to hear me say,\n\xe2\x80\x98I\xe2\x80\x99m Lindsey Graham, and I\xe2\x80\x99m running for president of the United States,\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d\nhe told a cheering crowd of dozens of flag-waving supporters gathered just\nsteps from the former pool hall on Main Street that he grew up in.\n\n\n\nIt\xe2\x80\x99s hard to talk about Graham\xe2\x80\x99s candidacy without mentioning his\nideological archrival, Sen. Rand Paul (R-Ky.), whose libertarian approach\nto civil liberties, dovish take on military conflict and deep skepticism of\nan active foreign policy runs directly counter to the South Carolina\nlawmaker\xe2\x80\x99s own stance.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI want to be president to defeat the enemies that are trying to kill us,\xe2\x80\x9d\nGraham said in his announcement.\n\n\n\nBoth candidates seem eager to play the mongoose to the other\xe2\x80\x99s snake as the\n2016 presidential campaign heats up. Their conflict reached its peak in\nrecent days after Paul successfully forced the temporary expiration of\nPATRIOT Act provisions that govern, among other things, the phone record\nspy program revealed by Edward Snowden. Graham favors a maximalist approach\nto counterterrorism.\n\n\n\nPaul frequently fires up supporters by quoting Graham\xe2\x80\x99s latest jingoisms on\nthe trail \xe2\x80\x93 this week he criticized Graham\xe2\x80\x99s boast that he would drone\nstrike an American citizen suspected of terrorism rather than \xe2\x80\x9ccall a\njudge.\xe2\x80\x9d During Paul\xe2\x80\x99s PATRIOT Act filibuster, Graham gave an eye roll\nworthy of the surliest teenager and a clip of it from a live C-Span\nbroadcast went viral. Paul went on to lambast the \xe2\x80\x9ceye roll caucus\xe2\x80\x9d in an\ne-mail to supporters last week and a pro-Paul super PAC responded with a\nweb ad going after Graham.\n\n\n\nGraham didn\xe2\x80\x99t mention Paul directly in his announcement Monday, but he\nalluded to conflicts with rival lawmakers back in Washington.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe\xe2\x80\x99ve made some dangerous mistakes in recent years,\xe2\x80\x9d Graham said. \xe2\x80\x9cThe\nObama administration and some of my colleagues in Congress have substituted\nwishful thinking for sound national security strategy.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nGraham boasted that he has \xe2\x80\x9cmore experience with our national security then\nany other candidate in this race \xe2\x80\x93 that includes you, Hillary.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nThe tension put USC senior Anna Chapman, 21, in an awkward spot. A devoted\nPaul supporter, she volunteered at the event as a favor to her fellow\nCollege Republicans.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m here to support Graham \xe2\x80\xa6 kind of,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. \xe2\x80\x9cHe is from South\nCarolina, it\xe2\x80\x99s cool that he\xe2\x80\x99s running. I\xe2\x80\x99m not going to bash him, but I\ndon\xe2\x80\x99t think he\xe2\x80\x99s going to win the nomination.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nForeign affairs may be Graham\xe2\x80\x99s calling card, but it\xe2\x80\x99s hardly all he\xe2\x80\x99s\nknown for. At times he has split from GOP conservatives to broker\nbipartisan deals, most notably as co-author of the immigration reform bill\nthat passed the Senate in 2013 but never came up for a vote in the House\namid intense conservative opposition. Graham\xe2\x80\x99s speech included a message\nfor fellow Democrats, whom he pledged to work with the to make progress on\nareas of agreement should he win the White House.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cOur differences are real and we\xe2\x80\x99ll debate them, but you\xe2\x80\x99re not my enemy,\nyou\xe2\x80\x99re my fellow countrymen,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.\n\n\n\nLanguage like this appealed to attendees like Jim Eshelman, an engineer in\nGreenville, who is interested in Graham but still not committed to backing\nhim.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI love his spirit of bipartisanship \xe2\x80\x93 the gridlock has been awful,\xe2\x80\x9d he\nsaid.\n\n\n\nGraham\xe2\x80\x99s advisers also see potential in showcasing his humble roots, which\n2016 candidates like Scott Walker and Marco Rubio have used to great effect\nin campaign speeches to connect with voters. The senator grew up in the\nback of a bar owned by his parents, who died within 15 months of each other\nwhile he was in his early 20s, leaving him to raise his younger sister\nhimself. Graham put himself through law school and took officer training in\nthe Air Force, where he ended up serving as a judge advocate.\n\n\n\nGraham, who was introduced by his sister, mentioned the Social Security\nbenefits he received after his parents\xe2\x80\x99 death in pledging to reform the\nprogram to sustain it in the long term.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cAs president I will gladly do what it takes to save the program that once\nsaved my family,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.\n\n\n\nA fixture on Sunday political talk shows, Graham is among the most\nprominent and frequently quoted lawmakers in the national media on a\nvariety of issues. Despite his high visibility, he\xe2\x80\x99s considered well short\nof the top tier in the presidential race, and polls show he may have a\ntough time qualifying for primary debates, which will choose participants\nbased on their support in national surveys.\n\n\n\nHe may have a bigger impact in South Carolina, however, a crucial early\nprimary state that helped galvanize conservative opposition to Mitt Romney\nin 2012 by going for Newt Gingrich and sealed John McCain\xe2\x80\x99s nomination in\n2008 against Mike Huckabee.\n\n\n\nMany of the supporters who gathered here on Monday knew Graham personally\nor mentioned his dedicated constituent work. He once threatened to shut\ndown the Senate to fast track a project deepening a major port. This\nattention to detail back home helped keep him safe from primary threats in\nhis easy 2014 re-election despite major tea party opposition.\n\n\n\nVendors at the rally sold \xe2\x80\x9cLindsey Graham: Native Son\xe2\x80\x9d buttons. If he takes\neven a sizable minority of votes, it\xe2\x80\x99s possible he could peel votes from\nother candidates in a way that affects the race. In 2008, for example,\nformer Tennessee Sen. Fred Thompson was widely credited with pushing McCain\npast the finish line by splitting southern conservative support with\nHuckabee.\n\n\n\n*The Lindsey Graham record: A lot like John McCain, who also ran for\npresident\n<https://www.yahoo.com/politics/the-lindsey-graham-record-a-lot-like-john-mccain-120369603781.html>\n// Yahoo News // Meredith Shiner \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nOn Monday, Republican Lindsey Graham of South Carolina will become the\nfifth sitting senator to formally announce a presidential bid, but his\nbiggest challenge to prove he\xe2\x80\x99s a viable candidate likely won\xe2\x80\x99t come\ndirectly from the crowded field of colleagues he\xe2\x80\x99s currently running\nagainst. It will be from the one senator who already has waged (and lost)\nmultiple bids for the White House: John McCain of Arizona.\n\n\n\nFor those who follow congressional politics, Graham and McCain have been\ninseparable \xe2\x80\x94 and practically indistinguishable \xe2\x80\x94 from each other for more\nthan a decade, since Graham arrived to the Senate in 2003. Graham is often\nspotted just feet from the Senate floor, barking into a flip phone to a\nstaffer about coordinating press strategy with McCain, meaning that\n\xe2\x80\x9cStatement by Senators John McCain and Lindsey Graham on [foreign policy\nissue X]\xe2\x80\x9d is a frequent refrain in reporters\xe2\x80\x99 mailboxes. A Graham bid now completes an unofficial fraternity\npledging ritual for the original group\xe2\x80\x99s triumvirate: a presidential run.\n\n\n\nWith a 2016 Graham campaign, four of the last five presidential elections\nhave featured an \xe2\x80\x9camigo\xe2\x80\x9d vying for a place at the top of the ticket\n(Lieberman, 2004; McCain, 2000, 2008). But there\xe2\x80\x99s no requirement for\nsuccess in this political hazing process. Only once has a major party\nselected an amigo as its nominee \xe2\x80\x94 McCain in 2008 \xe2\x80\x94 and America has never\nelected one as president.\n\n\n\n*Little Sister Lauds Lindsey Graham, the Bachelor, for Raising Her\n<http://www.nytimes.com/politics/first-draft/2015/06/01/little-sister-lauds-lindsey-graham-the-bachelor-for-raising-her/?module=BlogPost-Title&version=Blog%20Main&contentCollection=Politics&action=Click&pgtype=Blogs&region=Body>\n// NYT // Alan Rappeport \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nCENTRAL, S.C. \xe2\x80\x94 If elected, Senator Lindsey Graham would be the first\nbachelor to win the White House since Grover Cleveland. But that does not\nmean he will be on the campaign trail without any family members in tow.\n\n\n\nMr. Graham, 59, a Republican who is a hawk on foreign policy, featured his\nrelatives prominently at his announcement here on Monday \xe2\x80\x94 none more so\nthan his sister, Darline Graham Nordone, who introduced him. Ms. Nordone\ndid her best to show Mr. Graham\xe2\x80\x99s softer side by sharing stories of how he\ntaught her to ride a bicycle and recalling the pain of losing both their\nparents, one after the other, at young ages.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cLindsey was always my parent,\xe2\x80\x9d Ms. Nordone said in an interview in the bar\non Main Street that their family once owned. \xe2\x80\x9cThere was no doubt in my mind\nor anyone else\xe2\x80\x99s mind that Lindsey was my guardian.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nMr. Graham and his sister grew up in a small room behind the bar, which was\nthen known as the Sanitary Cafe. There\xe2\x80\x99s just only so much time in a\nday.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nMr. Graham later became his sister\xe2\x80\x99s legal guardian while he was in the Air\nForce, allowing her to qualify for his military benefits.\n\n\n\nMr. Graham\xe2\x80\x99s bachelorhood has been seized upon by his political opponents\nbefore, most recently last year, when a little-known conservative primary\nchallenger called him \xe2\x80\x9cambiguously gay.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nMs. Nordone said that such personal attacks were hard for her to take, but\nthat she tried to tune out criticism of her brother \xe2\x80\x94 while showing people\nthat Mr. Graham was much more than a politician.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cHe\xe2\x80\x99s kind of like a brother, a father and a mother rolled into one,\xe2\x80\x9d she\nsaid.\n\n\n\n*Paul: I was exaggerating on my terror attack claim\n<http://www.msnbc.com/msnbc/rand-paul-exaggerating-my-terror-attack-claim>\n// MSNBC //Aliyah Frumin and Anthony Terrell \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nSen. Rand Paul may have taken his stand against government surveillance a\nlittle too far in his presidential campaign.\n\n\n\nIn a campaign video released on Friday that includes explicit links to a\ncampaign donation page, Paul (R-Ky.) extensively uses footage from his\nlengthy speech on the Senate floor on May 20 against bulk data collection\nand surveillance in the PATRIOT Act. The Senate \xe2\x80\x9cstrictly\xe2\x80\x9d prohibits any\nuse of its proceedings for campaign activities.\n\n\n\nThe video, published under the \xe2\x80\x9cOfficial YouTube Channel of Rand Paul for\nPresident,\xe2\x80\x9d says it is paid for by \xe2\x80\x9cRand Paul for President\xe2\x80\x9d and includes a\nhyperlink to a secure donation page. According to the standing rules of the\nSenate, \xe2\x80\x9cThe use of any tape duplication of radio or television coverage of\nthe proceedings of the Senate for political campaign purposes is strictly\nprohibited.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nThe campaign video begins with a clip of Ronald Reagan, quoting him from a\n1964 speech on individual liberty saying that \xe2\x80\x9cthose who would trade our\nfreedom for security have embarked on this downward course.\xe2\x80\x9d The video then\npivots to Paul\xe2\x80\x99s 10-hour speech earlier this month against the PATRIOT Act,\nthree key provisions of which are set to expire on Sunday at midnight if\nPaul refuses to allow quick Senate votes.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cThere comes a time in the history of nations when fear and complacency\nallow power to accumulate and liberty and privacy to suffer. But that video clearly showed a Fox News chyron in it,\nputting it in a grey area ethically. The most recent video includes no such\nindication that it is from news footage.\n\n\n\nCampaign and Senate aides to Paul did not respond to a request for\ncomment.\n\n\n\n*Rand Paul\xe2\x80\x99s \xe2\x80\x9csugar daddy\xe2\x80\x9d problem: Billionaires don\xe2\x80\x99t love him \xe2\x80\x94 but that\ncould be a blessing in disguise\n<http://www.salon.com/2015/06/01/rand_pauls_sugar_daddy_problem_billionaires_dont_love_him_but_that_could_be_a_blessing_in_disguise/>\n// Salon // Jim Newell \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nCitizens United and subsequent court decisions loosening campaign finance\nrestrictions have made running for president easy-peasy: you can find one\nbillionaire to give you tens of millions of dollars and then you just do\nwhatever they tell you to do. It\xe2\x80\x99s a great country. There are billionaires\nall over the place nowadays looking to purchase politicians for themselves.\n\n\n\nAnd yet Rand Paul, who has a slender but not-nil chance of winning the\nRepublican presidential nomination can\xe2\x80\x99t find himself a single willing\nbillionaire into whose pockets he can dive deep. He\ncontended there was an obvious political reason for Paul\xe2\x80\x99s stance, pointing\nout how his colleague was tweeting supporters taking \xe2\x80\x9cselfies\xe2\x80\x9d of\nthemselves next to Paul speaking on TV.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI know what this is about \xe2\x80\x94 I think it\xe2\x80\x99s very clear \xe2\x80\x93 this is, to some\ndegree, a fundraising exercise,\xe2\x80\x9d McCain said Sunday. \xe2\x80\x9cHe obviously has a\nhigher priority for his fundraising and political ambitions than for the\nsecurity of the nation.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nThe stinging personal criticism of Paul showed just how unpopular the\nKentucky Republican\xe2\x80\x99s demands to kill the surveillance law is among party\nelders \xe2\x80\x94 and portended how this battle is likely to continue to hover over\nhis presidential campaign, for better or worse. It marked the first time in\nPaul\xe2\x80\x99s brief tenure in Washington where he\xe2\x80\x99s become the scourge of much of\nhis party \xe2\x80\x94 not unlike how the party establishment turned on Ted Cruz over\nhis role in the 2013 government shutdown.\n\n\n\nLike Cruz, Paul is clearly relishing it.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cTonight begins the process of ending bulk collection,\xe2\x80\x9d Paul said proudly\non the Senate floor, just hours before the expiration of key provisions in\nthe law. And in a sign of the ill will between him and his colleagues, Paul\ntook a personal whack of his own.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cPeople here in town think I\xe2\x80\x99m making a huge mistake,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cSome of\nthem, I think, secretly want there to be an attack on the United States so\nthey can blame it on me.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nSince becoming a senator, Paul has long railed against the PATRIOT Act,\narguing it\xe2\x80\x99s a blatant violation of Americans\xe2\x80\x99 constitutional privacy\nrights. His position gained steam among many civil libertarians after\nEdward Snowden exposed the National Security Agency\xe2\x80\x99s bulk data collection\nprogram of Americans\xe2\x80\x99 phone records.\n\n\n\nBuoyed by Snowden\xe2\x80\x99s leaks, a bipartisan majority in the House moved to\noverhaul the bulk data program through the USA Freedom Act by proposing\nthat phone companies \xe2\x80\x94 not the federal government \xe2\x80\x94 maintain those records,\nthough the NSA could access them via a secret court order.\n\n\n\nBut Paul contends that the USA Freedom Act would be an expansion of the\nPATRIOT Act and could torpedo a lawsuit aimed at ending the bulk data\nprogram. The phone companies, he said, \xe2\x80\x9cmay do the same thing\xe2\x80\x9d as the NSA.\n\n\n\nRepublican leaders in the Senate, after initially resisting the USA Freedom\nAct because of concerns it would hamper intelligence gathering, on Sunday\nreluctantly accepted it. They did so with a midnight deadline to extend the\nsurveillance law hours away, their backs against the wall.\n\n\n\nThat made Paul even more isolated than he was already.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI think there are some legitimate debates going on in the country over who\nshould hold the documents,\xe2\x80\x9d said Sen. Roy Blunt (R-Mo.), a member of GOP\nleadership and the Senate Select Committee on Intelligence. \xe2\x80\x9cI think there\naren\xe2\x80\x99t very many people in Sen. Paul\xe2\x80\x99s place that believe that none of\nthese provisions need to be extended or held onto in some way.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nAfter skipping the GOP meeting, Paul appeared for a tense floor debate\nbetween him and his colleagues, including the man who has endorsed him for\npresident: Senate Majority Leader Mitch McConnell, a fellow Kentuckian. The\nGOP leader was incensed at Paul\xe2\x80\x99s refusal to allow a two-week renewal of\nfar-less controversial provisions of the PATRIOT Act: The use of roving\nwiretaps for terrorism suspects that change phone numbers quickly and \xe2\x80\x9clone\nwolf\xe2\x80\x9d provisions that allow tracking of suspects who are not affiliated\nwith known terrorist groups.\n\n\n\nJust as McConnell attempted to pass a short-term extension, Paul launched\ninto his own impassioned speech\xe2\x80\x94 only to be shouted down by his colleagues.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cOne of the promises that was given when the PATRIOT Act was originally\npassed was that in exchange for allowing a less than constitutional\nstandard, we would only use the actions against \xe2\x80\xa6\xe2\x80\x9d Paul said before he was\ninterrupted by Sen. Roger Wicker (R-Miss.), who pounded his desk while\npresiding over the Senate.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cIs there objection?\xe2\x80\x9d Wicker asked as Paul tried to continue on. A number\nof Republican senators began yelling over Paul to restore order in the\nchamber and prevent another lengthy speech.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cRegular order!\xe2\x80\x9d shouted Sens. John Barrasso (R-Wyo.) and Tom Cotton\n(R-Ark.), among others.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI object,\xe2\x80\x9d Paul responded. That prompted McConnell to launch his own\nspeech. At times glaring at Paul, the Senate leader blasted what he called\n\xe2\x80\x9ca campaign of demagoguery and disinformation launched in the wake of\nunlawful actions of Edward Snowden, who was last seen in Russia.\xe2\x80\x9d Paul sat\nat his desk quietly, holding his glasses in his hand.\n\n\n\nMcConnell never named Paul in his passionate speech, but it was clearly\naimed at the man who had been a close political ally \xe2\x80\x94 until now.\n\n\n\nOther colleagues did criticize Paul by name.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t stand with Rand on this,\xe2\x80\x9d said Sen. Mark Kirk (R-Ill.). \xe2\x80\x9cI want to\nmake sure the ability to monitor terrorists continues uninterrupted.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI think he\xe2\x80\x99s nestled in with a very large bunch of very radical people \xe2\x80\x93\nfrom the left to the right,\xe2\x80\x9d said Utah Sen. Orrin Hatch, the president pro\ntempore. \xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t know if he feels comfortable being with all those\nleftists who hate the PATRIOT Act. But he has a right to do what he\xe2\x80\x99s\ndoing.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nPaul ended up delaying a final Senate vote on the USA Freedom Act until\nlater this week. After blocking that bill before the Memorial Day recess,\nMcConnell and GOP leaders agreed to move the House\xe2\x80\x99s measure, saying they\nhad no other choice. By a 77-17 vote Sunday, the Senate broke a filibuster\nand moved to begin debate on the bill.\n\n\n\nTo overcome Paul\xe2\x80\x99s delay tactics, McConnell was forced to employ a rarely\nused prerogative to force senators to debate after a filibuster has been\nbroken, allowing him to move to final passage as early as Tuesday.\n\n\n\nAs that vote was occurring, Paul was sitting at his desk. He huddled with\ntwo libertarian-minded House members: GOP Reps. Justin Amash of Michigan\nand Thomas Massie of Kentucky. His fellow 2016 rivals, Sens. Ted Cruz of\nTexas and Marco Rubio of Florida, were yukking it up nearby with a small\ngroup of senators. (Rubio voted against proceeding to the House bill, while\nCruz supported it.)\n\n\n\nIn an interview, Amash said Paul\xe2\x80\x99s positions are supported \xe2\x80\x9coverwhelmingly\xe2\x80\x9d\nby voters of \xe2\x80\x9call political affiliations.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s not politically risky to stand with the vast majority of Americans,\xe2\x80\x9d\nAmash said. \xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m astonished when I hear Republican candidates in particular\nspeak as though people want the PATRIOT Act. They don\xe2\x80\x99t.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cHe\xe2\x80\x99s exposing the country to the Constitution,\xe2\x80\x9d Massie added. \xe2\x80\x9cAnd the\nsenators that think that\xe2\x80\x99s dangerous are saying the Constitution\xe2\x80\x99s\ndangerous.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nSeveral dozen Paul supporters sat in the Senate gallery on Sunday night\nclad in red \xe2\x80\x9cRand\xe2\x80\x9d T-shirts.\n\n\n\nBut Paul didn\xe2\x80\x99t have many other defenders in the halls of the Senate.\n\n\n\nRubio called the expiration of the PATRIOT Act\xe2\x80\x99s provisions the result of\n\xe2\x80\x9cpolitical posturing.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cThere are other ways this could have been done,\xe2\x80\x9d said Sen. Jeff Flake\n(R-Ariz.).\n\n\n\nOne way Paul could have handled the matter would have been to simply object\nto short-term extensions of current law, rather than giving a nearly\n11-hour floor speech on the floor before the Memorial Day recess, Heller\nsaid.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt accomplished just the same, but he couldn\xe2\x80\x99t raise money objecting,\xe2\x80\x9d\nHeller said. \xe2\x80\x9cHe could only raise money filibustering.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\n*Mike Huckabee to Rand Paul: Decide what job you want\n<http://www.cnn.com/2015/06/01/politics/mike-huckabee-rand-paul-patriot-act/index.html>\n// CNN // Gregory Wallace \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\n(CNN)Former Arkansas Gov. Mike Huckabee wants Rand Paul to make a choice:\nProtest the Patriot Act either on the Senate floor or on the campaign trail.\n\n\n\nHe joined a chorus of Republican presidential hopefuls weighing in on the\nKentucky Republican senator\'s protest of the Patriot Act, key provisions of\nwhich lapsed Sunday.\n\n\n\nPaul claimed credit for blocking parts of the renewal of the controversial\nlaw, and his protests included an 11-hour speech on the eve of the\nchamber\'s Memorial Day break, as well as objections to several short-term\nextensions of the Act.\n\n\n\nIn response to a question about Paul, Huckabee said on Fox News Monday\nmorning that 2016 contenders must "decide what they want to be when they\ngrow up."\n\n\n\n"If you want to be a governor, be a governor. If you want to be a senator,\nbe a senator," Huckabee said. "If you want to be president, then let go of\nwhat you\'re doing, because it\'s a full time pursuit to run for the\npresidency."\n\n\n\nThose in government positions owe a responsibility to the taxpayer, he\ncontinued.\n\n\n\n"If you want a different job, then say I don\'t want this one anymore. I\'m\nbored with it," he said. "But be honest about it and go out and give the\ntaxpayers a break, and let them have someone on the job full time."\n\n\n\nHuckabee added in a follow-up question that he did not mean to "impugn his\n(Paul\'s) motives" because "this is not something he just took up because\nit\'s a political cause."\n\n\n\nMany of those running for president are out of office, though two of Paul\'s\nSenate colleagues -- Marco Rubio of Florida and Ted Cruz of Texas -- are in\nthe race, and Sen. Lindsey Graham of South Carolina is expected to announce\na bid on Monday. Sen. Bernie Sanders of Vermont is running for the\nDemocratic nomination. Several sitting governors -- including Chris\nChristie of New Jersey, John Kasich of Ohio, Louisiana Gov. Bobby Jindal\nand Scott Walker of Wisconsin -- are considering joining the GOP field.\n\n\n\nUnlike several other Republicans who have hammered Paul for blocking the\nPatriot Act renewal, Huckabee believes the original law went too far.\n\n\n\nHe said the original law was "hastily passed" in the wake of 9/11 without\nextensive debate. Public opinion has shifted now, he said.\n\n\n\n"Fourteen years ago, we were worried about terrorists. Now we\'re worried\nabout our government," Huckabee said, singling out controversies around the\nIRS and Justice Departments.\n\n\n\n*Rand Paul\'s Stand Against the Patriot Act Is About More Than Mass\nSurveillance\n<http://mic.com/articles/119766/rand-paul-s-stand-against-the-patriot-act-is-about-more-than-mass-surveillance>\n// Policy.Mic // Mark Kogan \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nOn Sunday night, controversial elements of the Patriot Act were allowed to\nexpire for the first time since its passage following the Sept. 11 attacks\nin 2001.\n\n\n\nSen. Rand Paul (R-Ky.), whose procedural maneuvers prevented the Senate\nfrom renewing the bill in its entirety, declared in a press release that\n"tonight begins the process of ending bulk collection" of data for mass\nsurveillance.\n\n\n\nPaul\'s efforts, whether motivated by personal beliefs, presidential\naspirations or a healthy mix of both, mark an important moment in American\npolitics, not just for the debate over mass surveillance, but for\ncongressional gridlock in general.\n\n\n\nIn recent decades, as congressional politics became increasingly polarized\nand meaningful compromise became less common, the practical challenge for\nlegislators was the sheer impossibility of moving legislation through the\nsystem without some sort of forcing function.\n\n\n\nLegislators began pushing fewer individual bills, instead packing their\nprojects and policies into "omnibus" bills that addressed entire sectors of\ngovernment rather than individual pieces. These amalgamated bills were\noften funding bills and therefore "must-pass" legislation. Voting against\nomnibus bills became too risky because failing to pass the larger bill over\ndisagreements with one or two relatively minor provisions carried the\nthreat of tremendous collateral damage (both real and political).\n\n\n\nAs this process of smashing through "must-pass" bills became standard\noperating procedure, the political leadership made another cynical\ndiscovery. By waiting until the last second and using the subsequent fear\nof imminent expiration to force passage, politicians were able to avoid\ndebating elements of the bill that put them at risk while simultaneously\nensuring passage.\n\n\n\nThe lead-up to this year\'s renewal of the Patriot Act played out similarly:\nEveryone from President Barack Obama to Senate Republicans warned of the\ndangers of failing to pass the bill wholesale.\n\n\n\nUrging the Senate to act this week, Obama warned of the dangers of letting\nsurveillance authorities expire.\n\n\n\n"I don\'t want us to be in a situation in which for a certain period of time\nthose authorities go away and suddenly we are dark," he said. "And heaven\nforbid we\'ve got a problem where we could have prevented a terrorist attack\nor apprehended someone who is engaged in dangerous activity but we didn\'t\ndo so simply because of inaction in the Senate."\n\n\n\nOthers in the administration pushed the same message. In an interview with\nCBS, newly minted Attorney General Loretta Lynch declared that failing to\nrenew the Patriot Act would make us "less safe" and cause us to "lose\nimportant eyes on people who have made it clear ... that their mission is\nto harm American people here and abroad."\n\n\n\nRepublicans also joined in on the fear-mongering as the vote deadline\napproached. Senate Majority Leader Mitch McConnell (R-Ky.) said on the\nSenate floor that failure to pass or extend the act "would mean disarming\ncompletely and arbitrarily."\n\n\n\nOthers were even more direct. "To go dark on this," said Sen. Dan Coats\n(R-Ind.), NPR reported, "is a risk on Americans\' lives."\n\n\n\nHistorically, this was a tried and true formula that would have ensured\nimmediate passage or at least temporary extension while the requisite\narm-twisting was done to secure passage. But for the first time in a long\ntime, it didn\'t work.\n\n\n\n"The people who argue that the world will end and we will be overrun by\njihadists tonight are trying to use fear... They want you to fear and give\nup your liberty," said Paul in his statement. "They tell you if you have\nnothing to hide, you have nothing to fear. That\'s a far cry from the\nstandard we were founded upon."\n\n\n\nNow, with two more days of mandatory debate forced by Paul, the contentious\nissue of mass surveillance will be brought to the forefront of civic\ndiscourse. This will almost certainly result in meaningful reforms as the\nSenate takes up the House-passed USA Freedom Act, which curtails\ncontentious mass data collection powers while leaving other elements of the\nPatriot Act in place.\n\n\n\nWhen Paul rose to speak on Sunday, he knew that his opposition was a\nbeginning, rather than an end. "The Patriot Act will expire tonight," Paul\nsaid, but, "It will only be temporary. They will ultimately get their way."\n\n\n\nYet even if they do get their way, this shock is good for the system and\nwill serve as a reminder that the politics of fear and pressure are not\nnecessary and are in fact anathema to good governance, doing far more harm\nthan good.\n\n\n\nBy forcing expiration and debate, the public has been given an opportunity\nto nudge public dialogue away from partisan grandstanding toward more\nmeaningful discussion of serious issues. Hopefully, we take advantage of it.\n\n\n\n*Rand Paul is getting way too much credit for killing 3 Patriot Act powers\n<http://www.vox.com/2015/6/1/8700111/rand-paul-patriot-act> // Vox //\nTimothy B. Lee \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nWhen three controversial provisions of the Patriot Act expired at midnight\non Sunday, May 31, 2015, news organizations put Rand Paul (R-KY) front and\ncenter. We at Vox did that ourselves, with a story titled "Rand Paul has\nforced three Patriot Act powers to expire."\n\n\n\nThis isn\'t wrong \xe2\x80\x94 it\'s true that Paul\'s obstructionist tactics helped\nensure that the Patriot Act powers would lapse before the Senate had time\nto pass a replacement. And Paul\'s dramatic 10-hour speech two weeks ago\nmade for a good story, which is why it got so much media attention. But the\nmedia\'s focus on Paul has led to the Kentucky Republican getting way too\nmuch credit for the ultimate outcome of this week\'s surveillance fight.\n\n\n\nThe fight is likely to result in the passage of the USA Freedom Act \xe2\x80\x94 which\nseeks to place stricter limits on NSA surveillance but which some privacy\nadvocates say doesn\'t go far enough \xe2\x80\x94 later this week. Paul has opposed\nthis legislation. And if Paul hadn\'t engaged in his theatrics, the most\nlikely outcome would have been exactly the same. The only difference is\nthat the USA Freedom Act might have passed a few days earlier.\n\n\n\nIf the USA Freedom Act passes in the Senate, credit (or blame) should go to\nthe 57 senators \xe2\x80\x94 mostly Democrats \xe2\x80\x94 who supported the legislation a week\nago, and to the 54 senators \xe2\x80\x94 again mostly Democrats \xe2\x80\x94 who voted down a\nstraight renewal of the Patriot Act during the same Friday-night session.\nRand Paul\'s filibuster was wildly successful at getting Rand Paul\'s name in\nheadlines. But it ultimately had little effect on the outcome of the\nlegislative fight.\n\n\n\nThe Republican leadership of the House also deserves a lot of credit for\nreining in the NSA. If the lower House had not passed the USA Freedom Act\nseveral weeks ago, Mitch McConnell might have convinced a majority of the\nSenate that renewing the Patriot Act was the only realistic option.\n\n\n\nThe Patriot Act powers died because 54 senators wanted them to die\n\n\n\nRep. James Sensenbrenner (R-WI) wrote the original version of the USA\nFreedom Act in 2013 and played a key role in shepherding the legislation\nthrough the House of Representatives. (Douglas Graham/Roll Call/Getty\nImages)\n\n\n\nThe crucial moment in the Patriot Act fight wasn\'t Rand Paul\'s filibuster\non Wednesday, May 20. It was a series of votes taken two days later, on\nFriday, May 22. Senate Majority Leader Mitch McConnell (R-KY) wanted to\nforce the Senate to renew the Patriot Act without changes. His plan was to\nbring the USA Freedom Act up for a vote, let it fail, and then tell\nsenators their only alternative was a short-term renewal of the Patriot Act\nwith no changes.\n\n\n\nThe first part of this plan worked. The USA Freedom Act got 57 votes, just\nshort of the 60 votes required to overcome a filibuster. But when McConnell\nthen called a vote on extending the Patriot Act for two months, the\nsenators didn\'t flinch \xe2\x80\x94 54 of them voted no.\n\n\n\nAt this point the question was who would blink first. Would pro-privacy\nsenators agree to extend the Patriot Act without changes? Or would\npro-surveillance senators agree to support the USA Freedom Act? On Sunday\nnight, it was McConnell himself who blinked, concluding that the USA\nFreedom Act he had opposed a week earlier was now "the only realistic way\nforward." This time 77 senators voted for the USA Freedom Act.\n\n\n\n"The Senate will pass a reform that just got 77 votes," says Julian Sanchez\na privacy advocate at the Cato Institute (where I worked from 2003 to\n2005). He notes that Paul joined "16 of the most hardcore NSA cheerleaders\nin the Senate" in opposing the legislation.\n\n\n\nMcConnell\'s capitulation was a real victory for pro-privacy senators. But\nPaul deserves little, if any, credit for it. After all, if Paul had backed\nthe USA Freedom Act and convinced two of his fellow Republicans to join\nhim, the legislation could have moved forward sooner. Paul\'s decision to\nbreak with the overwhelming majority of pro-privacy senators and oppose the\nUSA Freedom Act delayed the legislation\'s passage and created a risk that\nMcConnell would be able to stampede the Senate into renewing the Patriot\nAct.\n\n\n\nEven if Paul\'s defiant tactics didn\'t change the outcome of the debate,\nSanchez says they helped illustrate that "scaremongering" by surveillance\nhawks no longer works. "Americans aren\'t afraid of the dark anymore," he\nsays. "A sunset can\'t be used to coerce legislators into capitulation with\nunchecked surveillance powers."\n\n\n\nOther members of Congress deserve more credit than Rand Paul\n\n\n\nSen. Mike Lee (R-UT) provided key Republican support for the USA Freedom\nAct in the Senate. (Alex Wong/Getty Images)\n\n\n\nRand Paul\'s tactics have gotten him a lot of press attention \xe2\x80\x94 and,\ntherefore, a lot of undeserved credit \xe2\x80\x94 for the outcome of the legislative\nfight. But a larger share of the credit should go to other senators.\nSanchez points to Senators Ron Wyden (D-OR), Patrick Leahy (D-VT), and Mike\nLee (R-UT) as three examples of senators who did the hard work of building\na consensus for the USA Freedom Act in the Senate.\n\n\n\nAnd even more credit should go to House leaders such as Rep. James\nSensenbrenner (R-WI) who passed the USA Freedom Act in a lopsided,\nbipartisan vote several weeks ago. The fact that the House had already\npassed the USA Freedom Act made it a lot easier for pro-privacy senators to\nposition it as a reasonable alternative to renewing the Patriot Act.\n\n\n\n"It is valuable that Paul is using his platform as a presidential candidate\nto drive attention to this issue," Sanchez says. But "Paul hasn\'t\nultimately done much to drive the substantive policy outcome."\n\n\n\n*Dick Cheney and Daughter Push Hawkish Stances for G.O.P. Hopefuls\n<http://www.nytimes.com/politics/first-draft/2015/06/01/dick-cheney-and-daughter-push-hawkish-stances-for-g-o-p-hopefuls/?module=BlogPost-Title&version=Blog%20Main&contentCollection=Politics&action=Click&pgtype=Blogs&region=Body>\n// NYT // Jonathan Martin \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nThe rise of the Islamic State in the Middle East has pushed Republicans\ntoward embracing a more interventionist foreign policy, and now one\nprominent Republican family wants to be sure the party stays that way.\n\n\n\nFormer Vice President Dick Cheney and his daughter Liz Cheney are planning\nto make their presence felt in the 2016 presidential campaign through their\nadvocacy group, Alliance for a Strong America.\n\n\n\nThe organization is planning online and perhaps television ads pushing a\nmuscular line on national security, according to a Republican strategist\nfamiliar with the group\xe2\x80\x99s planning. The initiative may also pay for polling\nto help nudge Republican candidates toward hawkish stances in the primary\nseason.\n\n\n\nWhat is not clear, though, is whether the Cheneys intend to train their\nfire on Hillary Rodham Clinton or whether they plan to target Senator Rand\nPaul, the libertarian-leaning Kentuckian who has recently sought to bolster\nhis White House campaign by trying to block a renewal of parts of the\nPatriot Act.\n\n\n\nMr. Cheney criticized Mr. Paul as \xe2\x80\x9can isolationist\xe2\x80\x9d in an interview\npublished online Sunday in The Wall Street Journal, which first reported\nthe Alliance for a Strong America\xe2\x80\x99s plans.\n\n\n\nAsked about the assessment, Mr. Paul\xe2\x80\x99s top political adviser questioned Mr.\nCheney\xe2\x80\x99s conservative credentials.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnyone who defends warrantless spying on innocent U.S. citizens, like\nPresident Obama, has no right to call themselves a freedom-loving\nconservative,\xe2\x80\x9d said Doug Stafford, the adviser to Mr. Paul. \xe2\x80\x9cWorse is these\npeople are defending and supporting a program that the courts have said is\nillegal and the F.B.I. reports hasn\xe2\x80\x99t led to a single terrorist arrest or\nthwarted terror plot. It has only resulted in the trampling of Americans\xe2\x80\x99\nrights.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nThe harsh back-and-forth between the Cheneys and Mr. Paul\xe2\x80\x99s orbit\nillustrates not only the tension in the party over how to balance defense\nand civil liberties, but also, as Mr. Stafford notes, basic questions about\nwhat it means to be a conservative on matters of national security.\n\n\n\nThe resurgence of radical Islamic terrorism in the Middle East may have\npushed many primary voters toward a more hawkish orientation, but Mr.\nPaul\xe2\x80\x99s success in at least temporarily stopping the N.S.A.\xe2\x80\x99s use of\nmetadata suggests that Republicans are uneasy with some of the intelligence\npolicies put into effect during Mr. Cheney\xe2\x80\x99s time as vice president.\n\n\n\nRepublicans who have spoken with Mr. Cheney, who represented Wyoming in the\nHouse for 10 years and who  maintains an intense interest in both policy\nand political intrigue, say he is plainly concerned about the party backing\naway from intelligence programs.\n\n\n\nSelective about his public appearances, Mr. Cheney is engaged in the 2016\npresidential race behind the scenes. When aides to many of the leading\nRepublican candidates descended on Wyoming this year to make their pitch to\na group of wealthy donors, some of the staff members were surprised to find\nMr. Cheney in the audience.\n\n\n\n*How Bobby Jindal lost everything: A one-time GOP hope, gutted by Grover\nNorquist worship and his own ambition\n<http://www.salon.com/2015/06/01/how_bobby_jindal_lost_everything_a_one_time_gop_hope_gutted_by_grover_norquist_worship_and_his_own_ambition/>\n// Salon // Stephanie Grace \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nThese are not happy times in Baton Rouge, where government officials are\ndesperately trying to plug a $1.6 billion budget shortfall. But even by\nthat standard, Wednesday, April 22, was particularly fraught.\n\n\n\nIn the imposing state capitol that Huey Long built, the Senate Finance\nCommittee was wrestling with a complicated cost-cutting scheme to repeal an\ninventory tax that businesses pay to local governments and that the state\nrebates to the businesses, all while promising to somehow make stressed-out\nlocal leaders whole.\n\n\n\nJust down the road, Louisiana State University President and Chancellor F.\nKing Alexander said that the state\xe2\x80\x99s flagship university, which could lose\n80 percent of state funding after years of already deep cuts, was\ndeveloping a worst-case scenario plan for financial exigency\xe2\x80\x94basically the\nacademic equivalent of bankruptcy.\n\n\n\nIn the midst of it all came a message from Republican Governor Bobby\nJindal, whose policies and priorities have contributed mightily to the\nstate\xe2\x80\x99s fiscal mess.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cHelp wish my friends Willie, Phil and Si a happy birthday,\xe2\x80\x9d said the\ntweet, which was accompanied by a photo of Willie Robertson, whose family\nis featured on the popular homegrown reality TV show Duck Dynasty. It then\ndirected readers to the website for the American Future Project, a 527\nissue advocacy group that Jindal has set up in advance of his anticipated\npresidential run.\n\n\n\nIf the tweet suggests a stunning disconnect from the dire budget situation\nthat\xe2\x80\x99s unfolding on his watch, well, that\xe2\x80\x99s how it is these days.\n\n\n\nA Pure Record on Taxes\n\n\n\nJindal, a hard-charging former Rhodes Scholar, has always nursed grander\nambitions, and voters generally gave him a pass. That was when things were\ngoing well.\n\n\n\nThese days they\xe2\x80\x99re not, and Jindal\xe2\x80\x99s focus on the upcoming presidential\nprimaries has taken a toll back home. While he was popular and powerful\nenough to avoid a reelection fight in 2011, by 2015 his approval rating had\nsunk to 27 percent, according to one poll; a friendly survey by his own\nconsulting firm pegged the number at 46 percent, hardly a resounding vote\nof confidence.\n\n\n\nIt\xe2\x80\x99s not just his frequent trips to places like Iowa, New Hampshire, and\nWashington, D.C., that have angered his constituents. (He spent 165 days\nout of state in 2014, according to The Advocate newspaper.) Nor is it only\nhis odd forays into international and national affairs, from the tall tales\nin London about Muslim no-go zones, to his op-ed in The New York Times\naccusing companies that oppose religious freedom laws inspired by the\nspread of gay marriage of forming an unholy alliance with the \xe2\x80\x9cradical\nliberals.\xe2\x80\x9d It\xe2\x80\x99s not even his need to bask in the Robertsons\xe2\x80\x99 reflected\nglory.\n\n\n\nMore than any of that, his constituents are frustrated that their governor\ncan\xe2\x80\x99t be bothered to do his day job\xe2\x80\x94and when he does, that his actions are\noften transparently designed to build a national profile rather than meet\nLouisiana\xe2\x80\x99s needs.\n\n\n\nThat\xe2\x80\x99s clear in his refusal to take federal money to expand Medicaid\xe2\x80\x94which,\nof course, would mean acknowledging there are benefits to Obama\xe2\x80\x99s health\ncare law. But nowhere is it more obvious, or more damaging, than in\nJindal\xe2\x80\x99s stewardship of fiscal affairs.\n\n\n\nJindal chalks up the current budget shortfall to the drop in oil prices,\nand that\xe2\x80\x99s definitely contributed. A larger piece of the puzzle has been\nhis determination to maintain a pure record on taxes.\n\n\n\nJindal hasn\xe2\x80\x99t always been reckless about taxation. In the midst of a budget\nsurplus early in his first term, Jindal tried to quietly head off the\nLegislature\xe2\x80\x99s move to roll back a big income tax increase that had been\nenacted several years earlier. It was only after lawmakers seemed like they\nmight eliminate the income tax entirely that he got on board with the\nrollback, and he soon was boasting that he\xe2\x80\x99d signed the biggest tax cut in\nstate history.\n\n\n\nThe first real glimpse of the future came in 2011 when Jindal fought tooth\nand nail against extending a temporary four-cent levy on the state\xe2\x80\x99s\ncigarette tax\xe2\x80\x94at 36 cents, including the levy, the third lowest in the\nnation. His reasoning? If the tax rate is scheduled to automatically drop\nand the state acts to prevent that from happening, it amounts to an\neffective tax increase.\n\n\n\nThe stance left his constituents cold, but impressed Grover Norquist of\nAmericans for Tax Reform (ATR), who would endorse Jindal as Mitt Romney\xe2\x80\x99s\nrunning mate the following year.\n\n\n\nEven Republicans Are Bristling\n\n\n\nThese days it\xe2\x80\x99s hard to think of anyone who has as much influence over what\nJindal\xe2\x80\x99s willing to do than Norquist, whose rigid rules for what\nconstitutes a tax increase line up perfectly with Jindal\xe2\x80\x99s. In practice,\nthat means the governor has insisted that the budget be balanced without\ntax increases, despite the prospect of devastating cuts to higher education\nand health care, the two main areas that don\xe2\x80\x99t enjoy constitutional or\nstatutory protection.\n\n\n\nAnd it means some revenue-enhancing ideas the Republican-dominated\nLegislature might support, specifically a reexamination of giveaways to\nspecific industries, are off limits\xe2\x80\x94because eliminating a tax exemption\nwithout an offset that reduces another tax or cuts spending, according to\nATR, is raising a tax.\n\n\n\nThat\xe2\x80\x99s how the inventory tax wound up in everyone\xe2\x80\x99s crosshairs, despite the\nfact that eliminating the rebate but not the underlying tax would hurt\nbusinesses, and getting rid of the tax would devastate some parishes\n(that\xe2\x80\x99s Louisiana for county). Many companies, it turns out, receive rebate\nchecks that exceed their state tax liability, and in Jindal\xe2\x80\x99s view that\nmakes eliminating the payouts a spending cut, not a tax increase.\n\xe2\x80\x9cCorporate welfare,\xe2\x80\x9d he labeled it in his opening address to the\nLegislature, prompting chuckles from those who\xe2\x80\x99ve watched him promote\nbusiness incentives for years.\n\n\n\nIn fact, perhaps the most remarkable aspect of the frustration with Jindal\nis that it transcends partisanship.\n\n\n\nIt\xe2\x80\x99s not just the Democrats who are bristling. It\xe2\x80\x99s many a Republican.\n\n\n\nNothing Left to Cut\n\n\n\nRepublicans who belong to an informal group dubbed the \xe2\x80\x9cfiscal hawks\xe2\x80\x9d have\nbeen sharply critical of Jindal\xe2\x80\x99s reliance over the years on one-time money\ntransfers and accounting gimmicks to balance the budget without making even\ndeeper cuts.\n\n\n\nOne reason everything\xe2\x80\x99s hitting the fan is there\xe2\x80\x99s not much left. Gone are\n$800 million from the Medicaid Trust Fund for the Elderly and $450 million\nfor providing development incentives, and the rainy day fund has dropped\nfrom $730 million to $460 million on his watch.\n\n\n\nRepublicans like state Rep. Jay Morris, who, after hearing Jindal\xe2\x80\x99s vow to\nveto any measure that didn\xe2\x80\x99t have Grover Norquist\xe2\x80\x99s blessing, declared the\napproach \xe2\x80\x9cinsane.\xe2\x80\x9d And like state Sen. Jack Donahue, who chairs the Finance\nCommittee and who passed a bill last year seeking to determine how much the\nstate spends on tax exemptions, only to watch Jindal veto it.\n\n\n\nAnd perhaps most tellingly, the Republicans running to replace Jindal in\nthis fall\xe2\x80\x99s election. All three\xe2\x80\x94Lt. Governor Jay Dardenne, U.S. Senator\nDavid Vitter and Public Service Commissioner (and former Jindal aide) Scott\nAngelle\xe2\x80\x94say they will look for a way to accept the Medicaid money and take\na open-minded approach to examining tax exemptions.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat this state needs right now is a leader solely focused on Louisiana,\xe2\x80\x9d\nDardenne said in a recent speech. And in a clear swipe at Norquist, he\nadded that, \xe2\x80\x9cI represent the people of Louisiana; I don\xe2\x80\x99t represent someone\nwho lives in D.C.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nAnd Vitter said he\xe2\x80\x99d take a good, hard look at tax incentives and other\ngiveaways, even if it means raising revenue.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cGov. Jindal should be doing this now,\xe2\x80\x9d he pointedly said. \xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99ll do it the\nminute I\xe2\x80\x99m sworn in.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\n*UPDATE: Walker backs 20-week abortion ban with or without exemption\n<http://www.nbc15.com/home/headlines/Republicans-introduce-bill-banning-abortions-after-20-weeks-302953851.html>\n// NBC 15 \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nUPDATED Monday, June 1, 2015---10:35 a.m.\n\n\n\nDELAVAN, Wis. (AP) -- Wisconsin Republicans have introduced a bill that\nwould ban abortions after 20 weeks of pregnancy.\n\n\n\nRep. Jesse Kremer, a Kewaskum Republican, and Sen.
