Scott Walker on Thursday said he supports the bill and hopes the\nLegislature could move forward with the abortion ban while it works on the\nbudget.\n\n*Jeb Bush Faces Challenge in Winning Over Brother\xe2\x80\x99s Team\n<http://www.nytimes.com/2015/06/02/us/politics/jeb-bush-faces-challenge-in-winning-over-brothers-team.html>\n// NYT // Peter Baker \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nWASHINGTON \xe2\x80\x94 When George W. Bush first ran for president, he liked to say\nhe had inherited half of his father\xe2\x80\x99s friends and all of his enemies. For\nJeb Bush, now preparing his own bid for the White House, that may ring\nfamiliar.\n\n\n\nHis brother\xe2\x80\x99s enemies have made themselves known in recent weeks as Jeb\nBush has struggled to formulate his own take on the decisions made during\nthe last Bush presidency. But perhaps just as important for the fledgling\ncandidate has been the challenge in winning over his brother\xe2\x80\x99s friends.\n\n\n\nWhile George W. Bush himself and many in his circle, especially those\nclosest to the family, are enthusiastic about the prospect of a third Bush\npresidency, many of the Republican foot soldiers who worked for the former\npresident in his campaigns and his administration have not rushed to back\nhis brother\xe2\x80\x99s emerging operation.\n\n\n\nA sampling conducted largely by email of about 120 people who worked for\nGeorge W. Bush \xe2\x80\x94 from cabinet secretaries to foreign policy advisers to\nadvance aides \xe2\x80\x94 found about 25 who said they were supporting his younger\nbrother. Fifty others said they were neutral or supporting another\ncandidate, while the rest did not respond, passing up a chance to declare\nallegiance to the next Bush candidacy.\n\n\n\nSome harbor the same reservations that other Republicans do about the\nnotion of a dynastic presidency passed from one member of a family to\nanother. Some simply want a fresh start, concluding that the party would\nmake a stronger case against Hillary Rodham Clinton, the likely Democratic\ncandidate, by nominating a new figure like Senator Marco Rubio of Florida\nor Gov. Scott Walker of Wisconsin. Some nurse doubts about Jeb Bush\nspecifically, even on policies he shares with his brother.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m neutral,\xe2\x80\x9d said Matt Latimer, a former White House speechwriter. \xe2\x80\x9cIf\npressed, I\xe2\x80\x99m inclined to adopt the Barbara Bush philosophy \xe2\x80\x94 enough\nBushes.\xe2\x80\x9d (Mrs. Bush, the mother of the two brothers, who initially did say\nthat, has since taken it back. \xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99ve changed my mind,\xe2\x80\x9d she said.)\n\n\n\nAnother former White House official who worked closely with former\nPresident Bush said it would be a mistake for the country for his brother\nto become president. \xe2\x80\x9cI happen to believe the U.S. is Bushed and Clintoned\nout,\xe2\x80\x9d said this official, who like many others asked not to be named to\navoid offending his former boss. \xe2\x80\x9cIt is time for others to lead.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nA spokesman for Jeb Bush, a former governor of Florida, said he did not\ntake any support for granted. \xe2\x80\x9cGovernor Bush realizes that should he decide\nto move forward, he\xe2\x80\x99s going to have to work to earn support across the\nparty \xe2\x80\x94 just as the other prospective candidates will,\xe2\x80\x9d said Tim Miller,\nthe spokesman.\n\n\n\nMany of the Bush veterans unwilling to back him cited work reasons,\nexplaining that their current employers would not want them to take sides\npublicly. Some are now working as academics, party officials or television\npundits, and said they wanted to retain a professional detachment from any\none candidate. Some said they hoped to be able to advise several of the\nRepublican candidates, and there was no consensus for any of Mr. Bush\xe2\x80\x99s\nopponents.\n\n\n\nOthers held back not because they oppose Mr. Bush, but because they worried\nthat publicly supporting him would only hurt his chances by reinforcing his\nties to his brother. They were acutely aware of the criticism he received\nwhen he released a list of foreign policy advisers that included many who\nhad worked for his brother, like Paul D. Wolfowitz, the former deputy\ndefense secretary.\n\n\n\nWhatever the reason, the mixed emotions in the 43rd president\xe2\x80\x99s team\nunderscore a vicious quandary for Jeb Bush. Much as he wants to present\nhimself as his own man, he cannot assume that his brother\xe2\x80\x99s supporters will\nautomatically transfer to him. So he must make the case for their support,\nand for that of the broader electorate, even as he labors to avoid being\nbranded a copy of his brother.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt is fair to say that those who are inclined to support Jeb out of\nloyalty to 41 or 43 have already jumped in,\xe2\x80\x9d said Stephen Yates, who worked\non national security in the George W. Bush White House and is now chairman\nof the Idaho Republican Party. \xe2\x80\x9cEveryone else is up for grabs. He\xe2\x80\x99ll be\nable to get some of the remainder, but no advantage over others.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nNeil Patel, a Bush White House official and publisher of The Daily Caller,\na conservative news site, said the Republican field had many good choices.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t think anyone, including Jeb Bush, should expect to automatically\npick up support to become president \xe2\x80\x94 especially by virtue of being related\nto a past president. And I doubt he would disagree with that,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.\n\xe2\x80\x9cLots of former colleagues are lined up behind Jeb but many are also with\nRubio, Walker and others.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nThe distance kept by some from the 43rd president\xe2\x80\x99s team reflects the\nreality that the two brothers have long traveled in separate political\norbits, with the elder based in Texas and the younger based in Florida.\nThere has been relatively little overlap over the years beyond family\nretainers.\n\n\n\nAnd so some of George W. Bush\xe2\x80\x99s former aides were willing to publicly\ncriticize Jeb Bush a few weeks ago when he stumbled over the question of\nwhether he would have invaded Iraq had he known there were no\nunconventional weapons there.\n\n\n\nKarl Rove, the former president\xe2\x80\x99s longtime political strategist; Andrew H.\nCard Jr., the former White House chief of staff; and Ari Fleischer, the\nformer press secretary, all expressed concern at the handling of the issue.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t think it would have taken his brother that long to clean it up,\xe2\x80\x9d\nMr. Card said on MSNBC. But Mr. Card was among those who offered unstinting\nsupport for Jeb Bush. \xe2\x80\x9cI am proudly for Jeb,\xe2\x80\x9d he said by email.\n\n\n\nOthers offering their backing were some of the Republicans who were closest\nto his brother, including Margaret Spellings, the former education\nsecretary, who runs the George W. Bush Presidential Center, and Donald L.\nEvans, the former president\xe2\x80\x99s longtime Texas friend and commerce secretary.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI very much support Jeb and he would be a great president if he decides to\nrun,\xe2\x80\x9d Mr. Evans said.\n\n\n\nMs. Spellings said she was \xe2\x80\x9centhusiastically supporting\xe2\x80\x9d him. \xe2\x80\x9cAs you might\nimagine, Jeb and I have a relationship independent of his brother given our\nshared interest in education reform, and we have worked together for many\nyears,\xe2\x80\x9d she said.\n\n\n\nFor some, though, it seemed as much obligation as fervor. \xe2\x80\x9cYes,\xe2\x80\x9d a longtime\nfriend and financial donor to George W. Bush said when asked if he was\nsupporting the former president\xe2\x80\x99s brother. \xe2\x80\x9cDo I have a choice?\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nOne who decided he did have a choice was Wayne Berman, an official in the\nadministration of the first President George Bush, and a friend and\nfund-raiser for George W. Bush and whose wife worked in the 43rd\npresident\xe2\x80\x99s White House. This time around, Mr. Berman is a senior adviser\nto Mr. Rubio.\n\n\n\nAmong those declaring neutrality rather than publicly embracing Jeb Bush\xe2\x80\x99s\ncandidacy is former Vice President Dick Cheney, who with his daughter Liz\nCheney has started the Alliance for a Strong America to advocate tough\nnational security positions among various candidates.\n\n\n\nOthers include former Secretary of State Condoleezza Rice, although she is\nleading Mr. Bush\xe2\x80\x99s education foundation; Mr. Rove, who comments on Fox News\nand in The Wall Street Journal; Mr. Fleischer; Michael Gerson, a former\nsenior White House adviser now writing for The Washington Post; Ed\nGillespie, a former presidential counselor; Mark McKinnon, a campaign\nstrategist for the former president; and cabinet secretaries like former\nAttorney General John Ashcroft.\n\n\n\nPaul J. McNulty, who served as George W. Bush\xe2\x80\x99s deputy attorney general and\nis now president of Grove City College in Pennsylvania, said he was torn\nbetween Jeb Bush and former Gov. Mike Huckabee of Arkansas. \xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99ve always\nbeen a big fan of Jeb,\xe2\x80\x9d he said, \xe2\x80\x9cbut I worry about his electability.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nRyan Streeter, a former domestic policy aide to George W. Bush, said the\nissues had changed since his former boss left office. Fiscal concerns are\ngreater, and Republicans are more skeptical of enlarging the federal role\nin setting education standards for schools or expanding Medicare to cover\nprescription drugs, as the former president did.\n\n\n\nAs a result, said Mr. Streeter, who now directs the Center for Politics and\nGovernance at the University of Texas at Austin, \xe2\x80\x9clots of 43 staffers\xe2\x80\x99\nviews reflect those changes since many of them have stayed engaged in\npolicy and politics.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cThese issues, more than anything,\xe2\x80\x9d he said, \xe2\x80\x9cwill affect who they get\nbehind in 2016.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\n*Huckabee: Two-State Solution Is \xe2\x80\x9cIrrational, Unworkable\xe2\x80\x9d \xe2\x80\x94 Room For\nPalestinian State Elsewhere\n<http://www.buzzfeed.com/andrewkaczynski/huckabee-two-state-solution-is-irrational-unworkable-plenty#.abkVmV02Q>\n// Buzzfeed // Andrew Kaczynski \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nFormer Arkansas Gov. and Republican presidential candidate Mike Huckabee\nargued over the weekend a two-state solution is \xe2\x80\x9cirrational and unworkable\xe2\x80\x9d\nand that if a Palestinian state is created, it must exist outside of\nIsrael. Huckabee said there\xe2\x80\x99s plenty of land elsewhere in the world for a\nPalestinian state.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe two state solution, if we mean two governments holding the same piece\nof real estate is irrational and unworkable,\xe2\x80\x9d Huckabee told Arutz Sheva TV\non Sunday during an appearance at the Israel Day Concert in Central Park,\nNew York.\n\n\n\nHuckabee, who refers to the area commonly called the West Bank as Judea and\nSamaria, called arguing for the two-state solution a \xe2\x80\x9cpretentious game.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd I think it\xe2\x80\x99s time for us to quit playing this pretentious game that\nthere\xe2\x80\x99s gonna be a two-state solution where both sides share the same\ncountry and real estate and streets \xe2\x80\x98cause they\xe2\x80\x99re not,\xe2\x80\x9d said Huckabee.\n\xe2\x80\x9cOne of the sides the Palestinians continue to say that Israel doesn\xe2\x80\x99t have\na right to exist. You can\xe2\x80\x99t forge an alliance with that.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nHuckabee cited there being \xe2\x80\x9cplenty of land in the world\xe2\x80\x9d to find a place\nfor a Palestinian state outside of Israel.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cIf there\xe2\x80\x99s a two-state solution, the Palestinians state needs to be\noutside the boundaries of the nation of Israel. There\xe2\x80\x99s plenty of land in\nthe world where we can find a place and say, \xe2\x80\x98Okay, let\xe2\x80\x99s create a\nPalestinian state.\xe2\x80\x99 But not within the confides of a secure Israel.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nSpeaking at the event, Huckabee said \xe2\x80\x9cwe never can accept the notion that\nIsrael will be divided,\xe2\x80\x9d citing the boundaries of Israel being given \xe2\x80\x9cnot\nby the United Nations but by almighty God.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nIn his interview, Huckabee added he could not \xe2\x80\x9cexplain why there is a harsh\nanti-Israel sentiment that exists in the administration.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nHuckabee said if Israel was attacked he doesn\xe2\x80\x99t know what the Obama\nadministration would do.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI think if the Israelis were under attack right now, I\xe2\x80\x99m not sure what\nthis president would do,\xe2\x80\x9d said Huckabee when asked about Israel taking\nmilitary action against Iran.\n\n\n\n*Marco Rubio\'s appealing ambiguity\n<http://theweek.com/articles/557803/marco-rubios-appealing-ambiguity> //\nThe Week // Michael Brendan Dougherty \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nMarco Rubio is an older Republican\'s idea of a younger Republican, we\'ve\nbeen told.\n\n\n\nIn a fun bit of racial and generational essentialism, Ana Marie Cox went\nthrough the senator\'s positions and claimed that "the only demographic\nRubio can plausibly claim to represent is old white guys." This is not a\nsurprise. It isn\'t new. People jostle over these questions of identity all\nthe time: Sarah Palin isn\'t a real woman; Barack Obama isn\'t really black.\n\n\n\nBut a very diverse democracy makes ambiguous, line-crossing identities an\nasset. And Rubio presents the most intriguing kind of biography to the race.\n\n\n\nIn fact, Rubio is running on his biography more than he is running on\nposition papers, which is a good move. The heart of his campaign\nannouncement speech wasn\'t a list of policy proposals, it was a story about\nbeing an immigrant, about being working class, about rising to a position\nof prestige and power. Most of Rubio\'s big speeches are variations on\nthemes drawn from his biography.\n\n\n\nThe multiplicity of Rubio\'s identities doesn\'t make him illegible, it makes\nhim intriguing. And it gives different groups of voters different ways of\nrelating to him.\n\n\n\nRubio traverses a wide range of experience in his economic background. "My\nfather became a bartender. My mother a cashier, a maid, and a Kmart stock\nclerk. They never made it big. But they were successful. Two immigrants\nwith little money or education found stable jobs, owned a home, retired\nwith security, and gave all four of their children a life far better than\ntheir own," he says.\n\n\n\nIn American Son and some speeches, he talks about the burden of student\nloan debt that crushed his monthly budget as a young father and that seemed\nto be leading him away from his dream of pursuing a life in public service.\nAnd yet, Rubio proved more than successful at rising.\n\n\n\nThis diversity of experience extends to his religion, where Rubio manages\nto present himself almost simultaneously as a lifelong ethnic Catholic, an\nEvangelical convert, and a Catholic convert. And that\'s because basically,\nhe is those things. He was raised Catholic. But he and his wife eventually\nbegan attending an Evangelical church where she grew spiritually, and they\nheard the Biblical preaching they hungered for. And then he can talk about\nhis attachment to the liturgical life and sacraments of the Roman Church.\n\n\n\nA few listeners will find this all a bit too exotic, or even confused. But\nwhen he conveys these stories he can touch on little details that ring in a\nvery personal way with different groups of voters. They hear something of\ntheir own story in his, and then they hear something more.\n\n\n\nThis is what presidents do. John F. Kennedy managed to be the first\nelectable Catholic candidate for president, and could connect to the\nmassive pool of voters who descended from the Great Wave of Immigration in\nthe late 19th century. But the Kennedys lived in a style and fashion that\nwas far removed from the hardscrabble roots of Al Smith, the former New\nYork governor and unsuccessful presidential candidate. Smith seemed to\nstink of New York\'s fish markets. Kennedy lived like a WASP scion.\n\n\n\nBarack Obama\'s identity was similarly mixed by the circumstances of his\nbirth. He was black and white. He was raised in Hawaii, where racial\npolitics were entirely different from those of America\'s South or cities.\nBut he had adopted Chicago as his home, and put himself at the center of\nurban organizing.\n\n\n\nLike Obama and Kennedy, Rubio seems to have sensed at an early age how his\npersonal identity could make for an attractive political persona, and then\nshaped his resume, his policy-profile, and experiences to emphasize the\npoint. Politics at this level is almost like a casting call. The life of a\nnation is a kind of drama and voters are the audience. Politicians put\nthemselves forward as a stage-character, a protagonist who can meet the\nmoment.\n\n\n\nAs a protagonist in America\'s drama, Rubio\'s role is to represent the rise\nof the last great wave of immigration to this country, and his role is to\nreconcile the Republican Party with the future that includes these\nimmigrants and their descendants not just as beneficiaries of America\'s\ngenerous immigration policy and dynamic economy, but as full Americans with\na full say in the nation\'s future.\n\n\n\nThat older white Republican voters like Marco Rubio is only going to help\nMarco Rubio. He gives them hope that their ideals will outlive the\nNixon-Reagan coalition. And the voters that matter in battleground states\nare not always so ideological as journalists think.\n\n\n\nThere is no chance that, like Ana Marie Cox, voters will quickly roll\nthrough a known rolodex of Rubio\'s political positions and then re-classify\nhim as old, rich, and white. People in a diverse democracy want "one of us"\nto represent them; sympathetic voters will find the part of Rubio that\nmatches their own self-conception.\n\n\n\nOf course there is an element of fakery to political personas at this\nlevel. Rubio\'s own biography is sometimes messier than presented. But\nfakers have a way of becoming what they present, at least in America.\n\n\n\n*In Marco Rubio vs. Jeb Bush fight, will other GOP candidates compete in\nFlorida\xe2\x80\x99s March 15 primary?*\n<http://www.miamiherald.com/news/politics-government/article22746717.html#storylink=cpy>*\n// Miami Herald // Adam C. Smith \xe2\x80\x93 May 31, 2015*\n\n\n\nLeave it to Florida to host the best political soap opera of the\npresidential campaign.\n\n\n\nThe mega-state that all but delivered the Republican nomination to Mitt\nRomney in 2012 and John McCain in 2008, likely won\xe2\x80\x99t reprise that role\nagain because as many as two dozen states will weigh in before Florida. But\nthe March 15 Sunshine State primary is shaping up as potentially\nspectacular theater nonetheless.\n\n\n\nJeb Bush versus Marco Rubio.\n\n\n\nTwo Florida favorite sons, longtime friends, mentor and protege, near\nneighbors in Miami-Dade facing off in America\xe2\x80\x99s most important battleground\nstate. What many viewed as almost unthinkable a few months ago \xe2\x80\x94 Rubio\nbeating Bush among Florida Republicans \xe2\x80\x94 no longer seems far-fetched.\n\n\n\nOther leading candidates already are pondering whether even to compete in\nFlorida\xe2\x80\x99s primary.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t think there\xe2\x80\x99s a state out there we wouldn\xe2\x80\x99t play in \xe2\x80\x94 other than\nmaybe Florida, where Jeb Bush and Marco Rubio are in some of the polls\nessentially tied, and they are going to eat up a good amount of that\nfinancial advantage that Gov. Bush is going to have,\xe2\x80\x9d Wisconsin Gov. Scott\nWalker said on Laura Ingraham\xe2\x80\x99s radio show last week.\n\n\n\nWe may see a preview of that Bush/Rubio campaign contrast Tuesday at Disney\nWorld when Gov. Rick Scott hosts an \xe2\x80\x9ceconomic summit\xe2\x80\x9d that will include\nspeeches by presidential prospects Bush, Rubio, Govs. Walker, Chris\nChristie of New Jersey, Rick Perry of Texas and Bobby Jindal of Louisiana,\nand former Arkansas Gov. Mike Huckabee, who now lives in Florida\xe2\x80\x99s\nPanhandle.\n\n\n\nThat so many candidates would commit to a forum hundreds of miles away from\nearly voting states like Iowa and New Hampshire is testament to Florida\xe2\x80\x99s\nlofty status as a critical battleground and fundraising mecca. But Florida\nis treading on new ground this election cycle in fielding two frontrunners\nfor the GOP nomination and deciding for the first time in several cycles\nagainst holding one of the earliest primaries in the country.\n\n\n\nIn 2008 and 2012, state Republican leaders blatantly defied national party\nrules by holding earlier-than-allowed primaries, arguing that the country\xe2\x80\x99s\nbiggest and most diverse battleground state deserved more say in picking\nthe major party nominees. The Republican National Committee responded by\ncutting in half the number of delegates, but that didn\xe2\x80\x99t stop the leading\ncandidates from campaigning ferociously in Florida.\n\n\n\nThis year, with Bush looking increasingly likely to run, Republican\nlegislative leaders chose not to risk losing Sunshine State delegates.\nUltimately it takes about 1,235 delegates to win the nomination.\n\n\n\nFlorida legislators earlier this year scheduled the primary for March 15,\nthe earliest date in which a state can hold a \xe2\x80\x9cwinner-take-all\xe2\x80\x9d primary.\nThat means whoever wins the primary would win all 99 of Florida\xe2\x80\x99s\ndelegates. Another candidate could spend millions, fall just behind the\nwinner, and walk away with zero delegates.\n\n\n\nAt the time that was widely seen as a gift to Bush. Now, with Rubio off to\na strong early start and Bush struggling to generate widespread excitement\nwith the base of the party, it\xe2\x80\x99s not so clear.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe winner-take-all primary was a very good thing for Jeb \xe2\x80\x94 before Marco\ngot in,\xe2\x80\x9d said Ana Navarro, a Bush supporter in Miami who is friendly with\nboth. \xe2\x80\x9cWhen people, including me, were calling their legislators, telling\nthem to make it winner-take-all, we were all still under the mistaken\nimpression that Marco wasn\xe2\x80\x99t going to run.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nThe cost of campaigning in winner-take-all Florida provides a significant\nincentive for candidates to focus their efforts elsewhere. But that\xe2\x80\x99s a\nrisk, too.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cTactically, looking past Florida could make sense to some of the other\ncandidates not named Jeb or Marco,\xe2\x80\x9d said Republican strategist Kevin\nMadden. \xe2\x80\x9cBut Florida, as a major swing state, is still an important test\nfor any candidacy looking to make an argument that you can win a general.\nIt puts a lot of pressure on a campaign to really perform in Ohio and the\nother contests.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nEight months is an eternity in presidential politics, and the landscape is\nlikely to look far different by the time any actual voting begins next\nyear. Former 2012 Republican frontrunners Rick Perry, Herman Cain, Michele\nBachmann and Newt Gingrich can attest to how quickly the ground can shift.\n\n\n\nMaking it even harder for 2016 candidates to decide whether or not to spend\ntime and money in Florida is the prevalence of early voting. Florida\xe2\x80\x99s\nprimary may be in mid-March, but half the votes will be cast by then.\nOverseas absentee ballots start going out by Jan. 30 \xe2\x80\x94 before Iowa voters\ncast a single vote \xe2\x80\x94 and in-state mail ballots are sent starting Feb. 9.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2 \xe2\x80\xa2 \xe2\x80\xa2\n\n\n\nNot only should Florida\xe2\x80\x99s primary feel different from its recent contests,\nbut so should the entire primary season.\n\n\n\nParty leaders concluded that the protracted and contentious 2012 primary\nseason put Mitt Romney at a disadvantage heading into the general election.\nThe mandate for 2016 was fewer debates and a shorter primary season. Rather\nthan a late August nominating convention like Tampa hosted, the 2016\nconvention will be July 18-21 in Cleveland.\n\n\n\nThe season is expected to kick off in February, rather than January. And\nafter the initial four states cast their votes, the campaign for the\nnomination is likely to be defined by a series of election days featuring\nmultiple states voting.\n\n\n\nCome March 15, Florida probably will share the stage with Ohio, Missouri\nand Illinois.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s not going to be longer, it\xe2\x80\x99s going to be more intense,\xe2\x80\x9d Sean Spicer,\ncommunications director for the RNC, said of the 2016 nominating season.\n\n\n\nFlorida won\xe2\x80\x99t be the first big prize after the earliest contests in Iowa,\nNew Hampshire, Nevada and South Carolina, as it was in the last two\npresidential election. By March 15, at least 20 states will have voted and\nprobably half of all the available delegates awarded. March 1 is expected\nto serve as a Southern primary with half a dozen or so states voting.\n\n\n\nAll those pre-Florida states, however, will allocate their delegates\nproportionally rather than winner-take-all, which means no candidate may\nhave a big lead in delegates by March 15.\n\n\n\nAnother huge question for 2016? Money versus momentum. The advent of\npolitical committees accepting unlimited contributions and billionaires\nbankrolling campaigns has knocked aside some of the old assumptions about\npresidential campaigns and made it easier for candidates to keep pushing\nahead into state after state.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cIn the past, if you couldn\xe2\x80\x99t raise money, couldn\xe2\x80\x99t raise enough donations\nof $2,500 or less, that told you something politically,\xe2\x80\x9d said Republican\nstrategist John Weaver, another veteran of several presidential campaigns.\n\xe2\x80\x9cNow you only need one person to back you up and you can go deep into the\ncalendar whether you deserve to or not politically.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nBush is expected to have a vast fundraising advantage over the rest of the\nfield, which means he likely would have the resources for a long slog of a\ncampaign. Even an unlimited campaign account is not necessarily enough to\novercome a string of losses, however.\n\n\n\nRubio has at least two billionaires, Oracle founder Larry Ellison of\nCalifornia and auto dealer and former Philadelphia Eagles owner Norman\nBraman of Miami, supporting his campaign.\n\n\n\nThe 2016 primary calendar is in constant flux and will remain so for\nmonths, but Republican campaign officials say the rough, tentative schedule\nleading to Florida is shaping up along these lines:\n\n\n\nFeb. 1: Iowa\n\n\n\nFeb. 9: New Hampshire\n\n\n\nFeb. 20: South Carolina\n\n\n\nFeb. 23: Nevada\n\n\n\nMarch 1: Georgia, Oklahoma, Tennessee, Massachusetts, Vermont, Minnesota,\npossibly Alabama, Wyoming, Virginia\n\n\n\nMarch 5: Kansas, Louisiana, possibly Washington State\n\n\n\nMarch 8: Hawaii, Idaho, Michigan, Mississippi, possibly North Carolina and\nAmerican Samoa\n\n\n\nMarch 12: Virgin Islands, Guam, Puerto Rico\n\n\n\nMarch 15: Florida, Ohio, Missouri, Illinois, possibly Northern Mariana\nIslands\n\n\n\n*Trump: I won\xe2\x80\x99t do straw poll if everyone backs out\n<http://www.desmoinesregister.com/story/news/elections/presidential/caucus/2015/06/01/donald-trump-straw-poll-mitt-romney-gucci-store/28313569/>\n// The Des Moines Register // Josh Hafner \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nDonald Trump, the reality TV star, businessman and serial flirter with\npresidential campaigns, recently announced that he\xe2\x80\x99ll declare his 2016\nambitions on June 16 in New York City.\n\n\n\nBefore he heads to Iowa this week with visits in Mason City and Coralville,\nTrump spoke with The Des Moines Register about the Iowa Straw Poll, his\n\xe2\x80\x9cbeautiful\xe2\x80\x9d solution to the Islamic State, and discerning between celebrity\nand political appeal.\n\n\n\nAre you going to announce that you\xe2\x80\x99re running for president this month?\n\n\n\nA lot of people think that now. Well, if the consultant\'s so smart, why aren\xe2\x80\x99t they rich?\n\n\n\n*TOP NEWS*\n\n\n*DOMESTIC*\n\n\n\n*Senate to Take Up Spy Bill as Parts of Patriot Act Expire\n<http://www.nytimes.com/2015/06/02/us/senate-bill-patriot-act-spying-nsa.html>\n// NYT // Jennifer Steinhauer \xe2\x80\x93 June 1, 2015*\n\n\n\nWASHINGTON \xe2\x80\x94 The Senate will reconvene at midday on Monday to consider\nchanges to a House bill that would curtail the government\xe2\x80\x99s authority to\nsweep up vast quantities of phone records after the program, which began\nafter the 2001 terrorist attacks, expired at 12:01 a.m.\n\n\n\nSenator Rand Paul, Republican of Kentucky, blocked an extension of it\nduring an extraordinary and at times caustic Sunday session of the Senate.\n\n\n\nHamstrung by procedural rules that require the consent of all lawmakers,\nthe Senate is unable to restore the lapsed authorities until at least\nTuesday. The Senate was on recess last week.\n\n\n\nAfter senators pass a procedural measure on Monday to consider the House\nbill, they will begin amending it, a process that could take one to three\ndays.\n\n\n\nMr. Paul\xe2\x80\x99s stand may have forced the temporary expiration of parts of the\npost-9/11 Patriot Act used by the National Security Agency to collect phone\nrecords, but he was helped by the miscalculation of Senator Mitch\nMcConnell, the majority leader, who sent the Senate on a weeklong vacation\nafter blocking the House bill before Memorial Day.\n\n\n\nMr. McConnell, also of Kentucky, relented on Sunday, setting up a final\nround of votes on Tuesday or Wednesday that will most likely send a\ncompromised version of the House bill to President Obama for his signature.\nEven Mr. Paul, using the procedural weapon of an objection, conceded he\ncould not stop that.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cLittle by little, we\xe2\x80\x99ve allowed our freedom to slip away,\xe2\x80\x9d Mr. Paul said\nduring a lengthy floor soliloquy.\n\n\n\nThe expiration of surveillance authority demonstrates a profound shift in\nAmerican attitudes since the days after the Sept. 11, 2001, terrorist\nattacks, when national security was pre-eminent in both parties. Fourteen\nyears after that attack, even as American conflicts continue abroad, a\nswell of privacy concerns stemming from both the vast expansion of\ncommunication systems and an increasing distrust of government\xe2\x80\x99s use of\ndata has turned those concerns on their head.\n\n\n\nWhile it would represent a retrenchment on the part of the government, it\ndoes not end the argument over the dual imperatives of security and\nindividual liberty brought to light by Edward J. Snowden, the former\ncontractor for the National Security Agency.\n\n\n\nThe expiration of three key provisions of the Patriot Act means that, for\nnow, the N.S.A. will no longer collect newly created logs of Americans\xe2\x80\x99\nphone calls in bulk. It also means that the F.B.I. cannot invoke the\nPatriot Act to obtain, for new investigations, wiretap orders that follow a\nsuspect who changes phones, wiretap orders for a \xe2\x80\x9clone wolf\xe2\x80\x9d terrorism\nsuspect not linked to a group, or court orders to obtain business records\nrelevant to an investigation.\n\n\n\nHowever, the Justice Department may invoke a so-called grandfather clause\nto keep using those powers for investigations that had started before June\n1, and there are additional workarounds investigators may use to overcome\nthe lapse in the authorizations.\n\n\n\nMr. McConnell and other national security hawks who failed to continue the\nprogram badly underestimated the shift in the national mood, which has\nfound its voice with Democrats and the libertarian wing of the Republican\nParty. The moment also put him at odds with Mr. Paul, whom he has endorsed\nfor president.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI remain determined to work toward the best outcome for the American\npeople possible under the circumstances,\xe2\x80\x9d Mr. McConnell said. \xe2\x80\x9cThis is\nwhere we are, colleagues \xe2\x80\x94 a House-passed bill with some serious flaws, and\nan inability to get a short-term extension to improve the House bill.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nMr. Paul\xe2\x80\x99s effort clearly angered many of his Republican colleagues, who\nmet without him an hour before the Senate began to vote Sunday night.\nSenator John McCain, Republican of Arizona, who sparred with Mr. Paul on\nthe floor over procedure, said later that Mr. Paul was not fit for the\nWhite House job he seeks. \xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99ve said on many occasions that I believe he\nwould be the worst candidate we could put forward,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.\n\n\n\nEven as senators were trickling into the Capitol from the airport, Mr.\nMcConnell attempted to extend some aspects of the law. He asked senators to\nconsider a two-week continuation of the federal authority to track a \xe2\x80\x9clone\nwolf\xe2\x80\x9d terrorism suspect not connected to a state sponsor and to conduct\n\xe2\x80\x9croving\xe2\x80\x9d surveillance of a suspect, rather than of a phone number alone, to\ncombat terrorists who frequently discard cellphones.\n\n\n\nBut Mr. Paul objected, and Mr. McConnell denounced from the Senate floor\nwhat he called \xe2\x80\x9ca campaign of demagoguery and disinformation\xe2\x80\x9d about the\nprogram.\n\n\n\nMr. McConnell then moved to a second option, a procedural move to take up\nthe bill passed by the House, which he said the Senate would amend this\nweek. It was unclear Sunday how many amendments, including any from Mr.\nPaul, would be considered and whether any could pass the Senate or be\nadopted by the House.\n\n\n\nThe House bill would overhaul the Patriot Act and scale back the bulk\ncollection of phone records revealed by Mr. Snowden. Under the provisions\nof the House bill, sweeps that had operated under the guise of so-called\nnational security letters issued by the F.B.I. would end. The data would\ninstead be stored by the phone companies and could be retrieved by\nintelligence agencies only after approval of the Foreign Intelligence\nSurveillance Act court.\n\n\n\nPresident Obama and his director of national intelligence, James R. Clapper\nJr., have made dire warnings in recent days about the perils of letting the\nlaw expire and called for immediate approval of a surveillance bill passed\nby the House. The C.I.A. director, John O. Brennan, echoed the president on\nSunday during an interview on the CBS show \xe2\x80\x9cFace the Nation,\xe2\x80\x9d saying there\nhad \xe2\x80\x9cbeen a little too much political grandstanding.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nIn a statement issued Sunday night, the White House said: \xe2\x80\x9cWe call on the\nSenate to ensure this irresponsible lapse in authorities is as short-lived\nas possible. On a matter as critical as our national security, individual\nsenators must put aside their partisan motivations and act swiftly. The\nAmerican people deserve nothing less.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nSpeaker John A. Boehner, Republican of Ohio, also urged the Senate to act,\nciting the threat of groups like the Islamic State. \xe2\x80\x9cAl Qaeda, ISIL and\nother terrorists around the globe continue to plot attacks on America and\nour allies,\xe2\x80\x9d Mr. Boehner said in a statement. \xe2\x80\x9cAnyone who is satisfied with\nletting this critical intelligence capability go dark isn\xe2\x80\x99t taking the\nterrorist threat seriously.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nMr. McConnell had sought to get a series of short-term extensions passed so\nthat Congress could continue to work on a compromise \xe2\x80\x94 like giving the\nphone companies more time to adapt to the new law \xe2\x80\x94 but that effort\ncollapsed under the objections of Mr. Paul and two Democrats, Ron Wyden of\nOregon and Martin Heinrich of New Mexico. Further, members of the House\nrejected extending the current law, given the support for their bill.\n\n\n\nAfter a middle-of-the-night vote for a short-term extension failed on the\nSaturday before Memorial Day, senators left for a weeklong recess as the\nclock ticked. Senate Republican leaders sought a compromise that would make\na new bill acceptable to both hawkish lawmakers and Mr. Paul. \xe2\x80\x9cI still have\ndeep concerns,\xe2\x80\x9d said Senator Susan Collins, Republican of Maine.\n\n\n\nOver the week, negotiators on the House and Senate Intelligence Committees\nhad laid out a series of options to revise the bipartisan USA Freedom Act,\nincluding the addition of a certification process to ensure that the\ntechnology is ready to move metadata storage to the phone companies and\nallowing for a longer transition to phone company storage of the data. Roberts Jr., writing for the majority, said that\nprosecutors must do more than prove that reasonable people would view\nstatements as threats. The defendant\xe2\x80\x99s state of mind matters, the chief\njustice wrote, though he declined to say just where the legal line is drawn.\n\n\n\nChief Justice Roberts wrote for seven justices. Justice Samuel A. Alito Jr.\nvoted with the majority, though he said that a defendant\xe2\x80\x99s recklessness\nshould suffice. The majority opinion took no position on that possibility.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cAttorneys and judges are left to guess,\xe2\x80\x9d Justice Alito wrote.\n\n\n\nJustice Clarence Thomas issued a similar criticism in his dissent.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cOur job is to decide questions, not create them,\xe2\x80\x9d he wrote. \xe2\x80\x9cGiven the\nmajority\xe2\x80\x99s ostensible concern for protecting innocent actors, one would\nhave expected it to announce a clear rule\xe2\x80\x94any clear rule.
